Qisas in Wounds Below Mawdihah: The Hanafi Position
Ruling on qisas for non-mawdihah wounds with evidence and tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits qisas for wounds below mawdihah and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school allows qisas for soft-tissue wounds by measurement, despite a weak narration to the contrary.

The passage examines the ruling on qisas for wounds that are less severe than mawdihah. There is an ambiguity in the matn that suggests no qisas, but the commentary clarifies that the relied-upon position requires qisas. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the tarjih within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify wound categories
The passage distinguishes three types of wounds: mawdihah (exposing bone), wounds below mawdihah (soft tissue), and wounds above (bone breakage). For bone breakage, the matn says no qisas based on a hadith.
2
State the initial ruling from the matn
The matn says 'no qisas in other than al-mawdihah,' which seems to deny qisas for wounds below mawdihah. However, this is not the final view.
This statement is based on a weak narration.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa that there is no qisas in bone breakages and by extension below mawdihah. This derives from the hadith 'la qisas fi al-ʿazm'.
This is considered a weaker narration (nawadir).
4
Identify the zahir al-riwayah position
Muhammad al-Shaybani in al-Asl affirms that qisas is obligatory for wounds below mawdihah because equality can be achieved by measuring the wound and making a corresponding cut.
This is the relied-upon transmission.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The commentary declares the zahir al-riwayah position as 'asahh' (more correct) and thus mufta bihi. The reasoning is that without bone breakage, equality is possible and safe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا قصاص في غير الموضحة) لأنه لا يمكن اعتبار المساواة فيه لأن ما دون الموضحة ليس له حد ينتهي إليه السكين وما فوقها كسر العظم ولا قصاص فيه لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا قصاص في العظم» وهو رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله . وفي ظاهر الرواية يجب القصاص فيما دون الموضحة؛ ذكره محمد رحمه الله في الأصل وهو الأصح لأنه ممكن فيه اعتبار المساواة فيه إذ ليس فيه كسر العظم ولا خوف التلف فيستر قدرها اعتباراً ثم يتخذ حديدة بقدر ذلك فيقطع بها مقدار ما قطع فيتحقق استيفاء القصاص بذلك، وفي الموضحة القصاص إن كانت عمداً لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قضى بالقصاص في الموضحة لأن المساواة فيها ممكنة بانتهاء السكين إلى العظم فيتحقق استيفاء القصاص. قال رحمه الله : (وفي أصابع اليد نصف الدية) أي أصابع اليد الواحدة لأن في كل أصبع عشرة من الإبل لما روينا فيكون في الخمسة خمسون ضرورة وهو النصف، ولأن بقطع الأصابع تفوت منفعة البطش وهو الموجب على ما
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And no qisas in other than al-mawdihah) because it is not possible to consider equality in it, because what is below mawdihah has no limit for the knife to end at, and what is above it is bone breakage, and there is no qisas in it due to his saying (peace be upon him): "No qisas in bone." This is a narration from Hasan from Abu Hanifa. In the apparent riwayah (zahir al-riwayah), qisas is obligatory in what is below mawdihah; Muhammad mentioned it in al-Asl, and it is the more correct, because it is possible to consider equality in it, as there is no breakage of bone nor fear of death. So its measure is estimated, then an iron tool is made to that measure, and it is cut with it, and qisas is realized. And in mawdihah, qisas if it is intentional, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) decreed qisas in mawdihah, because equality is possible by the knife stopping at the bone. He said: (And in the fingers of the hand: half the diya), meaning the fingers of one hand, because each finger has ten camels as we narrated, so in the five there are fifty necessarily, which is half the diya. And because with cutting the fingers, the benefit of grasping is lost, which is the cause (of the obligation).
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage addresses qisas (retaliation) for wounds. The matn states no qisas for wounds below mawdihah, but the commentary clarifies that in the apparent riwayah (zahir al-riwayah) qisas is actually required for wounds below mawdihah, as equality can be achieved by measurement and use of a corresponding blade. For mawdihah itself, qisas is established by Prophetic decree. For fingers: each finger is 10 camels, so five fingers of one hand total 50 camels, which is half the full diya (100 camels). The wisdom is that the purpose of the hand (grasping) is lost.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The widely transmitted and relied-upon position within the Hanafi school, recorded in the six books of Muhammad al-Shaybani.
الموضحة (al-mawdihah): A wound that exposes the bone but does not break it.
القصاص (al-qisas): Retaliation in kind, prescribed for intentional injuries where equality is possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, is qisas wajib for an intentional wound below mawdihah (not reaching bone)?
A) No, because equality is impossible
B) Yes, because equality can be achieved by measurement
C) Only if the wound is small
D) Only if the victim requests it

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits qisas for soft-tissue wounds if equality can be achieved by measurement; the mufta bihi is the zahir al-riwayah.

Diyat for Fingers of One Hand: Half the Full Diya
Ruling on diyat for fingers of one hand as half the diya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the diyat for fingers of one hand and explain the reasoning behind the fixed amount.

Core Idea
Five fingers of one hand carry a fixed diyat of fifty camels, half the full diya, due to the loss of grasping function.

The passage concludes with a specific ruling on injuries to fingers. Each finger is worth ten camels, so all five fingers of one hand amount to half the full diya. The reasoning is based on the loss of the hand's primary function (grasping).

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The matn says 'In the fingers of the hand: half the diya.' This means the compensation for cutting all five fingers of one hand is fifty camels (half of the full diya of 100 camels).
2
Identify the per-finger diyat
The commentary explains that each finger has a diyat of ten camels, based on a narration from the Prophet (peace be upon him). Summing to fifty for five fingers.
All fingers are equal; no distinction.
3
Understand the basis
The text gives two reasons: the narrated amount (prophetic tradition) and the rationale: cutting the fingers eliminates the benefit of grasping (al-batsh), which is the primary function of the hand.
4
Explain the half-diaya calculation
Full diya (for a life) is 100 camels. Since the fingers of one hand are half of the body's limbs? Actually it's a specific ruling: the hand itself has a diyat of half, but the text specifically says fingers of one hand are half, which aligns with the hand's importance.
This is a fixed amount, not based on a percentage of the hand's diyat.

Source Text

Hukumat 'Adl for Head Wounds Below al-Mudihah: Wujub and Methods of Calculation
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on hukumat calculation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of hukumat 'adl for head wounds with no fixed arsh and explain the three Hanafi methods of calculation, identifying the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
For head wounds without fixed diyah, just compensation is wajib; the methods differ on whether to use value decrease or proportion to al-mudihah.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling of hukumat 'adl for six types of head wounds that are less severe than al-mudihah. Because these wounds have no fixed compensation from the Shari'ah, they cannot be ignored, and a just appraisal is obligatory. The main discussion turns on how to calculate this appraisal, with three methods proposed by prominent Hanafi scholars, and a preferred position identified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wounds and the ruling
List the six head wounds (al-kharisah, al-dami'ah, al-damiyah, al-badi'ah, al-mutalahimah, al-simhaq) and note that hukumat 'adl is wajib for them.
The ruling is explicit in the text: 'فيجب فيها حكومة عدل'.
2
Understand the rationale
Recognize that these wounds have no fixed arsh from Shari'ah and cannot be disregarded, necessitating a just appraisal.
The text says 'ليس فيها أرش مقدر' and 'لا يمكن إهدارها'.
3
Analyze al-Tahawi's method
Al-Tahawi proposes assessing the decrease in the value of a slave (or analogous human value) and then taking that proportion of the full diyah.
This method is criticized by al-Karkhi for potentially exceeding the diyah of al-mudihah.
4
Analyze al-Karkhi's method
Al-Karkhi proposes comparing the wound's size to al-mudihah and taking the same proportion of half a tenth of the diyah (50 camels).
This is the preferred method according to Shaykh al-Islam and al-Marghinani.
5
Note the third method and tarjih
Al-Muhit suggests proportioning to the smallest wound with a fixed arsh. Al-Sadr al-Shahid allows the mufti discretion, but the strongest view is al-Karkhi's.
The tarjih is based on the illa of referral to the textually fixed (al-mansus 'alayh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وفي الخارصة والدامعة والدامية والباضعة والمتلاحمة والسمحاق حكومة عدل) لأن هذه ليس فيها أرش مقدر من جهة الشرع ولا يمكن إهدارها فيجب فيها حكومة عدل، وهو مأثور عن ابراهيم النخعي وعمر بن عبد العزيز. واختلفوا في تفسير هذه الحكومة قال الطحاوي تفسيرها أن يقوم مملوكاً بدون هذا الأثر ثم يقوم وبه هذا الأثر ثم ينظر إلى تفاوت ما بينهما، فإن كان ثلث عشر القيمة مثلاً يجب ثلث عشر الدية، وإن كان ربع عشر القيمة يجب ربع عشر الدية. وقال الكرخي : ينظر كم مقدار هذه الشجة من الموضحة فيجب بقدر ذلك من نصف عشر الدية لأن ما لا نص فيه يرد إلى المنصوص عليه، وكان الكرخي رحمه الله يقول : ما ذكره الطحاوي ليس بصحيح لأنه اعتبر ذلك الطريق فربما يكون نقصان القيمة أكثر من نصف الدية فيؤدي إلى أن يوجب في هذه الشجاج وهو دون الموضحة أكثر مما أوجبه الشرع في الموضحة وأنه محال بل الصحيح الاعتبار بالمقدار. وقال الصدر الشهيد : ينظر المفتي في هذا إن أمكنه الفتوى بالثاني بأن كانت الجناية في الرأس والوجه يفتي بالثاني وإن لم يتيسر عليه ذلك يفتي بالقول الأول لأنه الأيسر قال؛ وكان المرغيناني يفتي به . وقال في المحيط : والأصح أنه ينظر كم مقدار هذه الشجة من أقل شجة لها أرش مقدر، فإن كان مقداره مثل نصف شجة لها أرش أو ثلثها وجب نصف أو ثلث أرش تلك الشجة، وأن ربعاً ،فربع ذكره بعد ذكر القولين فكأنه جعله قولاً ثالثاً والأشبه أن يكون هذا تفسيراً لقول الكرخي. وقال شيخ الإسلام وقول الكرخي أصح لأن علياً اعتبره بهذا الطريق فيمن قطع طرف لسانه على ما بيناه.
He (the author) said: (And in al-kharisah, al-dami'ah, al-damiyah, al-badi'ah, al-mutalahimah, and al-simhaq there is a just appraisal (hukumat 'adl)) because these have no fixed compensation from the Shari'ah, and it is not possible to disregard them, so a just appraisal is obligatory. This is transmitted from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz. They differed in the interpretation of this appraisal. Al-Tahawi said: Its interpretation is that a slave is valued without this effect and then valued with this effect, then the difference between them is considered. If it is, for example, a third of a tenth of the value, then a third of a tenth of the diyah is obligatory; if a quarter of a tenth of the value, then a quarter of a tenth of the diyah. Al-Karkhi said: One looks at how much of al-mudihah this wound is, and then the same proportion of half of a tenth of the diyah is obligatory, because what has no text is referred to the textually fixed. Al-Karkhi used to say: What al-Tahawi mentioned is not correct because he considered that method, so perhaps the decrease in value is more than half the diyah, leading to the obligation for these wounds, which are below al-mudihah, of more than what the Law obligated for al-mudihah, and that is impossible. Rather, the correct [method] is consideration by proportion. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: The mufti looks into this: if he is able to give a fatwa by the second [method] when the injury is on the head and face, he gives fatwa by the second; if that is not easy for him, he gives fatwa by the first opinion because it is easier. Al-Marghinani used to give fatwa by it. It is said in al-Muhit: The most correct is that one looks at how much this wound is relative to the smallest wound that has a fixed compensation. If its proportion is like half a wound that has a fixed compensation, or one third, then half or one third of the compensation of that wound is obligatory, and if a quarter then a quarter. This was mentioned after mentioning the two opinions, as if he made it a third opinion, and it is more likely that this is an interpretation of al-Karkhi's statement. Shaykh al-Islam said: The statement of al-Karkhi is more correct because 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) considered it by this method in the case of a person who cut the tip of his tongue, as we have explained.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on hukumat 'adl for six types of head wounds (the six terms are listed). The commentary explains that these wounds have no fixed diyah amount in the Shari'ah, so they cannot be ignored; hence a just appraisal (hukumat 'adl) is wajib. This is supported by transmission from early authorities. The main discussion concerns how to calculate the appraisal. Three methods are presented: (1) al-Tahawi's method: assess the decrease in value of a slave; (2) al-Karkhi's method: proportion the wound to al-mudihah and take that proportion of half a tenth of the diyah; (3) a third view in al-Muhit: proportion to the smallest wound with a fixed arsh. Al-Sadr al-Shahid suggests the mufti chooses the easier method. Shaykh al-Islam prefers al-Karkhi's method. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi approach to cases where no explicit text exists: such cases are referred to analogous textual rulings (ilhaq bi al-mansus 'alayh).

Key Terms
حكومة عدل (hukumat 'adl): An appraisal by a just expert of the compensation for a wound that has no fixed diyah.
شجة (shajjah): A head wound. Here the text lists types: al-kharisah (scratch), al-dami'ah (bleeding), al-damiyah (blood flowing), al-badi'ah (skin cut), al-mutalahimah (flesh cut), al-simhaq (skin peeled but bone exposed).
موضحة (al-mudihah): A head wound that reaches the bone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Karkhi, how is hukumat 'adl calculated for a head wound below al-mudihah?
A) By assessing the decrease in the victim's value as a slave
B) By taking the same proportion of half a tenth of the diyah as the wound's size relative to al-mudihah
C) By comparing to the smallest wound with a fixed arsh
D) By the mufti's discretion

Key Takeaway
Hukumat 'adl is wajib for head wounds without fixed arsh; the preferred Hanafi method calculates compensation in proportion to al-mudihah's diyah.

Diyah for Fingers, Hand, and Forearm: Hanafi Position and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling on diyah for fingers, hand, and forearm with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah for cutting the fingers and hand, apply the Hanafi rule that the forearm is not included in the hand's diyah, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
The hand's diyah is based on grasping; the forearm does not grasp, so it is not included.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the diyah for fingers, the hand, and the forearm. The central ruling is that cutting the fingers and palm (the hand) incurs half the diyah (50 camels), and if cut with half the forearm, an additional just appraisal (hukumat) is required for the forearm. The commentary then addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the forearm is separate, while a narration from Abu Yusuf includes it in the hand. Understanding the functional definition of 'yad' (hand) as the grasping instrument is key to the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for fingers and hand
The matn states that the diyah for the fingers of one hand is half the diyah (50 camels). The commentary explains that each finger is 10 camels, so five fingers make half. Cutting the fingers with the palm still incurs only half diyah because the palm is dependent on the fingers for grasping.
The hadith 'In the two hands is the diyah, in one of them half' is cited as proof.
2
Analyze the ruling when half the forearm is cut
The matn adds: 'And with half the forearm, half the diyah and a just appraisal.' This means the hand (fingers+palm) gets half diyah, and the forearm gets a separate hukumat (appraisal). The commentary explains that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad adopt this view.
The forearm does not contribute to grasping, so it is not part of the 'yad' for diyah purposes.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf (in one narration) argues that the forearm is included in the hand, so no additional compensation beyond half diyah is due. His proof is that the term 'yad' in the hadith includes the entire limb up to the shoulder. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond that grasping is the basis for diyah, and the forearm does not grasp.
The commentary favours Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's view as the apparent (zahir) position.
4
Understand the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, cutting the hand with half the forearm requires half diyah plus a hukumat for the forearm. Under Abu Yusuf's narration, only half diyah is due. The relied-upon position is the former.
The hukumat is determined by the value of the injured part as per appraisal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وفي أصابع اليد نصف الدية) أي أصابع اليد الواحدة لأن في كل أصبع عشرة من الإبل لما روينا فيكون في الخمسة خمسون ضرورة وهو النصف، ولأن بقطع الأصابع تفوت منفعة البطش وهو الموجب على ما اليد نصف الدية ولو الكف مع . ومع نصف الساعد نصف الدية وحكومة وفي قطع أقول : القائل أن يقول لمن ذكر فيما مر أن في كل أصبع من أصابع اليدين والرجلين عشر الدية كان ذكر هذه المسألة هنا مستدركاً إذ لا شك أن خمسة أعشار الدية نصف الدية وعلم قطعاً مما أن في أصابع اليد الواحدة وهي خمس أصابع نصف الدية ولو لم يكن الاستلزام والاقتضاء في حصول العلم بمثله بل كان لا بد فيه من التصريح بها للزم أن يذكر أيضاً أن في أصالة حتى يتوهم الاستدراك بل ليكون ذكرها توطئة للمسألة المعاقبة إياها وهي قوله فإن قطعها مع الكف ففيه أيضاً نصف الدية، فالمقصود في البيان هنا أن قطع الأصابع وحدها وقطعها مع الكف سيان في الحكم هذا قال في الوقاية في هذا المقام وفي أصابع يد بلا كف ومعها نصف الدية. قال وعن رحمه الله : (ولو مع الكف هذا متصل بما قبله أي في أصابع اليد نصف الدية وإن قطعها مع الكف ولا يزيد الأرش بسبب الكف لأن الكف سبب للأصابع في حق البطش فإن قوة البطش بها وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام في اليدين الدية، وفي أحدهما نصف الدية واليد اسم لجارحة يقع بها البطش لأن اسم اليد يدل على القدرة والقوة والبطش يقع بالأصابع والكف فيجب فيها دية واحدة لأن منفعتها جنس واحد فيكون الكف تبعاً للأصابع. قال (ومع نصف الساعد نصف الدية وحكومة عدل نصف الدية في الكف والأصابع والحكومة نصف الساعد وهو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف، وعنه ما زاد على الأصابع من اليدين والرجلين من أصل الساعد والفخذ هو تبع فلا يزيد على الدية لأن الشارع أوجب في الواحدة منهما نصف الدية واليد اسم لهذه الجارحة إلى المنكب والرجل إلى الفخذ فلا يزيد على تقدير الشارع ولأن الساعد ليس له أرش مقدر فيه كالكف. ووجه الظاهر أن اليد اسم لآلة باطشة ووجوب الأرش باعتبار منفعة البطش، وكذا في الأرش ولا يقع البطش بالساعد أصلاً ولا تبعاً فلا يدخل في أرشه. وقال بعض He (the author) said: (And in the fingers of the hand is half the diyah) meaning the fingers of one hand, because in each finger there are ten camels as we have narrated, so in five there are fifty by necessity, which is half [of the diyah]. And because by cutting the fingers the benefit of grasping (batash) is lost, which is the cause for [obligation]. [And] for the hand is half the diyah, even if [cut] with the palm. And with half the forearm is half the diyah and a just appraisal. And in cutting... I say: The objector may say to the one who mentioned earlier that each finger of the fingers of the hands and feet is a tenth of the diyah, the mention of this issue here is redundant, since there is no doubt that five-tenths of the diyah is half the diyah, and it is known definitively that in the fingers of one hand, which are five fingers, is half the diyah. If not for the implication and requirement in obtaining knowledge of the like, but rather explicit mention were necessary, then he would also have to mention that in two fingers is two-tenths of the diyah, and in three fingers three-tenths, and in four fingers four-tenths, and so on from the issues left unmentioned explicitly in the book. The answer to this is that the mention of this issue here is not to explain it itself originally so that redundancy is imagined, but rather its mention is a prelude to the following issue, which is his statement: 'And if he cuts them with the palm, then also half the diyah.' So the purpose of the explanation here is that cutting the fingers alone and cutting them with the palm are equal in ruling. This is what was said in al-Wiqayah in this context: 'And in the fingers of a hand without a palm and with it, half the diyah.' He said: And from him (may Allah have mercy on him): (And even with the palm) this is connected to what preceded, meaning: in the fingers of the hand is half the diyah, and if he cuts them with the palm, the arsh does not increase because of the palm, because the palm is a means for the fingers regarding grasping, since the strength of grasping is with them. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'In the two hands is the diyah, and in one of them half the diyah.' 'Hand' is a name for the limb by which grasping occurs, because the name 'hand' indicates power and strength, and grasping occurs with the fingers and the palm, so one diyah is obligatory because their benefit is of one genus, so the palm is dependent on the fingers. He said: (And with half the forearm, half the diyah and a just appraisal) half the diyah for the palm and fingers, and the just appraisal for half the forearm. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf. From him [another narration] that what is beyond the fingers of the hands and feet from the origin of the forearm and thigh is dependent, so it does not increase beyond the diyah, because the Legislator obligated half the diyah for one of them, and 'hand' is a name for the limb up to the shoulder, and 'foot' up to the thigh, so it does not increase beyond the Legislator's estimation. And because the forearm has no fixed arsh, like the palm. The apparent opinion is that 'hand' is a name for the grasping instrument, and the obligation of arsh is based on the benefit of grasping, and likewise in arsh, and grasping does not occur with the forearm at all, nor as a dependent, so it is not included in its arsh. Some commentators said: And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the hand is a grasping instrument, and grasping is related to the palm and fingers, not the forearm. I say: An objector may say that the apparent meaning of this statement is that each of the palm and fingers has a role in grasping, and the implication of his statement earlier—and because the palm is dependent on the fingers because grasping occurs by the fingers alone—so there is a contradiction between his two statements in the two places. The author of al-Kafi noticed this and changed his wording here, saying: For them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the arsh of the hand is obligatory only because it is a grasping instrument, and the origin of grasping is the fingers, and the palm is dependent on them. As for the forearm, it does not follow them because it is not connected to them, so it is not made dependent on them regarding liability. I say: It is also possible to reconcile between his two statements with some attention, by supposing an omitted part in his statement earlier, because grasping is only with the fingers.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the diyah for fingers and the hand. The matn states that the diyah for the fingers of one hand is half the diyah. This is because each finger is 10 camels, five fingers total 50 = half. The commentary notes that some might consider this redundant since the total for one hand is obvious, but it serves as a prelude to the next ruling: if the fingers are cut together with the palm, the diyah is still half, not more, because the palm is a dependent part (tabi') of the fingers for the function of grasping. The hadith 'In the two hands is the diyah, in one of them half' supports this. Then the ruling for cutting the hand with half the forearm: half diyah for the hand plus a just appraisal for the forearm. The main dispute is between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (who treat the forearm as separate, requiring hukumat) and a narration from Abu Yusuf (who treats the entire forearm as included in the hand, thus no additional compensation beyond half diyah). The commentator reconciles apparent contradictions in the definitions of 'hand' by noting that the benefit of grasping is the basis, and the forearm does not participate in grasping at all, so it is not included in the hand's arsh.

Key Terms
يد (yad): The hand, defined functionally as the grasping instrument, consisting of fingers and palm, excluding the forearm.
بطش (batash): The primary function of the hand; the loss of this function is the basis for diyah.
دية (diya): Fixed compensation for bodily injury, measured in camels.
حكومة (hukumat): A just appraisal (arbitrary compensation) for injuries that do not have a fixed diyah; determined by a qualified appraiser.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Half diyah plus a just appraisal for the forearm
C) Full diyah (100 camels) for the entire arm
D) A just appraisal for the entire arm

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi diyah for the hand is based on its grasping function; the forearm is not included and requires a separate hukumat.

The Diya for the Hand: Half the Full Diya
Ruling on diya for hand including palm and fingers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the diya for the hand (including palm and fingers) is half the full diya and explain why the palm is subordinate to the fingers.

Core Idea
The hand, from fingertips to wrist, carries half the diya; the palm adds no extra compensation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the compensation for injury to the hand. We focus on the hand itself—what it includes and how much diya is owed. The key ruling is that the hand, including the palm and fingers, is worth half of the full diya. The palm is considered subordinate to the fingers because the primary function of gripping is performed by the fingers, and the palm aids that function without adding separate value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Find the statement that the hand (yad) is half the diya. Note that the hand includes the palm and fingers, as clarified by the hadith and the definition of 'yad' as the limb from fingertips to wrist (zand).
The ruling is wajib (obligatory) compensation.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith: 'In the two hands is the full diya, and in one of them is half the diya.' This is a direct textual proof.
The hadith is ahad but accepted by the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the subordination of the palm
The passage explains that the palm is subordinate (tabi') to the fingers because gripping (batsh) occurs with the fingers, and the palm assists. Therefore, cutting the palm with the fingers does not increase the diya beyond half.
This is based on the purpose of the hand: it is the instrument of gripping.
4
Define the hand's boundary
The hand (yad) here refers to the part up to the wrist (zand), not the shoulder. This is supported by the verse of theft (Quran 5:38) which mentions cutting the hand at the wrist.
This distinguishes the Hanafi view from the Shafi'i, who include the forearm.
5
Apply the ruling
If someone cuts off the hand (including palm and fingers), the diya is half of the full diya. If only the fingers are cut, the diya is also half, because the fingers alone already constitute the hand's value.
The same applies if the palm is cut with the fingers—no extra compensation.

كتاب الديات اليد نصف الدية ولو الكف مع . مر . ومع نصف الساعد نصف الدية وحكومة وفي قطع أقول : القائل أن يقول لمن ذكر فيما مر أن في كل أصبع من أصابع اليدين والرجلين عشر الدية كان ذكر هذه المسألة هنا مستدركاً إذ لا شك أن خمسة أعشار الدية نصف الدية وعلم قطعاً مما أن في أصابع اليد الواحدة وهي خمس أصابع نصف الدية ولو لم يكن الاستلزام والاقتضاء في حصول العلم بمثله بل كان لا بد فيه من التصريح بها للزم أن يذكر أيضاً أن في الأصبعين عشري الدية وفي ثلاث أصابع ثلاثة أعشار الدية، وفي أربعة أصابع أربعة أعشار الدية إلى غير ذلك من المسائل المتروك ذكرها صراحة في الكتاب. ويمكن الجواب عنه بأن ذكر هذه المسألة هنا ليس ببيان نفسها أصالة حتى يتوهم الاستدراك بل ليكون ذكرها توطئة للمسألة المعاقبة إياها وهي قوله فإن قطعها مع الكف ففيه أيضاً نصف الدية، فالمقصود في البيان هنا أن قطع الأصابع وحدها وقطعها مع الكف سيان في الحكم هذا قال في الوقاية في هذا المقام وفي أصابع يد بلا كف ومعها نصف الدية. قال وعن رحمه الله : (ولو مع الكف هذا متصل بما قبله أي في أصابع اليد نصف الدية وإن قطعها مع الكف ولا يزيد الأرش بسبب الكف لأن الكف سبب للأصابع في حق البطش فإن قوة البطش بها وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام في اليدين الدية، وفي أحدهما نصف الدية» واليد اسم لجارحة يقع بها البطش لأن اسم اليد يدل على القدرة والقوة والبطش يقع بالأصابع والكف فيجب فيها دية واحدة لأن منفعتها جنس واحد فيكون الكف تبعاً للأصابع. قال (ومع نصف الساعد نصف الدية وحكومة عدل نصف الدية في الكف والأصابع والحكومة نصف الساعد وهو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف، وعنه ما زاد على الأصابع من اليدين والرجلين من أصل الساعد والفخذ هو تبع فلا يزيد على الدية لأن الشارع أوجب في الواحدة منهما نصف الدية واليد اسم لهذه الجارحة إلى المنكب والرجل إلى الفخذ فلا يزيد على تقدير الشارع ولأن الساعد ليس له أرش مقدر فيه كالكف. ووجه الظاهر أن اليد اسم لآلة باطشة ووجوب الأرش باعتبار منفعة البطش، وكذا في الأرش ولا يقع البطش بالساعد أصلاً ولا تبعاً فلا يدخل في أرشه. وقال بعض الشراح : ولهما أن اليد آلة باطشة والبطش يتعلق بالكف والأصابع دون الذراع أقول : لقائل أن يقول الظاهر من هذا الكلام أن يكون لكل واحد من الكف والأصابع مدخل في البطش ومدلول قوله فيما قبل، ولأن الكف تبع للأصابع لأن البطش بها أن يكون الباطش هو الأصابع لا غير فبين كلاميه في الموضعين نوع تدافع وكان صاحب الكافي تفطن له حيث غير تحريره ههنا فقال : لهما أن أرش اليد إنما يجب باعتبار أنه آلة باطشة والأصل في البطش الأصابع والكف تبع لها أما الساعد فلا يتبعها لأنه غير متصل بها فلم يجعل تبعاً لها في حق التضمين ا هـ . أقول : يمكن التوفيق بين كلاميه أيضاً بنوع عناية وهو أن يقدر المضاف في قوله فيما قبل لأن البطش بها فلا ينافي أن يكون بالكف أيضاً بطش في الجملة بالتبعية فيرتفع التدافع، ولأنه لو جعل تبعاً لا يخلو إما أن يجعل تبعاً للأصابع أو الكف ولا وجه إلى الأول لوقوع الفصل بينهما بالكف ولا إلى الثاني لأن الكف تبع للأصابع ولا تبع للتبع ولا نسلم اليد اسم لهذه الجارحة إلى المنكب بل هي اسم إلى الزند إذا ذكرت في موضع القطع بدليل آية السرقة .
Book of Diyat. The hand is half the diya, even if with the palm. And with half the forearm: half the diya and government arbitration (hukuma). And in cutting... I say: One might say: Regarding what was mentioned earlier that in each finger of the fingers of the hands and feet is one-tenth of the diya, mentioning this issue here is redundant, since there is no doubt that five-tenths of the diya is half the diya, and it is known definitively that the fingers of one hand, which are five, are half the diya. If the implication and necessitation in attaining knowledge of such were not sufficient, but rather explicit mention were necessary, then it would also be necessary to mention that in two fingers is two-tenths, in three fingers three-tenths, etc., which the book deliberately omitted. It can be answered that mentioning this issue here is not to explain it itself, making redundancy suspected, but rather to introduce the following issue, namely his statement: 'If he cuts it with the palm, then in it also is half the diya.' So the purpose here is to show that cutting the fingers alone and cutting them with the palm are equal in ruling. This is stated in al-Wiqayah in this context: 'In the fingers of a hand without the palm and with it is half the diya.' He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'Even if with the palm?' This is connected to what came before: that in the fingers of the hand is half the diya, even if he cuts them with the palm, and the compensation does not increase due to the palm, because the palm is a cause for the fingers in terms of gripping, for the strength of gripping is with them. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'In the two hands is the full diya, and in one of them is half the diya.' The hand is a name for the limb by which gripping occurs, because the name 'hand' indicates ability, strength, and gripping occurs with the fingers and the palm, so a single diya is obligatory because their benefit is of one type, thus the palm is subordinate to the fingers. He said: 'And with half the forearm is half the diya and government arbitration (hukuma).' That is, half the diya for the palm and fingers, and government arbitration for half the forearm. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf. And from him is that what exceeds the fingers from the hands and feet of the base of the forearm and thigh is subordinate, so it does not exceed the diya, because the Lawgiver made obligatory in one of them half the diya, and the hand is a name for this limb up to the shoulder, and the foot up to the thigh, so it does not exceed the estimation of the Lawgiver, and because the forearm has no fixed compensation, like the palm. The apparent view is that the hand is a name for a grasping instrument, and the obligation of compensation is based on the benefit of gripping, and likewise in compensation, and gripping does not occur with the forearm at all, nor subordinately, so it is not included in its compensation. Some commentators said: To them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) that the hand is a grasping instrument, and gripping is attached to the palm and fingers, not to the forearm. I say: One could say that the apparent meaning of this statement is that each of the palm and fingers has a role in gripping, and the implication of his earlier statement that the palm is subordinate to the fingers because gripping occurs with them is that the gripper is the fingers only, so there is a kind of contradiction between his two statements in the two places. The author of al-Kafi perceived this and modified his wording here, saying: To them, the compensation of the hand is obligatory because it is a grasping instrument, and the basis of gripping is the fingers, and the palm is subordinate to them. As for the forearm, it does not follow them because it is not connected to them, so it is not made subordinate in terms of liability. I say: Reconciliation between his two statements is possible with some attention, by implying an additional element in his earlier statement: 'because the palm ... so it does not contradict that the palm also has some gripping in a subordinate manner, and thus the contradiction is removed. And because if it were made subordinate, it would either be subordinate to the fingers or to the palm, and the first is not possible due to the separation by the palm, nor the second because the palm is subordinate to the fingers, and there is no subordinate to a subordinate. And we do not concede that the hand is a name for this limb up to the shoulder; rather, it is a name up to the wrist when mentioned in the context of cut, as evidenced by the verse of theft.'
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from the Book of Diyat, establishing the compensation for injuries to the hand, fingers, palm, and forearm. It opens by confirming that the diya for the hand (including the palm) is half the full diya, and that cutting the fingers alone or with the palm is the same. The author explains that this ruling is not redundant but serves as an introduction to the case where the hand is cut with the palm. The primary evidence is the hadith of the Prophet (saw): 'In the two hands is the full diya, and in one of them is half the diya.' The hand is defined as the limb used for gripping, and since gripping is performed by the fingers and the palm, the palm is subordinate to the fingers. Therefore, cutting the palm does not increase the diya beyond half. As for the forearm, it has no fixed diya; instead, it carries a government arbitration (hukuma) in addition to the half diya for the hand. The passage then discusses a disagreement about whether the hand extends to the shoulder or the wrist, favoring the wrist based on the verse of theft (Quran 5:38). It also addresses a potential contradiction in the reasoning of some commentators, reconciling it by showing that the palm has a subordinate role in gripping.

Key Terms
اليد (al-yad): In this passage, 'yad' refers to the hand from the fingertips to the wrist (zand), not to the shoulder, as evidenced by the verse of theft.
البطش (al-batsh): Gripping or grasping power; the primary function of the hand for which diya is paid.
الدية (al-diya): Blood money; compensation paid for bodily harm, fixed by the Shariah.
الحكومة (al-hukuma): Government arbitration; an estimated compensation for injuries that have no fixed diya, determined by a judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the diya for cutting off the entire hand (including palm and fingers) if the full diya is 100 camels?
A) 100 camels
B) 50 camels
C) 25 camels
D) Government arbitration (hukuma)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that the hand (from fingertips to wrist) carries half the full diya, with the palm subordinate to the fingers, and the forearm is compensated separately by hukuma.

The Forearm: No Fixed Diya, Only Government Arbitration (Hukuma)
Ruling on diya for forearm and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the forearm has no fixed diya in the Hanafi school and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on this issue.

Core Idea
The forearm has no fixed compensation; it incurs government arbitration (hukuma) in addition to the hand's half diya.

In this passage, after establishing the diya for the hand, the author turns to the forearm (sa'id). Unlike the hand, the forearm does not have a fixed diya because its primary function is not gripping. Instead, it is compensated by government arbitration (hukuma), a judge-determined amount. The passage also discusses an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf's alternative view that the forearm is subordinate to the hand and does not increase the diya at all. We will explore the evidence and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for the forearm
The passage states: 'And with half the forearm: half the diya and government arbitration.' This means that if the forearm is cut along with the hand, the compensation is half diya for the hand plus hukuma for the forearm.
Half diya for the hand is already included; hukuma is additional.
2
Understand why no fixed diya
The reason given is that the forearm is not an instrument of gripping (batsh). Gripping occurs with the fingers and palm, not the forearm. Therefore, the Lawgiver did not assign a fixed diya to it.
This is based on the 'illa (effective cause) of compensation being the benefit of gripping.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf has a narration that the forearm is subordinate to the hand and does not increase the diya beyond half. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that it deserves separate hukuma.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
4
Apply the ruling
If someone cuts off the hand at the wrist and also half the forearm, the total compensation is half diya for the hand plus hukuma for the forearm.
If only the forearm is cut without the hand, it would be hukuma alone (no half diya).
5
Reconcile potential contradictions in reasoning
The author addresses a seeming contradiction: earlier the palm was said to be subordinate, yet the forearm is not subordinate even though both are not primary grippers. The reconciliation is that the palm is connected to the fingers and has a role in gripping, while the forearm is separate and has no gripping role at all.
This highlights the precision of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms
الساعد (al-sa'id): The forearm; the part of the arm between the wrist and the elbow.
الحكومة (al-hukuma): Government arbitration; an estimated compensation for injuries that have no fixed diya, determined by a judge.
التضمين (al-tadmin): Liability for compensation; the legal obligation to pay diya or other damages.

According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what is the total compensation for losing the hand (palm and fingers) and the forearm?

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Cutting a Palm with One or Two Fingers
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diya for palm with one or two fingers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on diya for cutting a palm with one or two fingers and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The palm is subordinate to the fingers; only finger diya is paid, nothing for the palm.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the diya (blood money) for cutting a palm that contains only one or two fingers. Abu Hanifa held that only the finger diya is payable because the palm is subordinate, while his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, argued for the greater of the two compensations. This lesson will walk through their arguments and identify the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa as presented in the matn: when a palm with one or two fingers is cut, only the finger diya (1/10 or 2/10 of full diya) is due, and nothing for the palm.
This is the starting point for the dispute.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's objection
State the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani: they say to look at the compensation of the palm and the fingers, and pay the greater, including the lesser in the greater.
Their reasoning is that both palm and fingers are primary in some respect.
3
Analyze the proofs
Trace the dalil for each side: Abu Hanifa argues that fingers are primary in reality and ruling (based on the Prophet's hadith on finger diya), while the Sahibayn argue that each is primary from a different angle and analogize to a head wound.
Abu Hanifa's proof emphasizes that the hand's function is through fingers.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify which view is relied upon for fatwa. The text states 'al-awwal asahh' (the first is more correct) because the finger diya is established by consensus (ijma'), which is like a text.
The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's, and the Sahibayn's view is not operative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وفي قطع الكف وفيها أصبع أو اصبعان عشرها أو خمسها ولا شيء في الكف) أي إذا كان في الكف أصبع أو أصبعان فقطعهما يجب عشر الدية في الأصبع الواحدة وخمسها في أصبعين ولا يجب في الكف شيء وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : ينظر إلى أرش الكف وإلى أرش ما فيها من الأصابع فيجب أكثرها ويدخل القليل في الكثير لأن الجمع بين الأرشين متعذر إجماعاً لأن الكل شيء واحد لأن ضمان الأصابع هو ضمان الكف وضمان الكف فيه ضمان الأصبع ، وكذا إهدار أحدهما متعذر أيضاً لأن كل واحد منهما أصل من وجه، أما الكف فلأن الأصابع قائمة به ، وأما الأصابع فلأنها الأصل في منفعة البطش، فإذا كان واحد منهما أصلاً من وجه رجحنا بالكثرة كما قلنا فيمن شج رأس إنسان وتناثر بعض شعر رأسه يدخل القليل في الكثير. ولأبي حنيفة رحمه الله أن الأصابع أصل حقيقة لأن منفعة اليد وهي البطش والقبض والبسط قائمة بها وكذا حكماً لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام جعل اليد بمقابلة الأصابع حيث أوجب في اليد نصف الدية، ثم جعل في كل أصبع عشراً من الإبل ومن ضرورته أن تكون كلها بمقابلة الأصابع دون الكف والأصل أولى بالاعتبار وإن قل ولا يظهر التتابع بمقابلة الأصل فلا يعارض حتى يصار إلى الترجيح بالكثرة، ولئن تعارضا فالترجيح بالأصل حقيقة وحكماً أولى من الترجيح بالكثرة ألا ترى أن الصغار إذا مع الكبار تجب فيها الزكاة تبعاً وإن كان الصغار أكثر ترجيحاً للأصل بخلاف ما استشهد به من الشجة لأن أحدهما ليس بتبع للآخر وروى الحسن عنه أن الباقي إذا كان دون الأصبع يعتبر أكثرهما إرشاداً لأن أرش ما دون الأصبع غير منصوص عليه وإنما يثبت باعتباره بالمنصوص عليه بنوع اجتهاد وكونه أصلاً باعتبار النص، فإذا لم يرد النص بأرش مفصل ولا مفصلين : اعتبرنا فيه الكثرة والأول أصح لأن أرشه ثبت بالإجماع وهو كالنص، ولو لم يبق في الكف أصبع غير منصوص عليه يجب عليه حكومة عدل لا يبلغ بها أرش الأصابع، ولا يجب فيه الأرش بالإجماع لأن الأصابع أصل على ما بينا وللأكثر حكم الكل فاستتبعت الكف كما إذا كانت كلها قائمة قوله وفي قطع الكف الخ» لا يخفى أنه مكرر مع قوله وفي كل اصبع عشر الدية وقوله ولا شيء في الكف الخ» لا يخفى أنه مكرر مع الكف» لأنه إذا علم أن الكف لا شيء فيه مع كل الأصابع علم بالأولى مع بعضها.
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And in cutting the palm when it has one or two fingers: one-tenth or one-fifth of the diya, and nothing for the palm). That is, if the palm contains one or two fingers and he cuts them, one-tenth of the diya is due for one finger and one-fifth for two fingers, and nothing is due for the palm. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Look at the compensation of the palm and the compensation of the fingers in it; the greater of them is due, and the lesser is included in the greater, because combining the two compensations is impossible by consensus, since the whole is one thing, because the guarantee of the fingers is the guarantee of the palm and the guarantee of the palm includes the guarantee of the finger. Likewise, disregarding either is also impossible because each is a primary part in some respect: the palm because the fingers are based on it, and the fingers because they are the basis in the benefit of gripping. So when each is a primary part in some respect, we give preponderance to the greater, as we said in the case of one who wounds the head of a person and some of his hair falls out: the lesser is included in the greater. For Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, the fingers are truly primary because the benefit of the hand—gripping, grasping, and opening—is realized through them, and likewise in ruling, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, made the hand corresponding to the fingers when he made half the diya obligatory for the hand, then made for each finger ten camels. From this it necessarily follows that all (the hand) corresponds to the fingers, not the palm. The primary part is more deserving of consideration, even if it is lesser, and no sequence appears in consideration of the primary part, so it is not opposed until it becomes necessary to resort to preponderance by greater quantity. And if they do conflict, then preponderance by being primary in reality and in ruling is more appropriate than preponderance by greater quantity. Do you not see that young (animals) when they are with older ones, zakat is due on them as a subordinate, even if the young are more numerous, giving preponderance to the original? This is unlike the analogy of the head wound, because neither is subordinate to the other. Al-Hasan narrated from him (Abu Hanifa) that if the remaining part is less than a finger, the greater of the two compensations is considered, because the compensation for less than a finger is not textually prescribed; rather, it is established by analogy to the textual prescription through some ijtihad. Since it is primary in terms of text, when no specific compensation is prescribed for one or two parts, we consider the greater. The first (Abu Hanifa's view) is more correct because its compensation is established by consensus, which is like a text. If no finger remains in the palm for which compensation is not textually prescribed, a fair government arbitration must be paid, not reaching the compensation of fingers, and compensation is not due by consensus, because the fingers are primary as we explained, and the majority has the ruling of the whole, so they take the palm in tow, as when all (fingers) are present. His statement 'And in cutting the palm, etc.' is obviously repetitive with his statement 'And in each finger is one-tenth of the diya' and his statement 'and nothing for the palm' is obviously repetitive with 'the palm' because if it is known that nothing is due for the palm with all the fingers, then a fortiori with some of them.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the diya for cutting the palm when it contains only one or two fingers. The ruling from the matn is clear: one-tenth diya for one finger, one-fifth for two fingers, and nothing for the palm. This is Abu Hanifa's view. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: they say that the greater of the two compensations (palm diya or finger diya) should be paid, and the lesser is included, because both the palm and the fingers are considered primary parts from different perspectives. They analogize to a head wound where some hair falls out. Abu Hanifa argues that the fingers are truly primary because the hand's functions (gripping, grasping) are performed by them, and the Prophet (saw) fixed the hand's diya as corresponding to the five fingers. The palm is subordinate. Therefore, only the finger's diya is given, and the palm adds nothing. The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's, as the text states 'the first is more correct' (al-awwal asahh). The passage also discusses a narration from al-Hasan that when the remaining part is less than a finger, the greater of the two compensations is considered, but the primary view is still that of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
الكف (al-kaf): The palm of the hand; in this passage, the focus is on when it contains one or two fingers.
الأصبع (al-isba'): A finger; the primary organ for gripping, with fixed diya of 1/10 of full diya each.
الأصل (al-asl): Primary part; the part that is independently considered in determining compensation, as opposed to subordinate (tabi').
التبع (al-tabi'): Subordinate part; its compensation is included in that of the primary part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the diya for cutting a palm that has only one finger?
A) One-tenth of the full diya (for the finger only).
B) Half the full diya (for the hand).
C) One-tenth plus government arbitration for the palm.
D) Two-tenths of the full diya.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi diya, the palm is subordinate to the fingers; only the diya for the fingers is paid when the palm contains one or two fingers.

Extra Finger and Child's Organs: Hukuma vs. Full Diyat
Hanafi ruling and inter-madhhab dispute on diyat for extra finger and child's organs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation for an extra finger (hukuma) and for a child's eye, penis, and tongue (hukuma if health unknown, full diyah if known), and evaluate the Shafi'i objection regarding the default assumption of health.

Core Idea
For child's organs, full diyat requires proof of health—the default assumption only defends, not claims.

This lesson examines two cases of diyat: an extra finger and the sensitive organs of a child. The Hanafi school makes a crucial distinction between parts valued for beauty (nose, ear) and those valued for function (eye, penis, tongue). The Shafi'i school challenges this, arguing that health is the default. We will trace the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two specific cases
The passage first discusses an extra finger (isba' za'idah) and then the eye, penis, and tongue of a child. Note that the ruling for the extra finger is unconditional, while the child's organs depend on knowledge of health.
2
Analyze the extra finger ruling
For the extra finger, compensation is wajib as an honor to the human, even though it has no function or beauty. Qisas is not possible due to uncertainty about equality. Since no fixed arsh exists, a just government (hukuma) is assessed by the judge.
3
Analyze the child's organs ruling
For the eye, penis, and tongue of a child, if health is not proven by evidence (sight, movement, speech), only hukuma is due. If health is established, full diyah applies as for an adult. Health is known through external indicators.
4
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that full diyah is always due because the default assumption is health (al-ghalib al-sihha), analogous to the ear and nose where arsh is fixed for beauty.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response argues that the apparent assumption (zahir) is sufficient only for defense, not for establishing a claim. The ear and nose are distinguished because their primary purpose is beauty, which is apparent; the function of the eye, tongue, and penis requires verification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله «ولو مع الزائدة وعين الصبي وذكره ولسانه إن لم يعرف صحته بنظر وحركة وكلام حكومة ومن شج رجلاً موضحة فذهب عقله أو شعر رأسه دخل أرش الموضحة في الدية وإن ذهب بنظر وحركة وكلام (حكومة عدل . أما الأصبع الزائدة فلأنها جزء الآدمي فيجب الأرش فيها تشريفاً له وإن لم يكن فيها نفع ولا زينة كما في السن الزائدة، ولا يجب فيها القصاص، وإن كان المقطوع أصبعاً زائدة ولأن المساواة شرط لوجوب القصاص في الطرف ولم يعلم تساويهما إلا بالظن فصار كالعبد يقطع طرف العبد فإن تعذر القصاص للشبهة وجب أرشها وليس لها أرش مقدر في الشرع فيجب فيها حكومة عدل بخلاف لحية الكوسج حيث لا يجب فيها شيء لأن اللحية لا يبقى فيها أثر الحلق فلا يلحقه الشين بل ببقاء الشعرات يلحقه ذلك فيكون نظير من قلم ظفر غيره بغير إذنه، وفي قطع الأصبع الزائدة يبقى أثر ويشينه ذلك فيجب الأرش. وأما عين الصبي وذكره ولسانه فلأن المقصود من هذه الأشياء المنفعة فإذا لم يعلم صحتها لا يجب أرشها كاملاً بالشك بخلاف المارن والأذن الشاخصة لأن المقصود منها الجمال وقد فوته وتعرف الصحة باللسان في الكلام، وفي الذكر بالحركة، وفي العين بما يستدل به على الرؤية وهو المراد بقوله إن لم تعرف صحته بنظر وحركة كلام فيكون بعد معرفة صحة ذلك حكمه حكم البالغ في الخطأ والعمد إذا ثبت ذلك بالبينة أو بإقرار الجاني، فإن أنكر ولم يقم به بينة فالقول قول الجاني وكذا إذا قال لا أعرف صحته لا يجب عليه الأرش كاملاً إلا بالبينة وقال الشافعي تجب الدية كاملة كيفما كان لأن الغالب فيه الصحة فأشبه الأذن والمارن. قلنا : الظاهر لا يصلح للاستحقاق وإنما يصلح للدفع وحاجتنا الاستحقاق وقد ذكرنا الفرق بين هذه الأشياء وبين الأذن والأنف .
His saying: 'And along with the extra (finger), and the eye of a child, his penis, and his tongue, if his health is not known by sight, movement, or speech, then a government (hukuma); and whoever inflicts a head wound (mudiha) on a man causing loss of his mind or hair, the arsh of the mudiha enters into the diyah; and if (the loss) is by sight, movement, or speech, then a just government (hukuma).' As for the extra finger, it is part of a human, so compensation is due for it as an honor to him, even if it has no benefit or beauty—like the extra tooth. Qisas is not due even if the amputated is an extra finger, because equality is a condition for qisas in limbs, and their equality is not known except by conjecture, so it becomes like a slave whose limb is cut by another slave; when qisas is prevented by doubt, its arsh is due. It has no prescribed arsh in the law, so a just government is due. Unlike the beard of a beardless man where nothing is due, because shaving leaves no lasting effect, so it does not bring shame; rather, hair remaining brings shame, so it is like one who trims another's nail without permission. In cutting an extra finger, an effect remains and shames him, so arsh is due. As for the eye of a child, his penis, and his tongue, because the purpose of these things is function; if their health is not known, full arsh is not due due to doubt—unlike the nose (marin) and protruding ear, because their purpose is beauty and he has destroyed it. Health is known by the tongue through speech, by the penis through movement, and by the eye through what indicates vision—that is what is meant by his saying 'if his health is not known by sight, movement, or speech.' So after knowledge of his health, its ruling is like that of an adult in error and intent, if established by evidence or confession of the offender. If he denies and no evidence is brought, the statement is the offender's. Likewise, if he says 'I do not know his health,' the full arsh is not due upon him except by evidence. Al-Shafi'i said: Full diyah is due in any case because the dominant assumption is health, so it resembles the ear and nose. We say: The apparent (dominant assumption) is not valid for establishing a claim, only for defense, and we need a claim. And we have mentioned the difference between these things and the ear and nose.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings on diyat for specific body parts. First, for an extra (supernumerary) finger—a digit beyond the normal five—the Hanafi school holds that compensation is due as an honor to the human, even if it has no function or beauty, similar to an extra tooth. However, qisas (retaliation) is not applicable because equality between the limb and the victim's limb is not certain; only conjecture exists. Since there is no fixed arsh in the sacred texts for an extra finger, a just government (hukuma) is paid, assessed by the judge based on the injury's effect. This contrasts with a beardless man's facial hair (lihyat al-kusaj), where no compensation is due because shaving leaves no lasting mark, but if the hair is plucked, it may cause shame. Second, for the eye, penis, and tongue of a child (or an adult where health is unknown), full diyat is not due if the health or functionality of the organ is unknown. These organs primarily serve a function (sight, urination/sex, speech), not beauty. So before proven healthy, only a government is paid. Health is determined by evidence: the tongue by speech, the penis by erection/movement, the eye by tests showing vision. Once health is established, the ruling is like that for an adult, and full arsh or diyah may apply if proven by evidence or confession. If the offender denies and no evidence, his word is taken; if he claims ignorance of health, full arsh is not due without proof. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that health is the default, so full diyah is always due, comparing these organs to the nose and ear which have fixed arsh because beauty is the primary consideration. The Hanafi response is that the apparent (zahir) assumption is not sufficient to establish a right of compensation; it only serves as a defense. The difference is that the nose and ear are valued for beauty, whereas the child's organs are for function, which requires proof.

Key Terms
أصبع زائدة (isba' za'idah): Extra finger beyond the normal five; compensation is through hukuma, not fixed arsh.
حكومة (hukuma): A just compensation assessed by the judge for injuries without a fixed arsh, not exceeding the arsh of the nearest limb.
مارن (marin): The soft part of the nose (tip); it has a fixed arsh (1/5 of full diyat?) because its loss affects beauty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling for compensation if an extra finger is cut?
A) Full diyat of a finger (1/10 of full diyat)
B) Qisas is due
C) A just government (hukuma) is due
D) Nothing is due

Key Takeaway
Compensation for injuries depends on the nature of the organ and proof of health; Hanafi school uses hukuma when fixed arsh is absent or health is uncertain.

Mudiha Causing Loss of Mind or Hair: Inclusion of Arsh in Diyah
Hanafi ruling with proof (qiyas) and a commentator's objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that the arsh of a mudiha is included in the full diyah when the victim loses his mind or all scalp hair, and evaluate the commentator's objection based on Caliph 'Umar's judgement.

Core Idea
Loss of mind is like death for diyat: the wound's arsh merges into the full diyah.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling in diyat: when a head wound that exposes bone (mudiha) causes loss of mind or permanent loss of scalp hair, the fixed compensation (arsh) for the wound is not paid separately; instead, it is included in the full blood money (diyah). The basis is a qiyas (analogy) to death, since loss of mind nullifies all bodily benefits. However, the commentator Ibn Nujaym raises a troubling objection: the precedent of Caliph 'Umar awarding four full diyats for a single blow that caused loss of mind, speech, hearing, and sight seems to contradict this analogy. Understanding this ruling and its critique deepens your grasp of Hanafi reasoning in injury compensation.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling
Identify the legal consequence: if a mudiha causes loss of mind or hair, the arsh of the wound is subsumed into the full diyah (not paid separately).
The text says 'dakhala arshu al-mudihah fi al-diyah' – enters into the diyah.
2
Analyze the Proof (Qiyas)
The proof is an analogy to death. Loss of mind eliminates the benefit of all limbs, just like death. Therefore, the diyah covers the injury as if the victim died, and no separate arsh is due.
The illa (effective cause) is the total loss of functional benefit.
3
Consider the Restriction
The ruling is restricted to mudiha. If a different injury (e.g., cutting a hand) causes loss of mind, the arsh is not included, as will be explained later in the text.
This suggests the analogy is specific to head wounds exposing bone.
4
Evaluate the Objection
The commentator points out that if loss of mind is truly equivalent to death, then 'Umar's judgement of four diyats for a single blow causing multiple losses (mind, speech, hearing, sight) would contradict the principle (since death yields only one diyah). He asks for reflection, leaving the issue unresolved.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school; the ruling stands but is challenged.
5
Apply the Rule for Hair Loss
For hair loss due to mudiha: if a part of the hair is lost permanently, arsh of the mudiha is due; if all hair is lost permanently, full diyah is due. If hair regrows, no compensation.
The arsh is for permanent loss; regrowth negates the loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ومن شج رجلاً موضحة فذهب عقله أو شعر رأسه دخل أرش الموضحة في الدية فصار كما إذا أوضحه فمات لأن تفويت العقل يبطل منفعة جميع الأعضاء. قيد بالموضحة لأنه لو قطع يده فذهب عقله لا يدخل كما سيأتي. أقول : فيه نظر إذ لو كان فوات العقل بمنزلة الموت وكان هذا مدار دخول أرش الموضحة في الدية لما تم ما سبق في فصل فيما دون النفس من أنه روي أن عمر رضي الله عنه قضى بأربع ديات في ضربة واحدة ذهب فيها العقل والكلام والسمع والبصر فإنهم صرحوا بأنه لو مات من لم يكن فيه إلا دية واحدة فيتأمل وأرش الموضحة يجب بفوات جزء من الشعر حتى لو لم ينبت تجب الدية بفوات كل الشعر . قال صاحب النهاية : أي لو نبت الشعر والتأمت الشجة فصار كما كان لا يجب شيء، فثبت بهذا أن وجوب أرش الموضحة بشبب فوات الشعر ا هـ . وقال صاحب العناية : قوله وأرش الموضحة تجب بفوات جزء من الشعر لبيان الجزئية. قوله حتى لو نبت يعني الشعر يسقط يعني أرش الموضحة لبيان أن الأرش يجب بالفوات؛ كذا في النهاية، وليس بمفتقر إليه لكونه معلوماً ا أقول : إن قوله وليس بمفتقر إليه لكونه
He (the author) said: 'And whoever inflicts a mudiha (wound exposing bone) on a man causing loss of his mind or the hair of his head, the arsh of the mudiha enters into the diyah, so it becomes as if he caused a mudiha leading to death, because the loss of the mind nullifies the benefit of all limbs.' He restricted it to mudiha because if he cuts his hand and his mind is lost, it is not included, as will come. I say: There is consideration; if the loss of mind is like death and this is the basis for the mudiha's arsh entering into the diyah, then what came earlier in the chapter on cases below life (i.e., injuries not causing death) would not hold—that it is narrated that 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) judged four full diyats for a single strike that caused loss of mind, speech, hearing, and sight, and they explicitly stated that if he had died, there would have been only one diyah. So reflect. And the arsh of the mudiha is due for the loss of a part of the hair, so if the hair does not grow back, full diyah is due for the loss of all the hair. The author of al-Nihayah said: That is, if the hair grows back and the wound heals, returning to its original state, nothing is due. Thus it is established that the obligation of the arsh of the mudiha is due to the loss of hair. The author of al-‘Inayah said: His statement 'and the arsh of the mudiha is due for the loss of a part of the hair' is to indicate partiality. His statement 'even if it grows' means the hair falls out, meaning the arsh of the mudiha (falls) to indicate that the arsh is due for the loss; similarly in al-Nihayah, and it is not in need of this because it is known. I say: His statement 'and it is not in need of this because it is known'...
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a head wound that exposes bone (mudiha) causes loss of mind or loss of hair. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that the arsh (compensation) of the mudiha is included in the full diyah if the victim loses his mind or his scalp hair falls out. The reasoning: loss of mind is equivalent to death because it destroys the benefit of all limbs; thus the wound's arsh merges into the diyat (as if he had died). The commentator then raises an objection: if loss of mind is like death, then in the case of a single blow causing loss of mind, speech, hearing, and sight—for which Caliph 'Umar judged four full diyats—if the man died, he said there would be only one diyah. The commentator finds inconsistency, asking for reflection. He then discusses hair loss: the arsh of the mudiha is due for the loss of hair; if the hair does not regrow, full diyah is due for total loss. The author of al-Nihayah clarifies that if the hair regrows and the wound heals, nothing is due, proving that the arsh is contingent on permanent loss of hair. The author of al-‘Inayah explains that the text's phrase 'arsh of the mudiha is due for the loss of a part of the hair' indicates that the arsh is for the partial loss of hair; if the hair grows back, the arsh is not due. The commentator notes that this is obvious and perhaps not needed, but it is included for clarity.

Key Terms
موضحة (mudiha): A wound that exposes the bone; triggers a specific arsh as a type of shajja.
فوَّت العقل (fawwat al-'aql): Loss of intellect/mind due to injury; treated like death for diyat purposes.
شعر (sha'r): Hair of the head; its loss due to wound may require arsh; if all hair lost permanently, full diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, why is the arsh of a mudiha included in the full diyah when the victim loses his mind?
A) Because the mudiha is a serious injury that always results in death
B) Because loss of mind is analogized to death, nullifying all bodily benefits
C) Because the victim explicitly waived the arsh
D) Because the Hanafi school does not recognize arsh for head wounds

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a mudiha that causes permanent loss of mind or all scalp hair results in only one full diyah, with the wound's arsh included, based on a qiyas to death.

Compensation for an Extra Finger
Ruling on extra finger compensation with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why compensation for an extra finger is wajib and distinguish when it requires fair compensation (حكومة) rather than fixed arsh or qisas.

Core Idea
An extra finger requires compensation to honor the human, but only حكومة because no fixed arsh exists.

This lesson examines the ruling on cutting an extra finger. The Hanafi school holds that even though the finger may be useless, it is a human part deserving compensation. However, because retaliation (qisas) is not possible due to doubt, and no fixed compensation exists, the law prescribes fair assessment by a judge (حكومة). We will unpack the reasoning and contrast it with the case of a beard or nail.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is cutting an extra (supernumerary) finger. The ruling: wajib compensation (حكومة).
2
Examine the proof: human dignity
The extra finger is a part of a human being, so compensation is wajib as an honor, even if it has no benefit or beauty.
Analogous to an extra tooth.
3
Understand why no qisas
Qisas requires equality between limbs; equality with an extra finger is uncertain, as it contradicts the norm. Doubt prevents qisas.
Qiyas: like a slave cutting another slave's limb where equality is doubtful.
4
Note absence of fixed arsh
The extra finger has no fixed compensation (arsh) in Shariah, so fair compensation (حكومة) becomes wajib.
5
Distinguish from beard and nail
Shaving a smooth beard leaves no lasting defect, so no compensation. Cutting an extra finger leaves a defect and disfigurement, so wajib.
Contrast with filing a nail without permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الزائدة وعين الصبي وذكره ولسانه إن لم يعرف صحته بنظر وحركة وكلام حكومة. أما الأصبع الزائدة فلأنها جزء الآدمي فيجب الأرش فيها تشريفاً له وإن لم يكن فيها نفع ولا زينة كما في السن الزائدة، ولا يجب فيها القصاص، وإن كان المقطوع أصبعاً زائدة ولأن المساواة شرط لوجوب القصاص في الطرف ولم يعلم تساويهما إلا بالظن فصار كالعبد يقطع طرف العبد فإن تعذر القصاص للشبهة وجب أرشها وليس لها أرش مقدر في الشرع فيجب فيها حكومة عدل بخلاف لحية الكوسج حيث لا يجب فيها شيء لأن اللحية لا يبقى فيها أثر الحلق فلا يلحقه الشين بل ببقاء الشعرات يلحقه ذلك فيكون نظير من قلم ظفر غيره بغير إذنه، وفي قطع الأصبع الزائدة يبقى أثر ويشينه ذلك فيجب الأرش. وأما عين الصبي وذكره ولسانه فلأن المقصود من هذه الأشياء المنفعة فإذا لم يعلم صحتها لا يجب أرشها كاملاً بالشك بخلاف المارن والأذن الشاخصة لأن المقصود منها الجمال وقد فوته وتتعرف الصحة باللسان في الكلام، وفي الذكر بالحركة، وفي العين بما يستدل به على الرؤية وهو المراد بقوله إن لم تعرف صحته بنظر وحركة كلام فيكون بعد معرفة صحة ذلك حكمه حكم البالغ في الخطأ والعمد إذا ثبت ذلك بالبينة أو بإقرار الجاني، فإن أنكر ولم يقم به بينة فالقول قول الجاني وكذا إذا قال لا أعرف صحته لا يجب عليه الأرش كاملاً إلا بالبينة وقال الشافعي تجب الدية كاملة كيفما كان لأن الغالب فيه الصحة فأشبه الأذن والمارن. قلنا : الظاهر لا يصلح للاستحقاق وإنما يصلح للدفع وحاجتنا الاستحقاق وقد ذكرنا الفرق هذه الأشياء . الأذن والأنف .
The extra finger and the eye of a child, his penis, and his tongue: if his health is not known by sight, movement, and speech, then fair compensation. As for the extra finger, it is a part of a human being, so compensation is obligatory in it as an honor to him even if there is no benefit or beauty in it, just like the extra tooth. Retaliation is not obligatory in it, even if what was cut was an extra finger, because equality is a condition for wajib of retaliation in a limb and their equality is not known except by conjecture, so it becomes like a slave cutting the limb of a slave. When retaliation is prevented due to doubt, its compensation becomes wajib, and it has no fixed compensation in the Shariah, so fair compensation is wajib in it. Unlike the beard of a smooth-faced man where nothing is wajib because the beard does not retain the effect of shaving, so no defect is attached, but if hair remains, it becomes like the case of someone who files another's nail without permission. In cutting an extra finger, an effect remains and disfigures it, so compensation is wajib. As for the eye of a child, his penis, and his tongue, the purpose of these things is benefit. If their health is not known, full compensation is not wajib due to doubt, unlike the nose tip and protruding ear because their purpose is beauty and he has destroyed it. Health is known by the tongue through speech, in the penis by movement, and in the eye by what indicates vision. This is what is meant by his saying 'if his health is not known by sight, movement, and speech.' So after knowing its health, its ruling is the ruling of an adult in error and intent if that is established by evidence or by the confess of the offender. If he denies and no evidence is established, then the statement is the statement of the offender. Similarly, if he says 'I do not know his health,' the full compensation is not wajib upon him except by evidence. Al-Shafi'i said: The full blood money is wajib in any case because the predominant is health, so it resembles the ear and the nose tip. We said: The apparent (predominance) is not suitable for entitlement, rather it is suitable for defense, and our need is for entitlement, and we have mentioned the difference between these things: the ear and the nose.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining when fair compensation (حكومة) is given for injuries on certain body parts. The author begins by stating the ruling: an extra finger, and the eye, penis, and tongue of a child, if their health is not verified, require fair compensation. The commentary then expands the reasoning. For the extra finger, it is part of a human, so compensation honors that, even if useless. No qisas because equality doubtful, and no fixed arsh, so حكومة. A beard that does not regrow after shaving gets no compensation because the defect is temporary. For the child's organs, compensation is full if health is proven; otherwise, حكومة, since benefit is the purpose. The author then presents a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues full diya always because health is presumed. The Hanafi response: predominant opinion suffices for defense, not for claiming compensation. The proof: qiyas on the case of a free person's limb vs. slave's limb, and consideration of doubt.

Key Terms
حكومة (hukūmah): Fair compensation assessed by a judge for injuries without a fixed arsh in Shariah.
أرش (arsh): Financial compensation for injury to a body part, less than full diya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person cuts off an extra finger whose health cannot be verified, what compensation is due?
A) Full diya (blood money)
B) Fixed arsh for a normal finger
C) Fair compensation (حكومة)
D) No compensation

Key Takeaway
An extra finger, though non-functional, is a human part; compensation is wajib via حكومة, not full arsh.

Compensation for Child's Eye, Penis, and Tongue
Ruling on child's eye, penis, tongue compensation with inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that health must be proven for full arsh on child's organs, and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
Full compensation for child's organs requires proven health; otherwise, حكومة suffices.

This lesson addresses injuries to a child's eye, penis, and tongue. The Hanafi school requires verification of health (sight, movement, speech) for full arsh; otherwise, fair compensation. The Shafi'i school argues that health is predominant, requiring full diya. We will examine the proofs and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the organs and condition
The organs are the child's eye, penis, and tongue. The condition for full arsh: health must be known via sight (for eye), movement (for penis), speech (for tongue).
2
Understand the rationale: benefit as purpose
The purpose of these organs is benefit (manfa'ah). If health is not proven, full compensation is not wajib because doubt prevents the claim.
Contrast with nose tip and ear: purpose is beauty, so fixed arsh applies even if health unknown.
3
Learn how health is verified
Health of tongue: by speech. Health of penis: by movement (erection). Health of eye: by signs of vision. Once verified, ruling is like an adult.
4
Examine the dispute with Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i holds full diya wajib always because health is predominant (ghalib). Hanafi response: predominance suffices for defense (daf') but not for claim (istihqaq); proof is required.
The practical difference: if a child's eye is injured and health unknown, Hanafis give حكومة; Shafi'is give full diya.
5
Apply the ruling
If injury is proven by evidence or confession, full arsh applies. If perpetrator denies and no evidence, statement of perpetrator is accepted, and full arsh not wajib unless evidence brought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الزائدة وعين الصبي وذكره ولسانه إن لم يعرف صحته بنظر وحركة وكلام حكومة. أما الأصبع الزائدة فلأنها جزء الآدمي فيجب الأرش فيها تشريفاً له وإن لم يكن فيها نفع ولا زينة كما في السن الزائدة، ولا يجب فيها القصاص، وإن كان المقطوع أصبعاً زائدة ولأن المساواة شرط لوجوب القصاص في الطرف ولم يعلم تساويهما إلا بالظن فصار كالعبد يقطع طرف العبد فإن تعذر القصاص للشبهة وجب أرشها وليس لها أرش مقدر في الشرع فيجب فيها حكومة عدل بخلاف لحية الكوسج حيث لا يجب فيها شيء لأن اللحية لا يبقى فيها أثر الحلق فلا يلحقه الشين بل ببقاء الشعرات يلحقه ذلك فيكون نظير من قلم ظفر غيره بغير إذنه، وفي قطع الأصبع الزائدة يبقى أثر ويشينه ذلك فيجب الأرش. وأما عين الصبي وذكره ولسانه فلأن المقصود من هذه الأشياء المنفعة فإذا لم يعلم صحتها لا يجب أرشها كاملاً بالشك بخلاف المارن والأذن الشاخصة لأن المقصود منها الجمال وقد فوته وتتعرف الصحة باللسان في الكلام، وفي الذكر بالحركة، وفي العين بما يستدل به على الرؤية وهو المراد بقوله إن لم تعرف صحته بنظر وحركة كلام فيكون بعد معرفة صحة ذلك حكمه حكم البالغ في الخطأ والعمد إذا ثبت ذلك بالبينة أو بإقرار الجاني، فإن أنكر ولم يقم به بينة فالقول قول الجاني وكذا إذا قال لا أعرف صحته لا يجب عليه الأرش كاملاً إلا بالبينة وقال الشافعي تجب الدية كاملة كيفما كان لأن الغالب فيه الصحة فأشبه الأذن والمارن. قلنا : الظاهر لا يصلح للاستحقاق وإنما يصلح للدفع وحاجتنا الاستحقاق وقد ذكرنا الفرق هذه الأشياء . الأذن والأنف .
