فقال اشجه موضحة وأترك الباقي ليس له ذلك. والأصل عنده أن الفعل الواحد إذا أوجب مالاً في البعض سقط القصاص سواء كانا عضوين أو عضواً واحداً لا يجب لهما. وفي الخلاصة: إن الفعل في محلين مختلفين فيكون جنايتين لأن الفعل يتعدد بتعدد أثره فصار كجنايتين مبتدأتين فالشبهة في أحدهما لا يتعدى إلى الآخر. ولأبي حنيفة أن الجزاء بالمثل والجرح الأول سار وليس وسعه الساري فيسقط القصاص ويجب المال والدليل على أنه سار إن فعله أثر في نفس واحدة والسراية عبارة عن إيلام يتعاقب عن الجناية على البدن ويتحقق ذلك في موضعين منهما كما يتحقق في الأطراف مع النفس بأن مات من الجناية بخلاف نفسين فإن الفعل في النفس الثانية مباشرة على حدة ليس بسراية الأولى أو نقول : إن ذهاب البصر ونحوه جعل بطريق التسبب فإن الفعل باق على اسمه لم يتغير، والأصل في سراية الأفعال أن لا يبقى الأول بعد حدوث السراية كالقطع إذا سرى إلى النفس صار قتلاً فلم يبق قطعاً، وههنا الشجة أو القطع لم ينعدم بذهاب البصر ونحوه فكان الفعل الأول تسبباً إلى فوات البصر ونحوه بمنزلة حفر البئر والتسبب لا يوجب القصاص. وعن محمد رحمه الله في المسألة الأولى وهي ما إذا اشجه موضحة فذهب بصره أنه يجب القصاص منهما رواية ابن سماعة عنه، ووجهه أن الفعل انتسب إلى فاعله شرعاً حتى يجعل الفاعل مباشراً للسراية فيؤخذ به كما لو سرى إلى النفس فإنه يجب ويعتبر قتلاً بطريق المباشرة بخلاف ما لو قطع أصبعاً فشلت بجنبها أخرى أو شجه موضحة فذهب عقله أو كلامه لا يجب القصاص في السمع والكلام والشلل لعدم الإمكان، وفي البصر يجب لإمكان الاستيفاء ألا ترى أنه لو أذهبه وحده بفعل مقصود منه تجب الدية وإن شج رجلاً فالتحم ولم يبق له أثر أو ضرب فجرح فبرأ وذهب أثره فلا يجب القصاص في البصر دون الشلل والسمع والكلام فافترقا .
He (the author) said: (If he inflicted a head wound exposing bone (muwaddihah) and both eyes were lost, or he cut a finger and another became paralyzed, or cut a joint except that the remaining part became useless, or cut off a whole hand, or broke half a tooth and the remainder blackened, then there is no qisas. And this is all the absolute statement of Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Qisas is obligatory for the muwaddihah and diya for the eyes in the case where he inflicted a muwaddihah and both eyes were lost; similarly, if he cut a finger and another adjacent finger became paralyzed, he is subjected to qisas for the first and arsh is due for the other. According to him (Abu Hanifa), since qisas is not obligatory for the two limbs, full arsh is due for each of them. And if it is a single limb, like cutting the finger from the upper joint and the remainder becomes useless, only one arsh suffices if he does not benefit from what remains. If he does benefit, then diya for the cut part and a fair compensation (hukumat 'adl) for the remainder is due by consensus. Similarly, if he broke half the tooth and the remainder blackened, yellowed, or reddened, the full tooth diya is due by consensus. If he said, 'Cut the upper joint and leave the rest,' or said, 'Break the already broken part of the tooth and leave the rest,' that is not permissible because the act itself did not become grounds for qisas, like the case of shajjah munqilah where he said, 'Inflict a muwaddihah and leave the rest' – that is not allowed. The principle according to him (Abu Hanifa) is that when a single act necessitates financial liability for part, qisas falls, whether regarding two limbs or a single limb; it is not required for them. In al-Khulasa: The act is in two different places, thus two offenses, because the act multiplies by the multiplication of its effect, so it is like two independent offenses; the doubt in one does not extend to the other. Abu Hanifa's proof: Retribution is by equivalence, and the first wound has spread (saray), and its spread is not encompassed, so qisas falls and financial liability is due. The evidence that it has spread is that his action had an effect in one soul (nafs), and saraya is a term for pain that follows from the injury to the body, and this is realized in two places from it just as it is realized in the limbs along with the soul when he dies from the injury, unlike two souls because the act regarding the second soul is a separate direct act, not saraya of the first. Or we say: Loss of sight and the like are caused through causation (tasabbub), as the act remains in its name unchanged. The principle in saraya of acts is that the first does not remain after the occurrence of saraya, like cutting if it spreads to the soul becomes killing and is no longer a cut. Here, the head wound or cut does not cease to exist with the loss of sight and the like, so the first act becomes a cause for the loss of sight and the like, like digging a well; causation does not necessitate qisas. From Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) regarding the first issue, i.e., if he inflicted a muwaddihah and his sight was lost, that qisas is obligatory for both – a narration from Ibn Sama'a from him. Its reasoning: The act is attributed to its doer legally so that the doer is considered a direct agent of the saraya and is held liable, like if it spread to the soul, then it is obligatory and considered killing by direct action, unlike if he cut a finger and another adjacent became paralyzed, or inflicted a muwaddihah and his mind or speech was lost – qisas is not required for hearing, speech, and paralysis due to impossibility. For sight, it is possible to exact retaliation, do you not see that if he destroyed it alone by an intentional act, diya is due? And if he injured a man and it healed with no trace, or struck and wounded and it healed and its trace disappeared, then qisas is not due for sight, unlike paralysis, hearing, and speech – so they differ.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling on qisas when a single act of injury causes damage in two different body parts or causes partial damage that spreads. The text first states Abu Hanifa's absolute position: if a single act (e.g., a head wound that causes loss of eyesight, or cutting a finger that causes paralysis in an adjacent finger, or cutting a joint that leaves the remaining part useless, or breaking half a tooth that blackens the rest) results in harm in two locations or in spreading harm, then no qisas is due; instead, full financial compensation (diya or arsh) for each damaged part must be paid. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree and hold that qisas is still due for the part that was directly injured (e.g., the wound or the cut finger), while diya is due for the consequential damage (e.g., the eyes or the paralyzed finger). They argue that the act is in two different places and should be treated as two separate offenses, so a doubt in one does not affect the other. Abu Hanifa's proof is based on the principle of 'al-jaza' bil-mithl' (retribution by equivalence) and the concept of saraya (spread of the injury). He argues that the first wound is 'saraya' (its effect spreads) and since its full extent is not known, qisas is not possible; instead, financial compensation is obligatory. He compares it to a cut that spreads to the soul and becomes killing – there the original cut is no longer considered a cut. Here, the head wound or cut does not vanish with the loss of sight, so it is a cause (tasabbub) like digging a well, which does not necessitate qisas. The text also mentions a narration from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan via Ibn Sama'a in which he agrees with Abu Hanifa that qisas is due for both the wound and the lost sight, because the act is attributed to the doer as a direct cause. The discussion ends by contrasting sight with paralysis, hearing, and speech: for these, qisas is impossible due to lack of exact equivalence, so only financial liability applies. The passage is an expansion probe (sharh) explaining the matn ruling.

Key Terms
سراية (saraya): Spread of the effect of an injury from the original site to another part of the body, such as a wound causing blindness or a cut causing paralysis.
موضحة (muwaddihah): A head wound that exposes the bone.
تسبب (tasabbub): Causation; an act that indirectly leads to harm, as opposed to direct causation (mubasharah). In qisas, causation generally does not require retaliation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person cuts another's finger and due to that cut, an adjacent finger becomes paralyzed, what is the Hanafi ruling on qisas for the first finger?
A) Qisas is obligatory for the cut finger and arsh for the paralysis.
B) No qisas for either; full arsh for both fingers.
C) Qisas is obligatory only for the paralyzed finger.
D) Diya for the cut finger and no compensation for paralysis.

Key Takeaway
When a single injury spreads to another part of the body (saraya), exact retaliation becomes impossible, so qisas is replaced by financial compensation for all damages.

Tooth Growing Back: No Compensation According to Abu Hanifa
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for regrown tooth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding compensation for a regrown tooth and evaluate the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn using the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A tooth that grows back may cancel compensation — Abu Hanifa says no arsh; Sahibayn say full arsh.

In this lesson, we examine a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: if a tooth is knocked out and a new one grows in, does the liability for compensation (arsh) remain or drop? The matn presents Abu Hanifa's view that it drops, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, insist full arsh is due. Their disagreement turns on how to interpret the regrowth: is it a separate blessing that nullifies the injury's effect, or is the obligation fixed at the moment of injury? Let's walk through the reasoning and the later tarjih.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the legal issue: whether arsh is obligatory when a knocked-out tooth grows back. This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement.
The matn clearly presents the two positions.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa holds that arsh drops; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that full arsh remains due.
Both positions are from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Follow the reasoning (dalil) of each
Sahibayn use qiyas: injuring a tooth is like destroying property; the obligation is fixed at the moment of injury, and later acquisition of replacement does not cancel it. Abu Hanifa's implicit reasoning: regrowth is a new blessing that negates the original injury's effect.
The analogy to property destruction is explicit in the text.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
Al-Tatimma and al-‘Inaya discuss the correct view. The mufta bihi: for an adult, wait until the wound heals; if the tooth grows back, no arsh; if not, arsh is due. For a child, wait a full year. This effectively upholds Abu Hanifa's position with conditions.
Al-‘Inaya criticizes the claim of consensus and cites a hadith about waiting a year.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: if the tooth grows back, Abu Hanifa says no payment, Sahibayn say full payment. The mufta bihi requires waiting, so immediate payment is not made until healing or the year passes.
The dispute affects real-world cases of injury compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن قلع سنة فنبت مكانها أخرى سقط (الأرش) وهذا عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله . وقالا : عليه الأرش كاملاً لأن الجناية وقعت موجبة له والتي نبتت نعمة مبتدأة من الله تعالى فصار كما لو أتلف مال إنسان فحصل للمتلف عليه مال آخر ولهذا يستأني حولاً بالإجماع أي يؤجل سنة بالإجماع. وذكر في التتمة أن سن البالغ إذا سقط ينتظر حتى يبرأ موضع السن لا الحول هو الصحيح لأن نبات سن البالغ نادر فلا يفيد التأجيل إلا أن قبل البرء لا يقتص ولا يؤخذ الأرش لأنه لا يدري عاقبته .اهـ. قال صاحب العناية بعد نقل ذلك اجمالاً : وذلك ليس بظاهر وإنما الظاهر ما قالوه لأن الحول يشتمل على الفصول الأربعة ولها تأثير فيما يتعلق ببدن الإنسان فكل فصل منها يوافق مزاج المجني عليه فيؤثر في إنباته قال : ولكن قوله بالإجماع فيه نظر لأنه قال في الذخيرة وبعض مشايخنا قال الاستيناء حولاً من فصل القلع في البالغ والصغير جميعاً لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام في الجراحات كلها يستأني حولاً وهو كما ترى ينافي الإجماع.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he extracts a tooth and another grows in its place, the compensation is dropped). This is according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Full compensation is due, because the injury occurred and obligated it, and the new growth is a fresh blessing from Allah, so it is like someone who destroyed another's property and then the owner obtained other property. For this reason, it is deferred for a year by consensus, i.e., it is postponed for a year by consensus. And it is mentioned in al-Tatimma that if the tooth of an adult falls out, one waits until the place of the tooth heals, not a year; that is the correct view because the growth of an adult's tooth is rare, so deferral is not beneficial, but before healing no qisas is executed and no compensation is taken because one does not know its outcome. End quote. The author of al-‘Inaya said after summarizing that: That is not apparent; rather the apparent is what they said because the year includes the four seasons which have an effect on the human body, each season suiting the temperament of the victim and affecting its growth. He said: But his statement 'by consensus' is questionable because he said in al-Dhakhira: Some of our scholars said deferring for a year from the season of extraction is for both adult and child due to his statement, peace be upon him, regarding all wounds: one waits for a year. And that, as you see, contradicts consensus.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of compensation (arsh) when a tooth that has been knocked out grows back. The matn states the ruling of Abu Hanifa: if the tooth grows back, no arsh is due. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree, holding that full arsh is still obligatory. Their reasoning is that the injury itself created the obligation, and the new growth is a separate blessing from Allah, analogous to a case where someone destroys another's property but then the owner acquires other property—the original liability remains. For this reason, they argue that one should wait a full year (by consensus, they claim) to see if the tooth grows back; if it does not, then arsh is due. The Tatimma cites an alternative view: for an adult, one only waits until the wound heals, not a full year, because regrowth in adults is rare. The author of al-‘Inaya criticizes the claim of consensus, citing al-Dhakhira where some scholars report a hadith that one waits a year for all wounds, thus contradicting the notion of consensus. The lesson illustrates the Hanafi method of reasoning by analogy and the importance of evidence (naql and ‘aql) in resolving fiqhi differences.

Key Terms
أرش (arsh): Monetary compensation for bodily injury, paid by the perpetrator.
سن (sinn): Tooth.
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of scholars; here claimed but disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It remains due in full.
B) It is dropped.
C) It is reduced by half.
D) It is deferred for a year.

Key Takeaway
When a tooth grows back after extraction, compensation is dropped according to Abu Hanifa, and the mufta bihi supports a waiting period and conditional dropping for adults.

Tooth Regrowth After Qisas: When Diyah Becomes Due
Ruling with proof via istihsan and procedural details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a tooth regrows after qisas, explain the waiting period, and distinguish between the qiyas and istihsan positions on burden of proof.

Core Idea
If a tooth grows back after qisas, the qisas is void and diyah becomes wajib.

This lesson examines a subtle case in qisas (retaliation) for bodily injury. The Hanafi school holds that qisas is based on the permanence of injury; if the tooth regrows, the justification for qisas disappears. The passage also clarifies the procedural rule of waiting one year and explores a conflict between qiyas and istihsan on who bears the burden of proof when the effect of a blow is disputed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Locate the main legal statement: after qisas is executed on the aggressor's tooth, if the victim's tooth grows back, the one who had qisas executed must pay diyah (compensation) to the aggressor. The hukm level is wajib.
The ruling is based on istihsan, not strict analogy.
2
Understand the rationale
The basis for qisas is the permanent corruption of the tooth root. If the tooth regrows, the corruption is undone, so the qisas was executed without right. The diyah restores the balance.
This is a unique case where a completed capital punishment is reversed due to subsequent events.
3
Analyze the waiting procedure
The text states that one waits a full year to determine if the tooth will grow back. If it does not, qisas stands; if it does, diyah is due. This period is established to avoid wasting rights while ensuring fairness.
The year is based on the normal regrowth period for teeth.
4
Distinguish qiyas from istihsan on burden of proof
When a tooth is struck and becomes loose or blackened, the passage contrasts two approaches: by qiyas, the burden of proof is on the victim (the struck person) because the effect does not necessarily follow from the act; by istihsan, the burden is on the aggressor because causation is attributed to the apparent cause. The Hanafi school prefers istihsan.
This illustrates the Hanafi method of preferring istihsan over strict qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (وإن أقيد فنبتت سن الأول تجب الدية معناه إذا قلع سن رجل فأقيد أي اقتص من القالع ثم نبت سن الأول المقتص له يجب على المقتص له أرش سن المقتص منه لأنه تبين أنه استوفى بغير حق لأن الموجب فساد المنبت ولم يفسد حيث نبت مكانها أخرى فانعدمت الجناية ولهذا يستأني حولاً. وينبغي أن ينظر الناس في ذلك القصاص خوفاً من مثله إلا أن في اعتبار ذلك تصييع الحقوق فاكتفينا بالحول لأنه ينبت فيه ظاهراً على تقدير عدم الفساد، فإذا مضى الحول ولم تنبت فيه قضينا بالقصاص، ثم إذا تبين أنا أخطأنا فيه كان الاستيفاء بغير حق إلا أن القصاص سقط للشبهة فيجب المال. ولو ضرب سن إنسان فتحركت يستاني حولاً ليظهر فعله، فإن سقطت سنة واختلفا قبل الحول فالقول للمضروب لتيقن التأجيل بخلاف ما لو شجه موضحة ثم جاء وقد صارت منقلة حيث يكون القول للضارب لأن الموضحة لا تورث المنقلة والتحريك يورث السقوط. ولو اختلفا بعد القول كان القول للضارب لأنه منكر وقصد مضى الأجل الذي ضرب للثاني، ولو لم يسقط فلا شيء للضارب، وإن اختلفا في حصول الاسوداد بضربه فالقول قول الضارب قياساً لأنه . هو المنكر ولا يلزم من الضرب الاسوداد فصار إنكاره له كإنكاره أصل الفعل. وفي الاستحسان القول قول المضروب لأن ما يظهر عقيب فعل من الأثر يحال على الفعل لأنه هو السبب الظاهر إلا
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if qisas is executed and the first person's tooth grows back, the diyah is due). Meaning: If a man's tooth is extracted, and then qisas is executed (i.e., the extractor's tooth is extracted as retaliation), then the first person's tooth (the victim's) grows back, then the one who had qisas executed for him must pay the arsh of the tooth of the one from whom qisas was taken, because it becomes clear that he took retaliation without right, since the cause was the corruption of the root, and it was not corrupted because another grew in its place, so the injury is negated. For this reason, one waits a year. And people should consider this qisas for fear of a similar situation, but if we consider that, rights would be wasted, so we suffice with the year because it normally grows within it assuming no corruption. If the year passes and it does not grow, we rule for qisas. Then if it becomes clear that we erred, the execution was without right, but qisas is dropped due to the doubt, so wealth is due. And if he strikes a person's tooth and it becomes loose, one waits a year to see its outcome. If the tooth falls out and they differ before the year, the statement is of the struck person due to certainty of deferment, unlike if he wounds him with a clear wound and then it becomes a shifting wound, where the statement is of the striker because the clear wound does not cause a shifting wound, while loosening causes falling. And if they differ after the statement, the statement is of the striker because he is the denier and the term he set has passed. And if it does not fall, nothing is due from the striker. And if they differ regarding the blackening caused by his strike, by qiyas the statement is of the striker because he is the denier, and blackening does not necessarily follow from striking, so his denial of it is like his denial of the original act. But by istihsan, the statement is of the struck person because what appears as a trace after an act is attributed to the act, as it is the apparent cause, except...
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling when qisas (retaliation) has been executed by extracting a tooth, but then the victim's original tooth grows back. In that case, the victim (who had qisas executed for him) must pay diyah (compensation) to the one who suffered qisas, because the basis for qisas—the permanent loss of the tooth—is negated by regrowth. The text then discusses the procedure: one waits a year to see if the tooth grows back; if it does, qisas was unjustified and diyah is due; if not, qisas stands. Further cases are addressed: if a tooth is struck and becomes loose, one waits a year; differences of opinion on who bears the burden of proof are resolved by distinguishing between qiyas and istihsan. This lesson highlights the Hanafi reliance on istihsan where strict qiyas would lead to hardship.

Key Terms
أقيد (uqida): Qisas was executed (retaliation in kind).
دية (diyah): Blood money; compensation for homicide or injury.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from strict analogy for a better outcome.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If after executing qisas (tooth extraction) the victim's tooth grows back, what is the ruling?
A) The qisas is valid; no further action.
B) The one who had qisas executed must pay diyah to the other.
C) The qisas is reversed; the original aggressor must pay double.
D) The matter is dropped entirely.

Key Takeaway
If a tooth grows back after qisas, the qisas is considered unjustified and diyah becomes wajib.

Wound Healing Without Trace: No Compensation According to Abu Hanifa
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation when wound heals without trace

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on compensation for a wound that heals without trace and explain the basis for Abu Hanifa's ruling of no compensation.

Core Idea
When a wound heals without trace, no compensation is due because the cause (disfigurement) has ceased — mere pain does not create liability.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute on whether compensation (arsh) is owed for an injury that heals completely without leaving a blemish. Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani each hold distinct views, and the debate hinges on what exactly obligates compensation — the disfigurement itself, the pain inflicted, or the trace of the act. Understanding their reasoning clarifies the Hanafi framework for tort liability.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the issue
Identify the fact pattern: a wound that heals without leaving any trace. The legal question is whether compensation (arsh) is due.
Clear understanding of the trigger for the dispute.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling and reasoning
Note that according to Abu Hanifa, no compensation is required. His reasoning: the obligating factor (shayn/displacement) has vanished; benefits are compensable only by contract; pain alone does not obligate anything.
He uses analogy: a painful blow without wound yields no arsh.
3
Identify Abu Yusuf's ruling and reasoning
Abu Yusuf argues for compensation for pain (arsh al-alam) via fair assessment (hukumat 'adl), because the pain remains even after the wound heals.
His view focuses on the persistent harm of pain.
4
Identify Muhammad's ruling and reasoning
Muhammad requires the doctor's fee (ujrat al-tabib) as a trace of the act. The cost of treatment is a tangible consequence.
His view focuses on the financial loss incurred.
5
Reconcile and note the thamarah al-khilaf
Sharh al-Tahawi reconciles Abu Yusuf and Muhammad by interpreting AY's 'arsh al-alam' as the doctor's fee. The practical difference: Abu Hanifa gives nothing; the Sahibayn give something (either pain compensation or medical costs).
This shows how later scholars harmonized differing positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وإن شج رجلاً فالتحم ولم يبق له أثر أو ضرب فجرح فبرأ وذهب أثره فلا أرش) وهذا قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله. وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله : عليه أرش الألم وهو حكومة عدل لأن الشين الموجب إن زال فالألم الحاصل لم يزل. وقال محمد رحمه الله : عليه أجرة الطبيب لأن ذلك أثر فعله فكان له أخذ ذلك واعطاؤه الطبيب، وفي شرح الطحاوي فسر قول أبي يوسف عليه أرش الألم بأجرة الطبيب والمداواة فعلى هذا الاختلاف بين أبي يوسف ومحمد ولأبي حنيفة رحمه الله أن الموجب هو الشين الذي يلحقه بفعله وزوال منفعته وقد زال ذلك بزوال أثره والمنافع لا تتقوم إلا بالعقد ذلك كالإجارة والمضاربة الصحيحين أو ما يشبه العقد كالفاسد منهما ولم يوجد شيء من في حق الجاني فلا يلزم الغرامة، وكذلك مجرد الألم لا يوجب شيئاً لأنه لا قيمة له بمجرد الألم ألا ترى أن من ضرب إنساناً ضرباً مؤلماً من غير جرح لا يجب عليه شيء من الأرش، وكذا لأن لو شتمه شتماً يؤلم نفسه لا يضمن شيئاً.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he wounds a man and it heals and no trace remains, or he strikes and causes a wound and it heals and its trace disappears, then no compensation). This is the statement of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, said: He owes compensation for the pain, which is a fair assessment (hukumat 'adl), because the disfigurement that obligated it has gone, but the pain that occurred has not disappeared. Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said: He owes the doctor's fee, because that is a trace of his act, so he should take that and give it to the doctor. And in Sharh al-Tahawi, the statement of Abu Yusuf (compensation for pain) is interpreted as the doctor's fee and medication, so on this basis there is no difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Abu Hanifa's argument is that what obligates is the disfigurement (shayn) that he caused and the loss of benefit, and that has vanished with the disappearance of its trace. Benefits are not compensated except by contract, like valid ijara and mudaraba, or what resembles a contract like their invalid forms. None of that exists in the case of the offender, so no liability is incurred. Likewise, mere pain does not obligate anything because it has no value in itself; do you not see that if someone strikes a person a painful blow without a wound, nothing is owed in compensation, and similarly if he insults him with a painful insult, he does not guarantee anything.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning compensation (arsh) when a wound heals completely without leaving any trace. The matn states the ruling of Abu Hanifa: no arsh is due. Abu Yusuf argues that compensation for the pain (arsh al-alam) is still due, as the pain is a distinct harm. Muhammad argues for the doctor's fee (ujrat al-tabib) as the trace of the act. However, Sharh al-Tahawi reconciles their views by interpreting Abu Yusuf's compensation as the doctor's fee. Abu Hanifa's argument is that the sole basis for compensation is the disfigurement (shayn) and loss of benefit, which no longer exist. Benefits are only compensable through contracts, not through tort. Mere pain or insult does not create liability. This reflects the Hanafi principle that tort liability arises from property damage or bodily loss, not from intangible harm like pain alone.

Key Terms
شين (shayn): Disfigurement or blemish; the harm that necessitates compensation.
حكومة عدل (hukumat 'adl): Fair assessment of compensation by expert estimation.
أرش الألم (arsh al-alam): Compensation for pain and suffering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a wound heals without leaving a trace, what compensation is due?
A) Full arsh for the injury.
B) Compensation for pain (arsh al-alam).
C) No compensation.
D) Doctor's fee only.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa holds that when a wound heals without trace, no compensation is due because the cause of liability (disfigurement) no longer exists, and mere pain does not create tort liability in Hanafi law.

Delaying Qisas for Wounds: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on timing of qisas for wounds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school delays qisas for wounds and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using textual and rational evidence.

Core Idea
Qisas for a wound is delayed until healing because the wound may become fatal, changing the case to homicide.

In this lesson, we examine a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the timing of qisas (retaliation) for wounds. The Hanafi position, based on a direct prophetic prohibition, delays qisas until the wound heals. The Shafi'i school argues for immediate execution by analogy to homicide. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how textual evidence (naql) and rational consideration (sarayan) interact in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that qisas for a wound is not executed until the wound heals completely.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that qisas should be executed immediately because the cause is established, analogous to qisas for homicide.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is qiyas: just as in homicide the cause (death) triggers immediate qisas, so in wounds the cause (injury) triggers immediate qisas.
Qiyas is a valid source in usul al-fiqh, but it yields to explicit texts.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: (a) a direct hadith forbids immediate qisas, overriding qiyas; (b) wounds may spread (sarayan) and become fatal, so delay is necessary to ascertain the true nature.
The hadith is a sahih prohibition, so qiyas is not applicable.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in Hanafi school, the victim must wait until healing before qisas can be executed; in Shafi'i school, qisas is carried out immediately after the wound is inflicted and liability established.
This affects both timing and possible transformation to homicide.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا قود بجرح حتى يبرأ) وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : يقتص منه في الحال لأن الموجب قد تحقق فلا يؤخر كما في القصاص في النفس ولنا ما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام نهى أن يقتص من جرح حتى يبرأ صاحبه . رواه أحمد والدارقطني. ولأن الجراحات يعتبر فيها مآلهما لاحتمال أن تسري إلى النفس فيظهر أنه قتل فلا يعلم أنه جرح إلا بالبرء فيستقر به
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And no qisas for a wound until it heals). Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Qisas is executed immediately because the cause has been established and should not be delayed, like in qisas for life. Our evidence is what is narrated that he, peace be upon him, forbade that qisas be executed for a wound until its owner heals. Ahmad and al-Daraqutni narrated it. And because wounds are considered for their ultimate outcome due to the possibility that they may spread to the soul, so it becomes apparent that it was a killing, and it is not known that it was merely a wound until healing, by which it is established.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage addresses the timing of qisas for wounds. The matn states the Hanafi ruling: qisas for a wound is not executed until the wound heals. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that qisas should be immediate, just as in homicide. The Hanafi proof is a hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade executing qisas for a wound until the victim heals. The rational argument is that wounds may become fatal (sariya), turning the injury into murder; until healing, it is uncertain whether it is a wound or homicide. Thus, delay is necessary to determine the true nature of the injury. The Hanafi school prioritizes caution and the likelihood of spread (sarayan) over immediate retaliation.

Key Terms
قود (qawad): Qisas; retaliation in kind for injury or homicide.
يبرأ (yabra'u): Heals completely; the wound is fully recovered.
سراية (sarayan): Spreading of infection or wound to the rest of the body, potentially causing death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school delay qisas for a wound until it heals?
A) Because the victim may forgive.
B) Because the wound might become fatal (sarayan), changing the case to homicide.
C) Because qisas is not allowed for wounds.
D) Because the perpetrator may repent.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, qisas for wounds is delayed until healing due to the prophetic prohibition and the risk of the wound becoming fatal.

Diyah When Qisas is Dropped Due to Shubha: Not Borne by 'Aqila
Ruling on diyah in cases of shubha, sulh, iqrar, and low amounts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who bears diyah when qisas is dropped due to shubha, sulh, iqrar, or low amount, and explain the evidence and the cross-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i.

Core Idea
When qisas is dropped due to shubha, diyah is on the killer's wealth, not the 'aqila; the 'aqila only bears in accidental killing.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains that in cases where intentional killing does not result in qisas due to a legal doubt (shubha), such as a father killing his son, the diyah is payable by the killer himself, not by his 'aqila. The same applies to settlements by sulh, confessions (iqrar), and when the amount is less than half a tenth of the full diyah. The author provides the hadith evidence and rational arguments, then refutes the Shafi'i position that the diyah should be immediate. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly assigning liability in homicide cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four cases
List the four scenarios where diyah is on the killer's wealth: (1) intentional killing where qisas is dropped due to shubha (e.g., father-son), (2) settlement by sulh, (3) confession (iqrar), (4) diyah less than half a tenth.
These are exceptions to the general rule that 'aqila bears diyah in accidental killing.
2
Analyze the dalil
Examine the hadith from Ibn 'Abbas (marfu' and mawquf): 'The 'aqila does not bear for intentional killing, nor for a slave, nor for sulh, nor for iqrar.' This directly supports the ruling.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but accepted in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the rationale for each case
Why does 'aqila not bear? For 'amd: 'aqila is a concession for the excused (khati'), not for the intentional. For sulh: it is a contractual obligation, not from killing. For iqrar: the killer has authority over himself, not his 'aqila. For low amounts: no need for deferment to avoid hardship.
Each rationale is based on the nature of the obligation.
4
Clarify the deferment periods
Generally, diyah is deferred over three years. Exception: sulh is immediate (obligation by contract). Arsh of mudihah (if less than one-third of diyah) is due in one year.
Deferment is a precaution against ruining the killer.
5
Examine the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that diyah for a father killing his son is immediate, because qisas was dropped in exchange for a substitute, which should be immediate like other damages. Hanafi response: life is not property (mal), so qiyas on property fails; the shari'ah specified deferment.
The practical difference: Hanafi pay over 3 years, Shafi'i pay lump sum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وكل عمد سقط فيه قوده لشبهة كقتل الأب ابنه عمداً ففيه دية في مال القاتل وكذا ما صلحاً أو اعترافاً أو لم يكن نصف العشر) أي نصف عشر الدية لما روي عن ابن عباس موقوفاً ومرفوعاً لا تعقل العاقلة عمداً ولا عبداً ولا صلحاً ولا اعترافاً ولأن العاقلة تتحمل عن القاتل تخفيفاً . وذلك يليق بالمخطئ لأنه معذور دون المتعمد لأنه يوجب التغليظ والذي وجب بالصلح إنما وجب بعقده والعاقلة لا تتحمل ما يجب العقد وإنما تتحمل ما يجب بالقتل، وكذا ما لزمه بالإقرار لا تتحمله العاقلة لأن له ولاية على نفسه دون عاقلته فيلزمه دونهم. وإنما لا تتحمل أقل من نصف عشر الدية لأنه لا يؤدي إلى الإجحاف والاستئصال بالجاني والتأجيل تحرزاً عنه فلا حاجة إليه، ثم الكل يجب مؤجلاً إلى ثلاث سنين إلا ما وجب بالصلح فإنه يجب حالاً لأنه واجب بالعقد فيكون حالاً بخلاف غيره وما دونه أرش الموضحة يجب في سنة لا ما دون ثلث الدية والثلث وما دونه يجب في سنة. وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : ما وجب بقتل الأب ابنه حالاً لأن القصاص سقط شرعاً إلى بدل فيكون ذلك البدل حالاً كسائر المتلفات. ولنا أن المتلف ليس بمال وما ليس بمال لا يضمن بالمال أصلاً لأنه ليس بقيمة إذ لا تقوم مقامه وقيمة الشيء ما يقوم مقامه، وإنما عرفنا تقومه بالمال بالشرع والشرع إنما قومه بدية مؤجلة يجب عنه.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And every intentional act whose qisas is dropped due to a shubha, like a father killing his son intentionally, then the diyah is in the wealth of the killer, and likewise [for] what is [settled] by sulh or iqrar, or if it is not half of a tenth). That is, half of a tenth of the diyah, due to what is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas, both as a mawquf and marfu' hadith: 'The 'aqila does not bear [responsibility for] intentional killing, nor for a slave, nor for sulh, nor for iqrar.' And because the 'aqila bears for the killer as a concession; that is appropriate for the mistaken (khati') because he is excused, as opposed to the intentional (mut'amid) because it requires severity. And what becomes obligatory by sulh only becomes obligatory by contract, and the 'aqila does not bear what is obligatory by contract; they only bear what is obligatory by killing. Likewise, what is necessitated by iqrar (confession) the 'aqila does not bear, because he has authority over himself but not over his 'aqila, so it is binding on him, not them. And they do not bear less than half of a tenth of the diyah because it does not lead to oppression and ruin of the offender, and deferment is a precaution against that, so there is no need for it. Then everything is deferred for three years, except what becomes obligatory by sulh, which is immediate because it is obligatory by contract, so it is immediate unlike others. And what is less than that, the arsh of al-mudihah (a wound that lays bare the bone) is due in one year, not less than a third of the diyah, and a third and what is less is due in one year. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: What is obligated by a father killing his son is immediate, because qisas was dropped by law in exchange for a substitute, so that substitute is immediate like other damages. Our evidence is that the damaged thing (life) is not property, and what is not property is not guaranteed by property at all, because it is not a price since it does not stand in its place; the value (taqwim) of something is what stands in its place. We only know its valuation by property from the shari'ah, and the shari'ah valued it as a deferred diyah that must be paid [over three years].
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage elucidates the rules regarding diyah when qisas is not applied due to a legal doubt (shubha), such as a father killing his son. In such cases, diyah is obligatory upon the killer's personal wealth, not upon the 'aqila (tribal surety). The same applies to cases settled by sulh (compromise) or iqrar (confession), or where the amount is less than half of a tenth (i.e., minimal). The proof is a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas stating that the 'aqila does not bear responsibility for 'amd, 'abd, sulh, or iqrar. The rationale: the 'aqila's liability is a concession for the mistaken (khati') because they are excused, and it does not apply in intentional cases which warrant severity. Sulh is a contract, and the 'aqila does not bear contractual obligations. Iqrar (confession) binds only the confessor, not his 'aqila. The payment period: generally three years, except for sulh (immediate) and for arsh of mudihah (one year, if less than one-third of diyah). The passage concludes with a rebuttal of Shafi'i's view that diyah for father killing son should be immediate, because the life is not property and the shari'ah has made it deferred.

Key Terms
العاقلة (al-'aqila): The male paternal relatives (asaba) of the killer who bear diyah in cases of accidental killing.
الصلح (al-sulh): Compromise settlement between the parties, resulting in a contractual obligation.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Confession by the accused, which binds only himself.
شبهة (shubha): A legal doubt that prevents qisas, e.g., father killing son due to mistaken belief of discipline.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, diyah in a case where a father kills his son intentionally (but qisas is dropped due to shubha) is paid by whom and over what period?
A) The 'aqila, immediately.
B) The killer's wealth, immediately.
C) The killer's wealth, deferred over three years.
D) The state treasury, over one year.

Key Takeaway
When qisas is dropped due to shubha, diyah is on the killer's wealth, not the 'aqila, and is generally deferred over three years.

The Ghurrah for a Miscarried Fetus: Proof and Reasoning
Ruling on ghurrah with istihsan based on hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the ghurrah for a dead fetus, identify the hadith proof, and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
Causing miscarriage of a dead fetus incurs a ghurrah of 500 dirhams on the 'āqilah, based on a Prophetic judgment, not analogy.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on compensation for causing a pregnant woman to miscarry a dead fetus. The passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq first clarifies the legal status of the fetus (janīn) – it has limited capacity for rights but not obligations – then states the essential ruling: a ghurrah (half a tenth of the diyah of a man) is wajib upon the 'āqilah. The author presents the qiyas (analogy) that would suggest no compensation or full diyah, but then establishes istihsan (juristic preference) based on the authentic hadith of the woman from Hudhayl, which sets the amount at 500 dirhams. Understanding this interplay between qiyas and istihsan is key to mastering Hanafi legal methodology in injury cases.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Fetus's Legal Status
The passage explains that the fetus has a limited dhimma: it can receive rights (inheritance, bequest) but does not bear obligations until birth. This sets the stage for why miscarriage compensation is special.
The fetus is not a full independent person, but its life is protected.
2
State the Ruling and Its Amount
The ruling: if a woman's belly is struck and she miscarries a dead fetus, a ghurrah is wajib upon the 'āqilah. The ghurrah is half a tenth of the diyah of a man (500 dirhams) – equal for a male or female fetus because the fraction is relative.
The amount is fixed regardless of the fetus's sex, as both fractions yield 500 dirhams.
3
Analyze the Qiyas Arguments
Two analogies are considered: (1) qiyas suggests nothing is due because no injury to a living person is verified; (2) alternatively, full diyah could be due since the striker prevented life. Both are rejected in favor of the Prophetic ruling.
The first qiyas compares to a miscarried animal fetus; the second compares to killing a living person.
4
Apply Istihsan via the Hadith
Istihsan is based on the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged a ghurrah (slave worth 500 dirhams) for the dead fetus. This specific ruling overrides the general analogies, establishing the precise amount.
The hadith is a sunnah ahad, so it is zanni in transmission and meaning, but sufficient for istihsan.
5
Note Practical Applications and Scenarios
The passage includes complex scenarios (live then dead fetus, intentional sword strike) to show how the ghurrah interacts with diyah and qisas. The ruling applies to free women, Muslim or not.
The 'āqilah (paternal clan) bears the ghurrah, not the striker, except in intentional cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الجنين
لما ذكر أحكام الجناية المتعلقة بالآدمي شرع في بيان أحكامها المعلقة بالآدمي من وجه دون وجه وهو الجنين بيان ذلك ما ذكر شمس الأئمة السرخسي في أصوله أن الجنين ما دام مجتناً في البطن ليس له ذمة صالحة لكونه في حكم جزء من الأم لكنه منفرد بالحياة بعد إلا أن يكون نفساً له ذمة فباعتبار هذا الوجه يكون أهلاً لوجوب الحق له من عتق أو إرث أو نسب أو وصية، وباعتبار الوجه الأول لا يكون أهلاً لوجوب الحق عليه فأما بعدما يولد فله ذمة صالحة، ولهذا لو انقلب على مال إنسان أتلفه يكون ضامناً له ويلزمه مهر امرأته بعقد الولي. جنين على وزن فعيل بمعنى مفعول وهي مجنون أي مستور من جنه إذا ستره من باب طلب، والجنين اسم للولد في بطن أمه ما دام فيه والجمع أجنة فإذا ولد يسمى وليداً ثم رضيعاً إلى غير ذلك. قال رحمه الله : (ضرب بطن امرأة فالقت جنيناً ميتاً تجب غرة نصف عشر الدية) الغرة الخيار، غرة المال خياره كالفرس والبعير البخت والعبد والأمة ألفا درهم، وقيل إنما سمي ما يجب في الجنين غرة لأنه أول مقدار ظهر في باب الدية وغرة الشيء أوله كما أول الشهر غرة، سمي وسمي وجه الإنسان غرة لأنه أول شيء يظهر منه . والمراد بنصف عشر الدية دية الرجل لو كان الجنين ذكراً وفي الأنثى دية عشر المرأة وكل منهما خمسمائة درهم ولهذا لم يبين في المختصر أنه ذكر أو أنثى لأن دية المرأة نصف دية الرجل بالعشر في ديتها قدر نصف العشر من دية الرجل. والقياس أن لا يجب شيء من الجنين لأنه لم يتحقق جناية، الظاهر لا يصلح حجة للاستحقاق ولهذا لا يجب في جنين البهيمة الإنقصان الأم إن نقصت وإلا فلا يجب شيء، والقياس أن لا يجب كمال الدية لأنه بضربه منع حدوث الحياة فيه فيكون بذلك كالمزهق للروح ولهذا المعنى وجبت قيمة ولد المغرور فإنه منع من حدوث الرق فيه، وكذلك وجب على المحرم قيمة بيض الصيد في كسره وجه الاستحسان ما روي أن امرأة من هذيل ضربت بطن امرأة بحجر فقتلتها وما في بطنها فاختصموا إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقضى أن دية جنينها غرة عبد أو أمة قيمته خمسمائة ؛ كذا وجدته بخط شيخي. وفي المنتقى : رجل ضرب بطن امرأته فألقت جنيناً حياً ثم مات ثم ألقت جنيناً ميتاً ثم ماتت الأم بعد ذلك وللرجل الضارب بنت من غير هذه المرأة وليس له ولد من هذه التي ولدت ولها إخوة من أبيها وأمها فعلى عاقلة الأب دية الولد الذي وقع حياً ثم مات ترث من ذلك أمه السدس وما بقي فلأخت هذا الولد من أبيه وعلى والده كفارتان في الولد الواقع حياً وكفارة في أمه والولد الذي سقط ميتاً ففيه غرة على عاقلة الأب خمسمائة ويكون للأم من ذلك السدس أيضاً وما بقي فلأخت هذا الولد أبيه أيضاً، من فلو كان الرجل ضرب بطنها بالسيف عمداً فقطع البطن ووقع أحد الولدين حياً وبه جراحة السيف ثم مات ووقع الآخر ميتاً وبه جراحة السيف أيضاً ثم ماتت الأم من ذلك فعلى الرجل القود في الأم وعلى عاقلته دية الولد الحي وغرة الجنين الميت. قال محمد في الجامع الصغير : وأطلق في قوله امرأة قال في السراجية : فشمل الحرة مسلمة كانت أو كافرة ويكملون بدل الجنين
Chapter on the Fetus
When he mentioned the rulings on injury related to the human being, he began explaining its rulings that are attached to the human being from one aspect and not from another, namely the fetus. The explanation of that is what Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned in his Usul: that the fetus as long as it is hidden in the womb does not have a valid dhimma because it is in the status of a part of the mother, but it is distinguished with life afterwards, except that it is a soul that has a dhimma. So by this aspect, it is eligible for the obligation of a right in its favor such as emancipation, inheritance, lineage, or bequest. And by the first aspect, it is not eligible for the obligation of a right against it. But after it is born, it has a valid dhimma. For this reason, if it turns over and destroys someone's property, it is responsible for it, and the mahr of his wife is binding upon him through the guardian's contract. "Janīn" is on the pattern of fa'īl in the sense of maf'ūl (passive particle), meaning "concealed" from "jannah" if he conceals it. And "janīn" is the name for the child in its mother's womb as long as it is there, and the plural is "ajinnah". When it is born, it is called "walīd", then "raḍīʿ", etc. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: "If a woman's belly is struck and she miscarries a dead fetus, then a ghurrah is obligatory: half a tenth of the diyah." The ghurrah is the best (choice). The best of property is its best, like a horse, a Bactrian camel, a slave, a slave girl, two thousand dirhams? It is said that what is obligatory for the fetus is called ghurrah because it is the first amount that appeared in the chapter of diyah, and the first of something is its beginning, just as the first of the month is ghurrah, and the face of a person is called ghurrah because it is the first thing that appears from him. And what is meant by half a tenth of the diyah is the diyah of a man if the fetus is male, and for a female, a tenth of the diyah of a woman. And each of them is five hundred dirhams. For this reason, it is not specified in al-Mukhtasar whether it is male or female, because the diyah of a woman is half the diyah of a man, and by the tenth in her diyah the amount is half a tenth of the diyah of a man. The qiyas would dictate that nothing is obligatory for the fetus because no injury is verified. The apparent [situation] is not suitable as a proof for entitlement. For this reason, for the fetus of an animal, if the mother is diminished, then [it is considered], otherwise nothing is obligatory. And qiyas would dictate that the full diyah is not obligatory because by striking he prevented the occurrence of life in it, so he is like the extinguisher of the spirit. For this meaning, the value of the child of the deceived (al-maghrūr) is obligatory, because he prevented the occurrence of slavery in it. Likewise, the value of the eggs of game is obligatory on the pilgrim if he breaks them. The basis of istihsan is what has been narrated: "A woman from Hudhayl struck the belly of a woman with a stone, thus killing her and what was in her belly. They brought the case to the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him), and he judged that the diyah of her fetus is a ghurrah: a male or female slave whose value is five hundred." I found it thus in the handwriting of my teacher. And in al-Muntaqā: A man struck his wife's belly, and she miscarried a live fetus that then died, then she miscarried a dead fetus, then the mother died afterwards. And the man had a daughter from another woman, and he had no child from this woman who gave birth, and she [the mother] has brothers from her father and her mother. Then upon the 'āqilah of the father is the diyah of the child who was born alive and then died; the mother inherits a sixth from that, and the remainder is for the sister of this child from his father. And upon the father are two kaffārahs for the child born alive, and one kaffārah for the mother. And for the child who miscarried dead, there is a ghurrah upon the 'āqilah of the father of five hundred dirhams. And the mother also gets a sixth from that, and the remainder is for the sister of this child from his father. Then: So if the man struck her belly with a sword intentionally and cut the belly, and one of the two twins came out alive and had the wound of the sword, then died, and the other came out dead with the wound of the sword also, then the mother died from that, then upon the man is qisas for the mother, and upon his 'āqilah is the diyah of the live child and the ghurrah of the dead fetus. Muhammad said in al-Jāmi' al-Ṣaghīr: and he said generally "a woman" in his statement; said in al-Sirājiyyah: so it includes a free woman, whether Muslim or disbeliever, and they complete instead of the fetus.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rulings regarding the fetus. It begins with the legal capacity (dhimma) of the fetus: not fully capable but eligible for rights. Then it states the ruling: if a pregnant woman is struck and miscarries a dead fetus, a ghurrah is due, which is half a tenth of the diyah of a man (500 dirhams). The author provides the linguistic definition of ghurrah and then discusses the qiyas (analogy) that would dictate no compensation or full diyah, but istihsan (juristic preference) based on the hadith from the woman of Hudhayl establishes the ghurrah. The passage then presents a complex case from al-Muntaqā involving multiple deaths and inheritance distribution, as well as a case of intentional striking with a sword leading to qisas for the mother and diyah/ghurrah for the children. The final note from al-Jāmi' al-Ṣaghīr indicates that the ruling applies to free women, regardless of religion.

Key Terms
جنين (janīn): The child while it is still in its mother's womb, hidden.
غرة (ghurrah): The best of property, set at 500 dirhams as compensation for a miscarried dead fetus.
دية (diyah): Blood money; financial compensation for killing or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the amount of ghurrah for a miscarried dead fetus according to the Hanafi school?
A) Full diyah of a man (10,000 dirhams).
B) Half a tenth of the diyah of a man (500 dirhams).
C) Full diyah of a woman (5,000 dirhams).
D) Nothing.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school fixes the ghurrah for a dead fetus at 500 dirhams based on a Prophetic hadith, overriding analogical reasoning.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate

Diya and Ghurrah for Struck Pregnant Woman
Rulings with proof and dispute on diya/ghurrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diya and ghurrah in three scenarios (mother survives, mother dies first, fetus born alive), explain the proof from hadith and qiyas, and evaluate the dispute with al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
A fetus's compensation depends on the mother's survival; if she dies first, only her diya is due because the fetus's death is attributed to hers.

The Book of Diyat deals with financial compensation for wrongful death and injury. A particularly intricate case arises when a pregnant woman is struck, and the fetus and/or mother die. The ruling depends on the sequence of events and whether the fetus showed signs of life. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on these scenarios, the underlying proof, and a key difference with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
Read the passage and list the three basic scenarios: (1) mother dies and fetus found dead after her death, (2) fetus miscarried dead while mother is alive then mother dies, (3) fetus born alive then dies.
Focus on the sequence of death.
2
Understand the proof
The text cites a narrated hadith (lama rawayna) establishing ghurrah for a miscarried fetus. Also, the principle that the act is multiplied by multiplicity of effect (if one shot kills two persons, two diyas).
The hadith is ahad, making the ruling based on zanni evidence.
3
Analyze the dispute with al-Shafi'i
Al-Shafi'i argues that when the mother dies first and the fetus is found dead, ghurrah is also due because the strike apparently caused the fetus's death. The Hanafi response: the mother's death is the apparent cause (fetus's life dependent on hers), so only one diya is due.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different causal attribution.
4
Apply inheritance and slave rulings
The ghurrah is inherited from the fetus; the striker does not inherit. For a slave-woman's fetus, the compensation is a fraction of the slave's value. Note the conditions from al-Kafi and Sharh al-Tahawi.
Ghurrah is 500 dirhams for a free Muslim fetus.
5
Practice with twin scenarios
Work through the rulings for twins: if both born dead after mother's death, only mother's diya; if born alive then die, two diyas; if one emerges before mother's death (dead) and one after (dead), only one ghurrah for the first.
The inheritance rules depend on which twin is alive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الديات فدية فإن القت ميتاً فماتت الأم فدية وغرة وإن ماتت فالقتة ميتاً فدية فقط وما يجب فيه يورث عنه ولا يرث الضارب فلو ضرب بطن امرأته فألقت ابنه ميتاً فعلى عاقلة الأب غرة ولا يرث منها وفي جنين الأمة لو ذكرا نصف عشر قيمته لو كان حياً وعشر قيمته بين الورثة. وفي الكافي : هذا إذا تبين خلقه أو بعض خلقه. وفي شرح الطحاوي : أو كانت أمة علقت من سيدها والكفارة في الجنين تجب في سنة واحدة وفي شرح الطحاوي: ولو ألقت جنينين تجب غرتان، وإن كان أحدهما خرج حياً ثم مات والآخر خرج ميتاً تجب غرة ودية وعلى الضارب الكفارة، وإن ماتت الأم ثم خرج الجنينان تجب دية الأم وحدها إلا إذا خرج الجنينان ثم ماتا تجب عليه ثلاث ديات فاعتبر على هذا القياس وإن كان في بطنها جنينان فخرج أحدهما قبل موت الأم وخرج الآخر بعد موت الأم وهما ميتان تجب الغرة في الذي خرج قبل موت الأم ولا يرث من دية أمه شيئاً وترث الأم من ديته والجنين الآخر وهو الذي خرج بعد موت أمه لا يرث من أحد ولا يورث عنه قال ; وإن كان الذي خرج بعد موت الأم خرج حياً ثم مات ففيه الدية كاملة. وفي شرح الطحاوي : ولو خرج الولد حياً ثم مات تجب ديتان قال : ويرث هذا الجنين من دية أمه . وهل يرث هذا الجنين الأول وهو الذي خرج ميتاً قبل موت الأم؟ ينظر إن كان الآخر حياً لا يرث . وإن لم يكن حياً يرث . قال رحمه الله : (وإن ألقته حياً فمات فدية) أي تجب دية كاملة لأنه أتلف آدمياً خطأ أو شبه عمد فتجب فيه الدية كاملة . قال رحمه الله : (فإن القت ميتاً فماتت الأم فدية وغرة لما روينا ولأنهما جنايتان فيجب فيهما موجبهما وهذا لما عرف أن الفعل يتعدد بتعدد أثره فصار كما إذا رمى . فأصاب شخصاً ونفذت منه إلى آخر فقتله فإنه يجب عليه ديتان إن كان خطأ وإن كان الأول عمداً يجب القصاص في الأول وفي الثاني الدية قال رحمه الله وإن ماتت فالقتة ميتاً فدية فقط) وقال الشافعي: تجب الغرة مع الدية لأن الجنين مات بضربته ظاهراً فصار كما إذا ألقته ميتاً وهي بالحياة. ولنا أن موت الأم سبب لموته ظاهراً لأن حياته بحياتها وتنفسه بتنفسها فيتحقق بموتها فلا يكون في معنى ما ورد به النص إذا الاحتمال فيه أقل فلا يجب شيء بالشك، وإن ألقته حياً بعدما ماتت تجب ديتان دية الأم ودية الولد لأنه كما إذا ألقته حياً وماتت.
Book of blood money: For a [fetus] she miscarries dead then the mother dies: a blood money and a ghurrah. If she dies and miscarries a dead [fetus]: only a blood money. What is obligatory for it is inherited from him, and the striker does not inherit from it. So if he struck the belly of his wife and she miscarried his son dead, the father's 'aagilah must pay a ghurrah, and he does not inherit from it. For the fetus of a slave-woman, if male: half of a tenth of his value if alive, and a tenth of his value if female. Among the heirs. In al-Kafi: This is if his creation or part of it became apparent. In Sharh al-Tahawi: Or if she is a slave-woman who conceived from her master. The atonement for the fetus is obligatory in one year. In Sharh al-Tahawi: If she miscarries twins, two ghurrahs are obligatory. If one came out alive then died and the other came out dead, a ghurrah and a blood money are obligatory, and the striker must perform atonement. If the mother dies then the two fetuses come out, the mother's blood money alone is obligatory, unless the two fetuses came out and then they die; then three blood monies are obligatory upon him. So examine this by analogy. If she has two fetuses and one came out before the mother's death and the other came out after the mother's death, and they are dead: the ghurrah is obligatory for the one that came out before the mother's death, and he does not inherit anything from his mother's blood money, and the mother inherits from his blood money. The other fetus, which came out after his mother's death, does not inherit from anyone and is not inherited from. He said: If the one that came out after the mother's death came out alive then died, then the full blood money is due. In Sharh al-Tahawi: If the child came out alive then died, two blood monies are obligatory. He said: This fetus inherits from his mother's blood money. Does this first fetus, which came out dead before the mother's death, inherit? It is considered: if the other is alive, he does not inherit; if he is not alive, he inherits. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If she miscarries it alive then it dies: a blood money) meaning a complete blood money is obligatory because he destroyed a human being by mistake or quasi-intentional, so the complete blood money is obligatory. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If she miscarries it dead and the mother dies: a blood money and a ghurrah, because of what we narrated, and because they are two injuries, so their respective obligations must apply. This is because the act is multiplied by the multiplicity of its effect, so it becomes like if he shot and hit a person and it passed through him and hit another and killed him: then two blood monies are obligatory if it was a mistake, and if the first was intentional then retaliation for the first and blood money for the second.) He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If she dies and miscarries a dead [fetus]: only a blood money.) Al-Shafi'i said: The ghurrah is obligatory along with the blood money because the fetus died by his strike apparently, so it becomes like if she miscarried it dead while she was alive. Our evidence: The mother's death is a cause for its death apparently, because its life depends on her life and its breathing depends on her breathing, so it is realized by her death. Thus it is not in the meaning of what the text brought because the probability is less, so nothing is obligatory based on doubt. If she miscarries it alive after she died, two blood monies are obligatory: the mother's blood money and the child's blood money, because it is like if she miscarried it alive and she died.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rulings on compensation (diya and ghurrah) when a pregnant woman is struck and the fetus and/or mother die. It begins with the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and the commentator expands on various scenarios. The passage starts with the general rule: if the fetus is miscarried dead and the mother also dies, both diya (for the mother) and ghurrah (for the fetus) are obligatory. If the mother dies but the fetus is found dead after her death, only the mother's diya is due (no ghurrah). The ghurrah is 500 dirhams. The text then discusses inheritance briefly, stating the fetus's compensation is inherited but the striker does not inherit. It then addresses the fetus of a slave-woman: half a tenth of the slave's value if male, a tenth if female. The commentary from al-Kafi and Sharh al-Tahawi adds details: the ghurrah is only due if the fetus's limbs have formed; if from the master's own slave-woman, the same rules apply; kaffarah is required for killing the fetus; for twins, two ghurrahs are due; if one is born alive then dies, diya is due for that one and ghurrah for the other. If the mother dies first and then the twins emerge, only the mother's diya is due unless the twins emerge alive then die, then three diyas. If one twin emerges before the mother's death (dead) and the other after (dead), the ghurrah is only for the first, and inheritance rules differ. The matn then repeats the basic rulings and the commentator provides the proof: a hadith (marfu') and the principle that the act is multiplied by multiplicity of effect. A dispute with al-Shafi'i follows: he argues that if the mother dies first and the fetus is found dead, both diya and ghurrah are due because the fetus died by the strike. The Hanafi response is that the mother's death is the cause of the fetus's death (since its life depends on hers), so only the mother's diya is due; the ghurrah is not obligatory due to doubt. Finally, if the fetus is born alive after the mother's death, two full diyas are due because both lives were destroyed.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money; financial compensation for homicide or loss of a limb, specified as 1,000 dinars or 10,000 dirhams for a free Muslim.
غرة (ghurrah): A fixed compensation of 500 silver dirhams for a miscarried fetus that dies before birth.
عاقلة (aagilah): The male paternal relatives (asabah) of the offender who collectively pay the diyar in cases of accidental killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a pregnant woman is struck and dies, and the fetus is found dead after her death, what is due?
A) The mother's full diyah only.
B) The mother's full diyah and a ghurrah for the fetus.
C) A ghurrah for the fetus only.
D) Neither compensation, as it was an accident.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the ruling on diya and ghurrah for a struck pregnant woman depends on the sequence of death: if the mother dies first, only her diya is due; if the fetus dies first while she is alive, both are due; if the fetus is born alive then dies, full child diya is due.

Inheritance of the Fetus's Diya and Disqualification of the Striker
States that the compensation for a fetus is inherited, and the striker cannot inherit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the inheritance of the fetus's diya (ghurrah) and explain why the striker is disqualified from inheriting.

Core Idea
The killer cannot inherit from his victim, not even from the diya paid for the victim's life.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school concerning the inheritance of the diya (ghurrah) due for a miscarried fetus. The passage clarifies that the compensation becomes part of the fetus's estate and passes to his heirs, but the person who caused the miscarriage – the striker – is barred from inheriting any portion. This is rooted in the general principle that a killer does not inherit from his victim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the matn carefully: 'Whatever is obligatory for it is inherited from him, and the striker does not inherit.' This means the compensation (ghurrah) becomes part of the fetus's estate and is inherited by his heirs.
2
Understand the legal basis
The commentator explains that the ghurrah is a replacement for the fetus's life (which in a sense was a life). Therefore, it is treated like any property of the deceased and passes to heirs.
The fetus is considered a 'life in a way' (nafsun min wajh) in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Identify the disqualification
The striker (the one who caused the miscarriage) does not inherit any part of the ghurrah. This is because he is classified as a killer (qaatil) who directly caused death wrongfully.
The killer's disqualification from inheritance is a well-established principle in Islamic law.
4
Note the evidence
The text begins to cite a Quranic verse (the full verse is not in the OCR but is likely the inheritance verse that excludes the killer). This shows the ruling is based on divine text.
The principle that a killer does not inherit is derived from the hadith: 'The killer does not inherit.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وما يجب فيه يورث عنه ولا يرث الضارب فلو ضرب بطن امرأته فألقت ابنه ميتاً فعلى عاقلة الأب غرة ولا يرث منها وإنما يورث لأنه نفس من وجه على ما بينا والغرة بدله فيرثها وارثه ولا يرث الضارب من الغرة شيئاً لأنه قاتل مباشرة ظلماً ولا ميراث للقاتل بهذه الصفة قال الله :
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (Whatever is obligatory for it is inherited from him, and the striker does not inherit. So if he struck the belly of his wife and she miscarried his son dead, the father's 'aaqilah must pay a ghurrah, and he does not inherit from it. It is only inherited because it is a life in a way, as we have explained, and the ghurrah is its replacement, so its heir inherits it. The striker does not inherit anything from the ghurrah because he is a killer directly wrongfully, and there is no inheritance for the killer in this manner. Allah said:
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn ruling about the inheritance of the compensation (ghurrah) due for a miscarried fetus. The matn states: 'Whatever is obligatory for it (the fetus) is inherited from him, and the striker does not inherit.' The commentator explains that the ghurrah is inherited by the fetus's legal heirs. Even though the fetus himself is dead, the compensation is treated as his property and passes to his heirs. The striker (the one who caused the miscarriage) is disqualified from inheriting because he is the killer: he directly caused the death wrongfully. This is based on the general principle that a killer does not inherit from his victim. The text then begins to cite a Quranic verse (but the verse is not given in the OCR; likely إِنِ امْرُؤٌ هَلَكَ or the like). The ruling is illustrated with the case of a husband striking his pregnant wife: the father's 'aaqilah must pay the ghurrah, but the father does not inherit from that ghurrah because he is considered the killer (since he caused the miscarriage through his wife).

Key Terms
إرث (irth): Inheritance; the transfer of property from the deceased to his legal heirs.
قاتل (qaatil): The one who directly causes death; here, the striker who causes miscarriage is considered a killer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a man strikes his pregnant wife and she miscarries a dead fetus, who inherits the ghurrah (compensation)?
A) The father, because he pays it.
B) The fetus's maternal relatives.
C) The fetus's heirs, excluding the father.
D) The state treasury (bayt al-mal).

Key Takeaway
The diya for a fetus is inherited by its heirs, but the killer – even if he is the father – is disqualified from inheriting any part of it.

Dispute on the Value of a Slave's Fetus
Hanafi and Shafi'i dispute over compensation for a slave-woman's fetus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on compensation for a slave-woman's fetus, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
The fetus is a separate life; compensation is based on its own potential value, not the mother's.

When a slave-woman's fetus is killed, two views on compensation arise. The Hanafi school holds that the payment is for the fetus's own life, measured by its potential value. Imam al-Shafi'i, viewing it as a part of the mother, would base it on her value. The debate hinges on foundational principles of liability.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: for a male fetus, half a tenth of his value if alive; for female, a tenth of her value.
This appears in the matn as the opening statement.
2
Identify the opponent's view
State that Imam al-Shafi'i argues for a tenth of the mother's value by analogy to free woman's fetus and the ghurrah.
The opponent is not named in the Arabic but is understood as al-Shafi'i.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand that al-Shafi'i treats the fetus as a part; thus compensation is proportional to the mother's whole.
This is based on the principle that parts are compensated by proportion of the whole.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine the two proofs: ijma that no decrease in mother's value is required, and that compensation is inherited – both indicate it is for the self.
Also note the distinction between self and limb compensation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Compare results: Hanafi uses fetus's value, Shafi'i uses mother's value. Practical amounts differ when mother is valuable.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي جنين الأمة لو ذكرا نصف عشر قيمته لو كان حياً وعشر قيمته لو أنثى) وقال الشافعي : يجب فيه عشر قيمة الأم لأنه جزء من وجه وضمان الأجزاء يومئذ بمقدارها من الأصل ولهذا وجب في جنين الحرة عشر ديتها بالإجماع وهو الغرة. لنا أنه بدل نفسه فلا يقدر بغيره إذ لا نظير له في الشرع والدليل على أنه بدل نفسه أن الأمة أجمعت على أنه لا يشترط فيه نقصان الأصل، ولو كان ضمان الطرف لما وجب إلا عند نقصان الأصل. ويؤيد ذلك أن ما يجب في جنين الحرة موروث ولو كان بدل الطرف لما ورث والحر والعبد لا يختلفان في ضمان الطرف لأنه لا يورث وإنما يختلفان في ضمان النفس، لو كان ضمان الطرف لما روث في الحر فإذا ثبت أنه ضمان النفس كان دية مقدرة بنفس الجنين لا بنفس غيره كما في سائر المضمونات ولا نسلم أن الغرة مقدرة بدية الأم بل بدية نفس الجنين إذا لو كان حياً تجب نصف عشر ديته إن كان ذكراً، وعشر ديته إن كان أنثى فكذا في جنين الأمة يجب بتلك النسبة من قيمته لأن كل ما كان بقدر دية الحر فهو مقدر من قيمة العبد فيجب نصف عشر قيمته إن كان ذكراً وعشر قيمته إن كان أنثى. هذا دية الحر إذا كان الجنين من غير مولاها ومن غير مغرور وأما إذا كان من أحدهما ففيه الغرة المذكورة في جنين الحرة ذكراً كان أو أنثى كما تقدم.
For the fetus of a slave-woman: if male, half of a tenth of his value if alive, and a tenth of his value if female. Al-Shafi'i said: A tenth of the mother's value is obligatory because it is a part in a way, and compensation for parts at that time is by their proportion to the whole, and for this reason a tenth of her blood money is obligatory for the fetus of a free woman by consensus, and that is the ghurrah. Our evidence: It is a substitute for the self, so it is not measured by something else since there is no precedent for it in the Sharia. The proof that it is a substitute for the self is that the community agreed that no decrease in the original is required; if it were compensation for a limb, it would only be obligatory when there is decrease in the original. This is supported by the fact that what is obligatory for the fetus of a free woman is inherited; if it were compensation for a limb, it would not be inherited. The free and the slave do not differ in compensation for a limb because it is not inherited, but they differ in compensation for the self. If it were compensation for a limb, it would not be inherited in the free. So when it is established that it is compensation for the self, it is a blood money measured by the self of the fetus, not by the self of another, as in all other compensable items. We do not accept that the ghurrah is measured by the mother's blood money; rather, it is measured by the blood money of the fetus's own self: if he were alive, half a tenth of his blood money would be obligatory if male, and a tenth if female. So likewise for the fetus of a slave-woman, the same proportion of his value is obligatory, because every time something is by the measure of the free person's blood money, it is measured from the slave's value. So half a tenth of his value if male, and a tenth of his value if female. This is for the fetus of a free [woman] when the fetus is not from her master and not from a deceived [person]. If it is from either of them, then the ghurrah mentioned in the case of the free woman's fetus is due, whether male or female, as earlier.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on the compensation due for the fetus of a slave-woman (janeen al-amah) and the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi matn states: if the fetus is male, half a tenth of his value (if he had been alive) is due; if female, a tenth of his value. Al-Shafi'i argues that a tenth of the mother's value is due, analogizing it to compensation for a part of the mother, and citing that for a free woman's fetus, a tenth of her diya (the ghurrah) is due by consensus. The Hanafi response is detailed: the compensation for the fetus is a substitute for its own life (badal nafsih), not a part of the mother. Therefore, it is measured by the fetus's own value. Proof: (1) The community agrees that no decrease in the mother's value is required, which would be the case if it were limb compensation. (2) The compensation is inherited, whereas limb compensation is not inherited. (3) Free and slave differ in compensation for the self but not for limbs. So it must be compensation for the self. Thus, for a free fetus, the amount is based on the diya of a free person (1,000 dinars) — half a tenth (50 dinars) for a male, a tenth (100 dinars) for a female? Wait: The text says for a free male fetus, if alive, half a tenth of his diya; for female, a tenth of her diya. Then for a slave fetus, the same proportion of the slave's market value is applied. The commentary ends by noting an exception: if the fetus is from the mother's master (i.e., the owner) or from a deceived person (maghroor), then the ghurrah of 500 dirhams is due regardless of sex, as in the free woman's case.

Key Terms
جنين الأمة (janeen al-amah): The fetus of a slave-woman; its compensation is based on its own value, not the mother's.
ضمان النفس (daman al-nafs): Compensation for taking a life; the value of the self is replaced.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how is the compensation for a male fetus of a slave-woman calculated?
A) A tenth of the mother's value.
B) Half a tenth of the fetus's value if he were alive.
C) Full blood money (diyah) of a slave.
D) A fixed ghurrah of 500 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the compensation for the fetus of a slave-woman is based on the fetus's own potential value, not a proportion of the mother's value, because it is compensation for a self, not a limb.
