Diyat and Ghurrah for Fetal Death in Hanafi Fiqh
Collection of fatwas on diyat and ghurrah for fetal death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on ghurrah and diyah for fetal death to diverse scenarios, including those involving multiple fetuses, emancipated slaves, and intentional abortion.

Core Idea
The ghurrah (500 dirhams) is the baseline compensation for a dead fetus, but it varies with value, free status, and cause of death.

This lesson presents a collection of fatwas from later Hanafi sources (Nawadir, al-'Uyun, al-Tatimmah, al-Muntaqa, al-Nasafiyyah, al-Hawi, Jami' al-Fatawa) that apply the principles of diyat and ghurrah to intricate cases of miscarriage. These rulings illustrate how basic rules adapt to complex circumstances, such as multiple fetuses, partial emancipation, buyer's options, and self-inflicted abortion. By parsing these fatwas, you will learn the key factors that determine compensation amounts and who is liable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
For each fatwa, determine who caused the miscarriage (criminal), who is the victim (fetus, mother), and any relevant relationships (owner, husband, father).
2
Extract the fetal compensation
Note the exact compensation awarded for each fetus: is it a fixed ghurrah (500 dirhams), a fraction of value, or full diyah? Distinguish between stillbirth and live birth followed by death.
3
Identify additional rulings
Look for related rulings: expiation (kaffarah), liability of 'aaqilah, inheritance rights, and options for buyers or husbands.
4
Generalize the principles
From these specifics, deduce the general Hanafi rules: ghurrah for dead fetus, no kaffarah unless live birth, 'aaqilah pays for accidental killing, and compensation goes to the heir (father or mother's owner).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي نوادر ابن سماعة : رجل قال لأمته الحبلى أحد الولدين اللذين في بطنك حر فضرب إنسان بطنها فألقت جنينين ميتين غلام وجارية قال: على الجاني غرة وذلك خمسمائة وعليه أيضاً في الغلام ربع عشر قيمته لو كان حياً، وعليه في الجارية نصف خمسمائة ونصف عشر قيمتها. وفي العيون هشام عن أبي يوسف في رجل اشترى أمة حاملاً فلم يقبضها حتى أعتق ما في بطنها ثم ضرب إنسان بطنها فألقت غلاماً ميتاً فالمشتري بالخيار إن شاء أخذ الأمة بجميع الثمن واتبع الجاني بأرش الجنين أرش طيباً، وإن شاء فسخ البيع في الأمة ولزمه الولد بحصته من الثمن. ولو كان للجنين أب حر كان أرش الجنين لوالده في الوجهين جميعاً ولا شيء للمشتري. وفي التتمة وسئل يوسف بن محمد البلالي عن رجل زنى بجارية الغير فأحبلها ثم احتال هو وامرأته فأسقطا الحمل من الجارية وماتت الجارية بذلك السبب ما الحكم في ذلك وما يجب عليهما؟ فقال: أما الجارية فإنه يجب عليه ضمانها إذا ماتت بذلك السبب، وفي الحمل الغرة إن كان ميتاً، وإن سقط وهو حي ثم مات فإنه يجب قيمته وإن كان الحمل ماء ودماً فإنه لا يجب فيه شيء. وفي المنتقى قال أبو يوسف : إذا ضرب الرجل بطن امرأته فألقت جنيناً ميتاً فلا كفارة عليه ولا يرث منه، وإن ألقت جنيناً ميتاً قد استبان من خلقه شيء ثم ماتت هي من تلك الضربة ثم ألقت جنيناً حياً ومات ففي الأول الغرة، وفي الأم الدية وفي الجنين الثاني الدية كاملة. وفي النسفية سئل عن مختلعة حامل مضت عدتها بإسقاط الولد هل للزوج أن يخاصمها في هذا الحمل ؟ فقال : إن أسقطته بفعلها وجب عليها للزوج غرة قيمتها خمسمائة . خالصة ولا يسقط شيء من ذلك لميراثها لأنها قاتلة فلا ترث. وسئل أبو القاسم عن امرأة شربت الدواء فألقت جنينها ميتاً أو حملت حملاً ثقيلاً فألقت جنيناً ميتاً أن على عاقلتها خمسمائة درهم في سنة واحدة لوارث الحمل أباً كان أو غيره، وإن لم يكن لها عاقلة فهي في مالها في سنة. وفي الحاوي : وذلك لزوجها لأنه هو الوارث ؛ قاله يوسف بن عيسى. وفي جامع الفتاوى : ولو لم يعلم أنه ذكر أو أنثى يؤخذ بالمتيقن كالخنثى المشكل ضاع الجنين ولا يمكنها درهم نقرة [؟]
From Nawadir Ibn Sama'ah: A man said to his pregnant slave-woman: 'One of the two children in your womb is free.' Then a person struck her belly and she miscarried two dead fetuses, a boy and a girl. He said: the criminal owes a ghurrah, which is five hundred, and also on him for the boy: a quarter of a tenth of his value if alive, and on him for the girl: half of five hundred and half a tenth of her value. From al-'Uyun: Hisham from Abu Yusuf regarding a man who bought a pregnant slave-woman but did not take possession until he emancipated what was in her womb; then a person struck her belly and she miscarried a dead boy. The buyer has the option: if he wishes, he may take the slave-woman for the full price and pursue the criminal for the compensation for the fetus (a favorable compensation), and if he wishes, he may rescind the sale of the slave-woman and the child is binding on him for his share of the price. If the fetus had a free father, the compensation for the fetus belongs to his father in both cases, and the buyer gets nothing. From al-Tatimmah: Yusuf ibn Muhammad al-Bilali was asked about a man who committed fornication with someone else's slave-girl and made her pregnant; then he and his wife conspired to abort the pregnancy from the slave-girl, and the slave-girl died from that cause. What is the ruling and what is due from them? He said: As for the slave-girl, he must guarantee her if she died by that cause. For the pregnancy: the ghurrah if it was dead; if it came out alive then died, its value is due; if the pregnancy was water and blood, nothing is due. From al-Muntaqa: Abu Yusuf said: If a man struck the belly of his wife and she miscarried a dead fetus, there is no expiation on him and he does not inherit from it. If she miscarried a dead fetus whose creation had become distinct, then she died from that strike, then she miscarried a living fetus and it died: for the first, the ghurrah; for the mother, the diya; for the second fetus, the complete diya. From al-Nasafiyyah: He was asked about a divorced woman (mukhtali'ah) who was pregnant and passed her waiting period by aborting the child. Does the husband have a right to litigate her regarding this pregnancy? He said: If she aborted it by her action, she owes the husband a ghurrah of five hundred pure dirhams, and nothing of that is dropped due to her inheritance because she is a killer so she does not inherit. And he was asked al-Qasim about a woman who drank medicine and miscarried her dead fetus, or carried a heavy load and miscarried a dead fetus: that her 'aaqilah must pay five hundred dirhams in one year to the heir of the pregnancy, whether the father or someone else; if she has no 'aaqilah, then it is in her own wealth within a year. In al-Hawi: That is [due] to her husband because he is the heir; said by Yusuf ibn 'Isa. In Jami' al-Fatawa: If it is not known whether it is male or female, the certain [minimum] is taken, like in the case of a hermaphrodite [khuntha mushkil]. The fetus is lost and she cannot [give] a dirham of نقرة[؟]
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage collects several fatwas from later Hanafi sources (Nawadir, al-'Uyun, al-Tatimmah, al-Muntaqa, al-Nasafiyyah, al-Hawi, Jami' al-Fatawa) that apply the principles of diyat and ghurrah to various intricate scenarios. (1) Nawadir Ibn Sama'ah: A man declares one of his slave's twins free, then both are miscarried dead by a blow. The criminal owes a ghurrah (500 dirhams) plus additional amounts based on the value of each twin, accounting for one being free. (2) Al-'Uyun: A purchased slave-woman's fetus is emancipated before delivery, then struck and miscarried. The buyer has an option: keep the slave and claim the fetus's compensation from the striker, or rescind the sale and the fetus's share of the price is debited. If the fetus has a free father, the compensation goes to the father, not the buyer. (3) Al-Tatimmah: A fornicator and his wife conspire to abort the slave-girl's pregnancy, causing her death. The fornicator must guarantee the slave-girl's value. For the pregnancy: if dead, ghurrah; if born alive then dies, full value; if it was just water/blood, nothing. (4) Al-Muntaqa (Abu Yusuf): Striking one's wife causing miscarriage: no kaffarah (since no certain life?), and striker does not inherit. If fetus was formed then mother dies and second live fetus dies, separate compensations apply. (5) Al-Nasafiyyah: A divorced woman aborts her pregnancy by her own action, she must pay the husband a ghurrah of 500 dirhams, and she does not inherit from that because she is the killer. (6) Al-Qasim: A woman who intentionally aborts by medicine or heavy lifting must pay ghurrah to the heir (usually the father) via her 'aaqilah over one year; if no 'aaqilah, it's her personal liability. (7) Al-Hawi specifies the husband as the heir. (8) Jami' al-Fatawa: If the fetus's sex is unknown, the lower amount is taken (like a hermaphrodite case). The last part about 'lost fetus' is unclear.

Key Terms
غرة (ghurrah): Compensation for a dead fetus, fixed at 500 dirhams or 5 camels; also used for other fetal death compensations.
دية (diyah): Blood money for killing a free person; in these fatwas, full diyah is due when a live birth occurs and then the child dies.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for killing; Abu Yusuf rules no kaffarah for a stillborn fetus in the fatwa given.
عاقلة ('aaqilah): Paternal male relatives who pay diyah on behalf of a killer; in the fatwa, they pay the ghurrah for a woman's accidental abortion.
مختلعة (mukhtali'ah): A divorced woman who initiated khul' (divorce by redemption). In the fatwa, she aborts the pregnancy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa of Abu Yusuf in al-Muntaqa, what is required regarding expiation (kaffarah) when a man strikes his wife causing a dead miscarriage?
A) Expiation is required.
B) No expiation is required.
C) Expiation is required only if the fetus was fully formed.
D) Expiation is required only if the mother dies.

Key Takeaway
The ghurrah (500 dirhams) is the baseline for a dead fetus, but additional compensation may apply based on value, live birth, or free status, and the 'aaqilah may be liable for accidental miscarriages by women.

Fetal Diyat (Ghurrah) in Hanafi Case Rulings
Narrates multiple specific scenarios of fetal death and their rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ghurrah ruling for fetal death in different Hanafi scenarios and identify who is liable and who inherits.

Core Idea
A fetus's diyat (ghurrah) is fixed at 500 dirhams, but variations occur based on life signs, parent status, and cause of death.

The Hanafi fiqh literature records numerous case rulings (nawazil) on diyat for miscarried fetuses. This lesson surveys several such cases from authoritative Hanafi works, revealing the consistent rule of ghurrah and its exceptions. You will learn how the ruling changes when the mother is a killer, when the buyer has not taken possession, and when the gender is unknown.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and parties
For each scenario, list the parties involved (offender, mother, father, owner, etc.) and the nature of the injury.
2
Determine the state of the fetus
Was it dead at birth? Alive then died? Undetermined? Does it have evident creation?
3
Apply the ghurrah rule
State the basic compensation: 500 dirhams for a dead fetus; value of the child if born alive.
If gender unknown, the minimum (ghurrah) is taken.
4
Determine liability and inheritance
Who pays (aaqilah, self)? Who inherits? Note that a killer does not inherit.
5
Note the special conditions
E.g., free father vs slave, buyer's option, unknown gender.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي نوادر ابن سماعة : رجل قال لأمته الحبلى أحد الولدين اللذين في بطنك حر فضرب إنسان بطنها فألقت جنينين ميتين غلام وجارية قال: على الجاني غرة وذلك خمسمائة وعليه أيضاً في الغلام ربع عشر قيمته لو كان حياً، وعليه في الجارية نصف خمسمائة ونصف عشر قيمتها. وفي العيون هشام عن أبي يوسف في رجل اشترى أمة حاملاً فلم يقبضها حتى أعتق ما في بطنها ثم ضرب إنسان بطنها فألقت غلاماً ميتاً فالمشتري بالخيار إن شاء أخذ الأمة بجميع الثمن واتبع الجاني بأرش الجنين أرش طيباً، وإن شاء فسخ البيع في الأمة ولزمه الولد بحصته من الثمن. ولو كان للجنين أب حر كان أرش الجنين لوالده في الوجهين جميعاً ولا شيء للمشتري. وفي التتمة وسئل يوسف بن محمد البلالي عن رجل زنى بجارية الغير فأحبلها ثم احتال هو وامرأته فأسقطا الحمل من الجارية وماتت الجارية بذلك السبب ما الحكم في ذلك وما يجب عليهما؟ فقال: أما الجارية فإنه يجب عليه ضمانها إذا ماتت بذلك السبب، وفي الحمل الغرة إن كان ميتاً، وإن سقط وهو حي ثم مات فإنه يجب قيمته وإن كان الحمل ماء ودماً فإنه لا يجب فيه شيء. وفي المنتقى قال أبو يوسف : إذا ضرب الرجل بطن امرأته فألقت جنيناً ميتاً فلا كفارة عليه ولا يرث منه، وإن ألقت جنيناً ميتاً قد استبان من خلقه شيء ثم ماتت هي من تلك الضربة ثم ألقت جنيناً حياً ومات ففي الأول الغرة، وفي الأم الدية وفي الجنين الثاني الدية كاملة. وفي النسفية سئل عن مختلعة حامل مضت عدتها بإسقاط الولد هل للزوج أن يخاصمها في هذا الحمل ؟ فقال : إن أسقطته بفعلها وجب عليها للزوج غرة قيمتها خمسمائة . خالصة ولا يسقط شيء من ذلك لميراثها لأنها قاتلة فلا ترث. وسئل أبو القاسم عن امرأة شربت الدواء فألقت جنينها ميتاً أو حملت حملاً ثقيلاً فألقت جنيناً ميتاً أن على عاقلتها خمسمائة درهم في سنة واحدة لوارث الحمل أباً كان أو غيره، وإن لم يكن لها عاقلة فهي في مالها في سنة. وفي الحاوي : وذلك لزوجها لأنه هو الوارث ؛ قاله يوسف بن عيسى. وفي جامع الفتاوى : ولو لم يعلم أنه ذكر أو أنثى يؤخذ بالمتيقن كالخنثى المشكل ضاع الجنين ولا يمكنها درهم نقرة
And in Nawadir Ibn Sami'a: A man said to his pregnant slave-woman, 'One of the two children in your womb is free.' Then a person struck her belly, and she miscarried twins, a boy and a girl, both dead. He said: Upon the offender is a ghurrah, which is five hundred, and also upon him for the boy one-fourth of one-tenth of his value had he been alive, and upon him for the girl half of five hundred and half of one-tenth of her value. And in Al-Uyun: Hisham from Abu Yusuf regarding a man who bought a pregnant slave-woman, did not take possession until he freed what was in her womb, then a person struck her belly and she miscarried a dead boy. The buyer has the option: if he wishes, he may take the slave-woman for the full price and pursue the offender for the compensation of the fetus, compensation good; if he wishes, he may rescind the sale of the slave-woman, and the child becomes binding with its share of the price. And if the fetus had a free father, the compensation for the fetus goes to his father in both cases, and nothing to the buyer. And in Al-Tatmimah: Yusuf ibn Muhammad al-Bilali was asked about a man who committed zina with someone else's slave-girl and impregnated her, then he and his wife conspired and aborted the pregnancy from the slave-girl, and the slave-girl died from that cause. What is the ruling and what is obligatory upon them? He said: As for the slave-girl, he is liable for her (compensation) if she dies from that cause; and for the pregnancy, the ghurrah if it was dead; and if it came out alive then died, then its value is obligatory; and if the pregnancy was water and blood, then nothing is obligatory. And in Al-Muntaqa: Abu Yusuf said: If a man strikes his wife's belly and she miscarries a dead fetus, there is no expiation upon him, and he does not inherit from it. And if she miscarries a dead fetus whose creation was evident, then she dies from that blow, then she delivers a live fetus that dies, then for the first is the ghurrah, for the mother the diyah, and for the second fetus the full diyah. And in Al-Nasfiyyah: He was asked about a divorced woman (mukhtali'ah) who is pregnant and passed her iddah by aborting the child. Does the husband have the right to dispute with her regarding this pregnancy? He said: If she aborted it by her action, the ghurrah of five hundred dirhams is obligatory upon her for the husband, pure, and nothing of that falls due to her inheritance because she is a killer, so she does not inherit. And Abu al-Qasim was asked about a woman who drank medicine and aborted her fetus dead, or carried a heavy load and aborted a dead fetus: that upon her aqilah (tribal guarantors) is five hundred dirhams in one year for the heir of the fetus, father or other; and if she has no aqilah, then it is in her wealth over one year. And in Al-Hawi: That is for the husband because he is the heir; said by Yusuf ibn Isa. And in Jami' al-Fatawa: And if it is not known whether it is male or female, the certain amount is taken, like the ambiguous hermaphrodite; the fetus is lost and she cannot [pay] dirhams [؟].
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a collection of specific case rulings from various Hanafi sources (Nawadir, Al-Uyun, Al-Tatmimah, Al-Muntaqa, Al-Nasfiyyah, Al-Hawi, Jami' al-Fatawa) on diyat for a fetus. Each scenario involves unique circumstances: a slave with a partially free fetus, a purchased slave with a freed fetus, zina and abortion, a wife struck, a divorced woman aborting, etc. The common thread is the obligation of ghurrah (500 dirhams) or value depending on whether the fetus is born alive or dead, and who is liable. Notably, if the mother kills the fetus by her action, she does not inherit. If gender is unknown, the minimum amount (ghurrah) is taken.

Key Terms
غرة (ghurrah): Fixed compensation of 500 dirhams for a fetus miscarried due to injury.
عاقلة (aaqilah): The tribal or clan group responsible for paying diyat on behalf of a killer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario from Al-Nasfiyyah, why does the divorced woman not inherit anything from the ghurrah she must pay?
A) She is the killer
B) She is not an heir
C) The husband is the sole heir
D) The ghurrah is not inheritable

Key Takeaway
The core ruling is that a ghurrah (500 dirhams) is wajib for a deceased fetus; special conditions affect who pays and who inherits, but a killer never inherits.

Diyat — Blood Money

Fetal Death After Manumission: Value vs. Diyah
Ruling on diyat when a slave is freed after being struck, then fetus dies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school obligates the full value (qimah) rather than diyah for a fetal slave when the mother is freed after being struck, and state the intra-Hanafi variant views.

Core Idea
Liability attaches at the moment of the strike; the slave status at that time determines compensation, not the eventual manumission.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: what compensation is due when a pregnant slave is struck by a third party, then freed by her master, and subsequently miscarries a dead fetus? The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq rules that the full value (qimah) of the fetus as a living slave is owed, not the diyah of a free person. The commentator unpacks the reasoning, drawing analogies to shooting versus wounding and recording the differing positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the matn's ruling
The scenario: a pregnant slave is struck, then freed, then miscarries a dead fetus. The matn states: 'Then its value when alive is due' and 'the diyah is not obligatory.' Recognize that the obligation is based on the time of the strike when the fetus was a slave.
The ruling explicitly rejects diyah because the fetus was not free at the time of injury.
2
Understand the reasoning: why full value rather than decrease
The commentator argues by analogy to shooting an arrow: the act (striking the mother) is completed at the time of the strike, just as shooting is completed when the arrow is released. Manumission does not cut off progression because the injury to the fetus is not direct until separation. Therefore, full value is due, not just the decrease in value from strike to manumission (as would be the case for a direct wound).
The analogy to cutting off a hand is rejected because that is a direct injury; manumission cuts off progression in that case.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad has a divergent narration: he holds that only the difference in value between the struck and unstruck state is due, because he considers manumission as cutting off the progression of injury. Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa agree on full value. The mufta bihi (operative position) is the full value.
The dispute turns on whether the striking is analogized to shooting (full value) or wounding (decrease).
4
Consider the scenario of manumission before the strike
If the slave were freed before the strike, then according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, diyah is due (free person). According to Abu Hanifa, only the difference in value is due. This shows the importance of the timing of the strike.
The text qualifies: 'after striking him' indicates the ruling changes if manumission precedes the strike.
5
Determine who receives the compensation
The passage ends by noting a difference among later scholars: some say the compensation goes to the heirs of the fetus, others to the master. This is a further ikhtilaf not resolved in this text.
The preferred view in the Hanafi school is for the master, as the fetus was his property at the time of the strike.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لو أنثى فإن حرره سيده بعد ضربه فالقته فمات ففيه قيمته حياً ولا كفارة في الجنين تقويمه باعتبار قيمته وهيآته ووقع التنازع في قيمته القول للضارب لأنه المنكر كما لو قتل عبداً خطأ ووقع التنازع في قيمته وعجز القاضي عن تقويمه باعتبار حاله كان القول للضارب ؛ كذا في شرح الهداية للعيني. قال رحمه الله : (فإن حرره سیده بعد ضربه فالقته فمات ففيه قيمته (حياً ولا تجب الدية وإن كان بعد العتق لأن الوجوب بالضرب والضرب صادفه وهو رقيق فتجب قيمته حياً لأنه صار قاتلاً له وهو حي فاعتبرنا حالتي السبب والتلف فأوجبنا عليه القيمة باعتبار حالتي السبب وهو الضرب لأنه رقيق حينئذ، وأوجبنا عليه جميع قيمته باعتبار حالة التلف كأنه ضربه في الحال، وكان ينبغي أن يجب ما نقص بضربه إلى أن يوجد العتق كما لو قطع يد عبد أو جرحه فأعتقه المولى ثم مات يجب عليه أرش اليد والجرح وما نقص من قيمته إلى العتق لأن العتق يقطع السراية لكن اعتبر فيه الحالتان فجعل كأن الضرب لم يوجد في حق الجنين لأن المقصود بالضرب الأم فأوجبنا القيمة دون الدية لأنه صار قاتلاً له بالضرب الأول فصار كما لو رمي - عبداً فأعتقه المولى ثم وقع عليه السهم فمات فإنه تجب عليه القيمة للمولى لأن الرمي ليس بجناية ما لم يتصل بالمحل فلا يجب فيه شيء هذا بدون الاتصال بخلاف القطع والجرح لأنه جناية في الحال والعتق يقطع السراية ومع تجب القيمة دون الدية لأنه يصير قاتلاً له من وقت الرمي لأنه الفعل المملوك له. وقال فخر الإسلام قال بعض مشايخنا : معنى قوله ضمن أي الدية وقوله ولا تجب الدية ليس هو في الجامع الصغير ووجه أن الضرب وقع على الأم فلم يعتبر جناية في الجنين إلا بعد الانفصال حياً ولذلك لم تنقطع سرايته بخلاف من جرح فأعتقه مولاه. قال بعضهم: بل المراد به حقيقة القيمة لأن الجناية قد تمت منه لكن لا يعتبر في حق الجنين مقصوداً إلا بعد الانفصال فأشبه الرمي الذي تم من الرامي ولا يعتبر في حق المرمي إليه إلا بعد الإصابة. وقيل: هذا عندهما، وعند محمد تجب قيمته ما بين كونه مضروباً إلى كونه غير مضروب لأن القطع قاطع السراية. وقيد بقوله بعد ضربه لأنه لو حرره قبل الضرب فألقته حياً فالواجب الدية على قولهما، وعلى قول الإمام تجب قيمته ما بين كونه مضروباً إلى كونه غير مضروب، واختلف المشايخ لمن يكون هذا المقدار قال بعضهم : لورثة هذا الجنين. وقال بعضهم : للمولى؛ كذا في التتارخانية .
If female, then if her master freed her after striking her, and she miscarried and the fetus died, then its value when alive is due, and no expiation for the fetus. Its valuation is based on its value and condition. If there is a dispute over its value, the statement of the striker is accepted because he is the denier, just as if he killed a slave by mistake and there was a dispute over his value and the judge was unable to assess it based on his condition, the statement of the striker is accepted. Such is in Sharh al-Hidayah by al-Ayni. The author (rahimahullah) said: (For if her master freed her after striking her, and she miscarried and the fetus died, then its value when alive is due, and the diyah is not obligatory even if after manumission, because the obligation is by the striking, and the striking encountered it while it was a slave, so its value when alive is due because he became its killer while it was alive, so we considered both the time of cause and the time of destruction, and we obligated its full value based on the state of destruction as if he struck it at that moment. And it would have been necessary to obligate the decrease in its value from the strike until manumission, just as if he cut off the hand of a slave or wounded him, then the master freed him, then he died – he must pay the compensation for the hand and wound and the decrease in his value until manumission, because manumission cuts off the progression. But here both states are considered, making it as if the striking did not exist in regard to the fetus because the striking was directed at the mother, so we obligated the value, not the diyah, because he became its killer by the first strike. So it is like if he shot an arrow at a slave, then the master freed him, then the arrow struck and he died – then the value is due to the master because the shooting is not an injury until it reaches the target; nothing is due without contact. This is unlike cutting or wounding, which is an immediate injury, and manumission cuts off progression. Nonetheless, the value is due, not the diyah, because he becomes his killer from the time of the shooting, as the act is owned by him. And Fakhr al-Islam said: Some of our mashayikh said: The meaning of his statement 'he is liable' is the diyah, and his statement 'the diyah is not obligatory' is not in al-Jami' al-Saghir. The reason is that the striking occurred on the mother, so it is not considered an injury against the fetus until after live separation; therefore its progression is not cut off, unlike one who wounds and then the master frees him. Some said: Rather the intended meaning is the actual value because the injury has been completed by him, but it is not considered in relation to the fetus as intended until after separation; so it resembles the shooting which is completed by the archer but not considered in relation to the target until impact. And it is said: This is according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Muhammad, its value as the difference between being struck and not struck is due because cutting off progression. And it is qualified by his statement 'after striking him' because if he freed him before striking, and she miscarried alive, then the diyah is obligatory according to them; and according to the Imam, its value as the difference between being struck and not struck is due. And the mashayikh differed as to whom this amount goes: some said it is for the heirs of this fetus; some said it is for the master. Thus in al-Tatarkhaniyyah.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling when a pregnant slave is struck, then the owner frees her, and she miscarries a dead fetus. The matn states that the value of the fetus when alive is due, not the diyah, even if the slave was freed after the strike. The commentator explains: the obligation arises from the strike, which occurred when the fetus was still a slave, so the full value is due as if it were killed as a slave. However, if the mother had been freed before the strike, then diyah would apply. There is a difference among the Hanafi imams: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (and the preferred view), the value is due; according to Imam Muhammad in another narration, only the decrease in value from the strike to manumission is due (as with wounding). The discussion also notes that the ruling is analogous to shooting an arrow at a slave who is then freed before impact; in that case, full value is due because the act was complete at the time of shooting. The passage ends with a note that the scholars differ as to who receives the compensation: the fetus's heirs or the master.

Key Terms
قيمة (qimah): The market value of the fetus as a slave if it had been alive at the time of the strike.
دية (diyah): Blood money for a free person; not applicable here because the fetus was a slave at the time of the strike.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Full diyah of a free person
B) Full value as a slave at the time of death
C) Full value as a slave at the time of the strike
D) Only the decrease in value from the strike until manumission

Key Takeaway
Liability for a fetal slave's death is determined by its status at the moment of the strike, not at death, so full slave value (qimah) is due, even if the mother is later freed.

No Kaffarah for Killing a Fetus: Hanafi Refutation of Shafi'i
Hanafi rebuttal to Shafi'i on kaffarah for fetus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kaffarah for a fetus and explain the Hanafi rebuttal to the Shafi'i argument, including the inconsistency in the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Kaffarah is only for a complete soul; a fetus is a part of the mother, so no expiation.

This lesson examines a classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on whether causing a miscarriage requires kaffarah (expiation). The Hanafi school firmly holds that no kaffarah is due, while the Shafi'i school argues it is obligatory as a precaution. We will explore the Hanafi evidence—both textual and rational—and the contradiction the Hanafis identify in the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the opening lines: the Hanafi matn states 'there is no kaffarah for the fetus,' while Imam al-Shafi'i argues it is wajib.
This is an ikhtilaf between schools.
2
Understand the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi reasoning: kaffarah is only for a 'nafs mutlaqah' (complete independent soul). The fetus is not such a soul. Punishment (like kaffarah) cannot be extended by analogy (qiyas).
The key term is 'nafs mutlaqah'.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i argument
Al-Shafi'i argues that the fetus is a soul 'in some respects,' so kaffarah is wajib as a precaution (ihtiyat).
Shafi'i relies on the potential of the fetus.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response points out a contradiction: al-Shafi'i considers the fetus a part of the mother for diyah (obligating one-tenth), yet here he treats it as an independent soul for kaffarah. The Hanafis consistently consider it a part.
Consistency is key in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا كفارة في الجنين) وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : تجب الكفارة لأنه نفس من وجه فتجب احتياطاً لما فيها من العبادة ولنا أن الكفارة فيها معنى العقوبة لأنها شرعت زاجرة، وفيها معنى العبادة لأنها تتأدى بالصوم وقد عرف وجوبها في النفس المطلقة فلا تتعداها لأن العقوبة لا يجري فيها القياس، وقول الشافعي فيه تناقض لأنه يعتبره جزءاً حتى أوجب عليه عشر قيمة الأم وههنا اعتبره نفساً حتى أوجب فيه الكفارة، ونحن اعتبرناه جزءاً
The author (rahimahullah) said: (And there is no expiation for the fetus.) And al-Shafi'i (rahimahullah) said: Expiation is obligatory because it is a soul in some respects, so it is obligatory as a precaution due to the worship involved. Our evidence is that expiation contains the meaning of punishment because it was legislated as a deterrent, and it also contains the meaning of worship because it can be performed by fasting. It has been established that it is obligatory for an absolute soul, so it is not extended beyond that because punishment cannot be made by analogy. And the statement of al-Shafi'i is contradictory because he considers it a part (of the mother) to the extent that he obligated one-tenth of the mother's value, and here he considers it a soul to the extent that he obligated expiation. We consider it a part.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether kaffarah (expiation) is due for causing a miscarriage. The Hanafi matn states there is no kaffarah for a fetus. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since the fetus is a soul in some sense, expiation should be obligatory as a precaution because it involves an act of worship (freeing a slave or fasting). The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) Kaffarah has both punitive and worship aspects, but it is only legislated for a complete soul (nafs mutlaqah), and punishment cannot be extended by analogy (qiyas). (2) Al-Shafi'i is inconsistent: elsewhere he considers the fetus a part of the mother (so he obligates one-tenth of the mother's diyah), but here he considers it an independent soul to require expiation. The Hanafi position treats the fetus as a part, not an independent soul, so no kaffarah.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for killing a human being, usually freeing a slave or fasting two months.
نفس مطلقة (nafs mutlaqah): An absolute, independent soul – a fully developed human life.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is there no kaffarah for a fetus?
A) Because the killing was accidental
B) Because the fetus is not a complete soul
C) Because the mother's diyah suffices
D) Because kaffarah is only for intentional killing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require kaffarah for causing a miscarriage because the fetus is not a complete soul; only diyah in the form of ghurrah is owed.

Striking a Pregnant Slave Who Is Later Freed
Ruling on compensation for fetal death when slave is freed after the blow

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on compensation for fetal death when the mother is a slave later freed, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad regarding the amount.

Core Idea
When a pregnant slave is struck, then freed, then miscarries, full slave value is wajib because the blow occurred while she was a slave.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq on a complex case: a man strikes a pregnant slave woman, her master later frees her, and then she miscarries a dead fetus. The key question is whether emancipation affects the compensation. The Hanafi school holds that the obligation arises from the blow, not the death, so the fetus's value as a slave is wajib, not the full diyah of a free person. The passage also presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the full value or only the depreciation is due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is striking a pregnant slave who is later freed, causing fetal death. The ruling is that the striker must pay the value of the fetus as a live slave (qimah), not blood money (diyah).
The ruling applies even though the fetus dies after emancipation.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is that the blow occurred while the mother was a slave, so the obligation is based on slave status at the time of the cause. The text also uses an analogy to shooting a slave: the shooting is not a crime until it hits, so full value is due.
The analogy contrasts with cutting a slave's hand, where emancipation cuts off propagation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal reasoning)
The blow is the direct cause of the fetal death. Although emancipation occurs before death, it does not cut off propagation because the blow was aimed at the mother, not directly at the fetus. The injury to the fetus is considered to have been caused by the first blow entirely.
Key concept: sirāyah (propagation) is blocked by direct injuries like cuts, but not here.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (dispute)
Abu Hanifa holds that full value of the fetus as a slave is wajib. Muhammad holds that only the depreciation in value (difference between struck and unstruck) is wajib, because emancipation would cut off propagation if the injury were direct.
The text attributes the second view to Muhammad, but also says 'this is according to the two' (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preference)
The passage does not explicitly resolve the dispute. Later Hanafi works may adopt one view, but the text leaves it open. The student should understand both positions and the reasoning behind each.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is the amount of compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن حرره سيده بعد ضربه فالقته فمات ففيه قيمته حياً ولا كفارة في الجنين تقويمه باعتبار قيمته وهيآته ووقع التنازع في قيمته القول للضارب لأنه المنكر كما لو قتل عبداً خطأ ووقع التنازع في قيمته وعجز القاضي عن تقويمه باعتبار حاله كان القول للضارب ؛ كذا في شرح الهداية للعيني. قال رحمه الله : (فإن حرره سیده بعد ضربه فالقته فمات ففيه قيمته (حياً ولا تجب الدية وإن كان بعد العتق لأن الوجوب بالضرب والضرب صادفه وهو رقيق فتجب قيمته حياً لأنه صار قاتلاً له وهو حي فاعتبرنا حالتي السبب والتلف فأوجبنا عليه القيمة باعتبار حالتي السبب وهو الضرب لأنه رقيق حينئذ، وأوجبنا عليه جميع قيمته باعتبار حالة التلف كأنه ضربه في الحال، وكان ينبغي أن يجب ما نقص بضربه إلى أن يوجد العتق كما لو قطع يد عبد أو جرحه فأعتقه المولى ثم مات يجب عليه أرش اليد والجرح وما نقص من قيمته إلى العتق لأن العتق يقطع السراية لكن اعتبر فيه الحالتان فجعل كأن الضرب لم يوجد في حق الجنين لأن المقصود بالضرب الأم فأوجبنا القيمة دون الدية لأنه صار قاتلاً له بالضرب الأول فصار كما لو رمي - عبداً فأعتقه المولى ثم وقع عليه السهم فمات فإنه تجب عليه القيمة للمولى لأن الرمي ليس بجناية ما لم يتصل بالمحل فلا يجب فيه شيء هذا بدون الاتصال بخلاف القطع والجرح لأنه جناية في الحال والعتق يقطع السراية ومع تجب القيمة دون الدية لأنه يصير قاتلاً له من وقت الرمي لأنه الفعل المملوك له. وقال فخر الإسلام قال بعض مشايخنا : معنى قوله ضمن أي الدية وقوله ولا تجب الدية ليس هو في الجامع الصغير ووجه أن الضرب وقع على الأم فلم يعتبر جناية في الجنين إلا بعد الانفصال حياً ولذلك لم تنقطع سرايته بخلاف من جرح فأعتقه مولاه. قال بعضهم: بل المراد به حقيقة القيمة لأن الجناية قد تمت منه لكن لا يعتبر في حق الجنين مقصوداً إلا بعد الانفصال فأشبه الرمي الذي تم من الرامي ولا يعتبر في حق المرمي إليه إلا بعد الإصابة. وقيل: هذا عندهما، وعند محمد تجب قيمته ما بين كونه مضروباً إلى كونه غير مضروب لأن القطع قاطع السراية. وقيد بقوله بعد ضربه لأنه لو حرره قبل الضرب فألقته حياً فالواجب الدية على قولهما، وعلى قول الإمام تجب قيمته ما بين كونه مضروباً إلى كونه غير مضروب، واختلف المشايخ لمن يكون هذا المقدار قال بعضهم : لورثة هذا الجنين. وقال بعضهم : للمولى؛ كذا في التتارخانية .
If her master frees her after his blow and she miscarries and it dies, then it requires its value alive, and no expiation for the fetus. Its valuation is based on its value and condition. If dispute arises over its value, the statement of the striker is accepted because he is the denier, just as if he killed a slave accidentally and dispute arose over its value and the judge is unable to appraise it based on its condition, the statement of the striker is accepted; likewise in Sharh al-Hidayah al-'Ayni. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (If her master frees her after his blow and she miscarries and it dies, then it requires its value (alive) and the blood money is not obligatory even if it is after emancipation, because the obligation is due to the blow and the blow encountered her while she was a slave, so its value alive is obligatory because he became its killer while it was alive, so we considered the two states of cause and destruction and made obligatory upon him the value considering the state of the cause, which is the blow, because he was a slave at that time, and we made obligatory upon him its entire value considering the state of destruction as if he struck it at that moment. And it would have been necessary to make obligatory what decreased by his blow up to the time of emancipation, just as if he cut the hand of a slave or wounded him and then the master freed him and then he died, then the compensation for the hand and wound and what decreased from his value up to emancipation is obligatory because emancipation cuts off the propagation; but here the two states were considered so that it is as if the blow did not occur with respect to the fetus because the intended target of the blow was the mother, so we made the value obligatory instead of blood money because he became its killer by the first blow, so it is like if he shot a slave and the master freed him and then the arrow hit him and he died, then the value is obligatory to the master because the shooting is not a crime until it reaches the target, so nothing is obligatory without connection, unlike cutting and wounding because it is a crime immediately and emancipation cuts off propagation, yet the value is obligatory instead of blood money because he becomes his killer from the time of the shooting because it is an action he owned. And Fakhr al-Islam said: Some of our shaykhs said: The meaning of his statement 'he is liable' is the blood money, and his statement 'blood money is not obligatory' is not in al-Jami' al-Saghir; the reason is that the blow was on the mother, so it is not considered a crime against the fetus until after separation alive, and therefore its propagation is not cut off, unlike one who wounds and his master frees him. Some said: Rather what is meant is the real value because the crime was completed from him, but it is not considered with respect to the fetus as intended until after separation, so it resembles the shooting that was completed from the shooter but is not considered with respect to the target except after impact. And it is said: This is according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Muhammad its value is what is between its being struck and its being unstruck because the cut cuts off propagation. And it is conditioned by his saying 'after his blow' because if he freed her before the blow and she miscarried alive, then the wajib is blood money according to the two, and according to the Imam the value between being struck and unstruck is wajib. And the shaykhs differed over to whom this amount belongs: some said to the heirs of this fetus, and some said to the master; likewise in al-Tatarkhaniyyah.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is explaining a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The case: a man strikes a pregnant slave woman; later her master frees her; then she miscarries and the fetus dies. The ruling is that the striker must pay the value of the fetus as if it were a live slave (qimah), not the full diyah (blood money). The reasoning: the obligation arises from the blow, which occurred while the woman was a slave, so the compensation is based on slave value. Even though the fetus dies after the mother's freedom, we consider both the time of the cause (blow) and the time of death; the full value is paid because the fetus is considered to have died from the blow. The text contrasts this with a case where a slave's hand is cut and then he is freed and dies; there only the compensation for the hand is due, because emancipation cuts off the propagation of the injury. But here, since the blow was aimed at the mother, the injury to the fetus is not considered a direct crime until the fetus separates alive. Therefore, the striker is fully liable. There is a dispute: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that if the mother is freed before the blow, then full diyah is wajib. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that even then the value difference is due. The text also discusses to whom the compensation goes: some say to the fetus's heirs, others to the master. The relied-upon position is not explicitly stated, but the detailed reasoning indicates the Hanafi acceptance of qimah.

Key Terms
جنين (janīn): The fetus in the womb; in this passage, the fetus of a slave woman.
قيمة (qīmah): The monetary value of the fetus evaluated as a live slave.
دية (diyah): Blood money payable for taking a life; in this context, the full diyah of a free person.
عتق (itq): Emancipation of the slave; here it occurs after the blow but before the death of the fetus.
سراية (sirāyah): The propagation of injury from the initial wound to the eventual death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a pregnant slave is struck, then freed, and then miscarries a dead fetus, what is the compensation according to Abu Hanifa?
A) Full diyah of a free person
B) The value of the fetus as a live slave (qimah)
C) One-tenth of the mother's value (ghurrah)
D) No compensation because the blow was not directly on the fetus

Key Takeaway
Compensation for fetal death when the mother is a slave is based on the status at the time of the blow, not at the time of death.

No Expiation for Fetal Death
Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i on fetal kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on kaffarah for fetal death and refute the Shafi'i argument using the principle that punishments are not subject to qiyas.

Core Idea
Kaffarah applies only to a complete free soul; the fetus is a part, not a soul.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: should a person who causes a fetal death be required to perform kaffarah? The Hanafi school firmly says no, and here the commentator provides a detailed critique of the Shafi'i position, exposing an internal inconsistency. Understanding this ruling sharpens your grasp of how the Hanafi school restricts penal obligations to textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling from the matn: 'No kaffarah for the fetus.' This is the Hanafi position.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The opponent is Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that kaffarah is wajib because the fetus is a soul in some respects.
Al-Shafi'i uses caution (ihtiyat) due to the worship element.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i argues that the fetus resembles a soul, and since kaffarah involves worship (fasting), it should be required out of caution.
This is an analogical argument (qiyas).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: Kaffarah is primarily a punishment, and punishments are not extended by qiyas. Moreover, al-Shafi'i is inconsistent because he treats the fetus as a part for diyah (1/10th) but as a soul for kaffarah.
The Hanafi consistently treat the fetus as a part.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, a Hanafi judge does not require kaffarah, while a Shafi'i judge would require it along with ghurrah.
This difference affects the religious obligations placed on the offender.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا كفارة في الجنين) وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : تجب الكفارة لأنه نفس من وجه فتجب احتياطاً لما فيها من العبادة ولنا أن الكفارة فيها معنى العقوبة لأنها شرعت زاجرة، وفيها معنى العبادة لأنها تتأدى بالصوم وقد عرف وجوبها في النفس المطلقة فلا تتعداها لأن العقوبة لا يجري فيها القياس، وقول الشافعي فيه تناقض لأنه يعتبره جزءاً حتى أوجب عليه عشر قيمة الأم وههنا اعتبره نفساً حتى أوجب فيه الكفارة، ونحن اعتبرناه جزءاً من وجه ولهذا لم يجب فيه كل البدل فكذا لا تجب فيه الكفارة لأن الأعضاء لا كفارة فيها إلا إذا تبرع بها هو لأنه ارتكب محظوراً فإذا تقرب بها إلى الله تعالى كان أفضل ويستغفر الله تعالى مما صنع من الجريمة العظيمة. والجنين الذي استبان بعض خلقه في جميع ما ذكرنا من الأحكام كالتام لإطلاق ما روينا ولأنه ولد في حق الأحكام كأمومية الولد وانقضاء العدة به والنفاس وغير ذلك فكذا في حق هذا العلقة فلا ولأنه الحكم، يتميز من والدم بد منه .
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And no expiation for the fetus). And al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Expiation is obligatory because it is a soul in some respects, so it is obligatory out of caution because of the worship it contains. Our evidence: Expiation has the meaning of punishment because it was prescribed as a deterrent, and it has the meaning of worship because it can be performed by fasting, and its obligation has been established for the absolute soul, so it is not extended to others because punishment is not subject to analogy. And al-Shafi'i's statement is contradictory because he considers it a part such that he made obligatory one-tenth of the mother's value, yet here he considers it a soul such that he made expiation obligatory. And we consider it a part in some respects, and for this reason the full compensation is not wajib for it, so likewise expiation is not wajib for it because limbs do not require expiation unless he volunteers it because he committed a prohibited act; if he draws near to Allah by it, it is better, and he seeks forgiveness from Allah for the great crime he committed. And the fetus whose some of its limbs have become apparent is in all the rulings we mentioned like the complete fetus, due to the generality of what we have narrated, and because it is a child with respect to rulings like motherhood of the child, expiry of the waiting period with it, post-partum bleeding, and others; so likewise with respect to this clot? No, because the ruling is distinguished from the blood? ... (unclear).
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and al-Shafi'i regarding the obligation of kaffarah (expiation) for causing the death of a fetus. The Hanafi matn states, 'No kaffarah for the fetus.' The commentator explains that al-Shafi'i argued for kaffarah on the grounds that the fetus is a soul in some aspects, so out of caution (ihtiyat) it should be required. The Hanafi response is that kaffarah contains both elements of punishment and worship. As a punishment, it cannot be extended by qiyas (analogy) to cases beyond the clear texts (which limit kaffarah to the killing of a free soul). As an act of worship, it is prescribed only where explicitly stated. Moreover, al-Shafi'i is inconsistent: for compensation (diyah), he treats the fetus as a part of the mother (thus 1/10th of her value), but for kaffarah he treats it as a full soul. The Hanafi consistently treat the fetus as a part, so no kaffarah and no full diyah. The passage also clarifies that a fetus with discernible limbs (istabāna ba‘ḍu khalqih) is treated as a complete fetus for all these rulings, based on the general evidence that such a fetus is considered a child for legal purposes like establishing motherhood, completing the waiting period, and postnatal bleeding. The final sentence is somewhat corrupt but affirms that the same rules apply to the non-distinct embryo (al-‘alaqah?) as well? Actually it distinguishes between the fetus with limbs and the clot (nutfah/‘alaqah) which is not yet formed. The intended meaning is that once limbs are formed, it is a full fetus; before that, it may be considered mere blood (dam) or a clot.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffārah): Expiation; a combination of punishment and worship (freeing a slave, fasting, etc.) for certain sins, including accidental killing of a believer.
نفس (nafs): Soul; a living human being with full legal capacity.
جزء (juz'): Part; the fetus is considered a part of the mother for diyat and kaffarah purposes.
استبان بعض خلقه (istabāna ba‘ḍu khalqihī): The fetus shows some of its limbs (i.e., has taken human form).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school not require kaffarah for causing the death of a fetus?
A) Because kaffarah is only for intentional killing
B) Because the fetus is considered a part of the mother, not a complete soul
C) Because the fetus is not a Muslim yet
D) Because kaffarah must be performed by the mother, not the striker

Key Takeaway
Kaffarah for fetal death is not required in Hanafi fiqh because the fetus is not a complete soul, and penal obligations are confined to textual stipulations.

Woman Inducing Abortion: Liability, Permission, and Exceptions
Expanded ruling on induced abortion with multiple scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman who induces abortion, identify the conditions that trigger ghurrah vs kaffarah, and apply the rules to scenarios involving permission, slave status, fetus viability, and medical necessity.

Core Idea
A woman who aborts without permission is a transgressor; her 'aqlah pay ghurrah, she inherits nothing – kaffarah only if the fetus was born alive.

Classical Hanafi texts present a detailed landscape of liability when a woman intentionally induces abortion. Beyond the basic ghurrah, the ruling shifts with permission, the mother's slave status, the fetus's viability, and even the mother's intent. This lesson unpacks these layers from the passage of Al-Bahr al-Raiq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Find the core principle: if she takes medicine or treats herself without husband's permission and miscarries, her 'aqlah must pay a ghurrah, and she does not inherit from it because she killed the fetus.
The key term is 'ta'addī' (transgression) – without permission, she is a transgressor.
2
Distinguish the umm walad case
If the woman is a slave concubine (umm walad) and she aborts, no ghurrah is due because a slave cannot owe a debt to her master. But if the child was conceived in a situation where the master was deceived (maghrur), the child is free and ghurrah is wajib.
3
Differentiate live vs dead fetus
If the fetus is born alive then dies, the 'aqlah pay ghurrah, and kaffarah is also wajib on her. If expelled dead, only ghurrah is wajib (with a dispute on kaffarah).
Kaffarah is an additional expiation – fasting or feeding the poor.
4
Examine the role of intent
If she drank a medicine for a purpose other than abortion, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, only ghurrah is due, no kaffarah. Some later scholars (in al-Hawi) said kaffarah is also wajib.
Intent affects the obligation of kaffarah, but ghurrah remains.
5
Apply the medical exception
If a pregnant woman has a medical condition (e.g., overwhelming blood) that threatens her, she may take necessary treatment after consulting medical experts. Cupping and phlebotomy are allowed with caution, especially after the child moves.
This shows the balance between preserving the mother's life and protecting the fetus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (وإن شربت دواء لتطرحه أو عالجت فرجها حتى أسقطته ضمن عاقلتها الغرة إن فعلت بلا إذن لأنها ألقته متعدية فيجب عليها ضمانه وتتحمل عنها العاقلة لما بينا، ولا ترث هي من الغرة شيئاً لأنها قاتلته بغير حق والقاتل لا يرث بخلاف ما إذا فعلت ذلك بإذن الزوج حيث لا تجب الغرة لعدم التعدي. ولو فعلت أم الولد ذلك بنفسها حتى أسقطت فلا شيء عليها لاستحالة وجوب الدين على المملوك لسيده، ولو استحقت وجب للمولى غرة أنه ليس بمالك لهما وأنه مغرور وولد المغرور حر الأصل وهي متعدية بذلك الفعل لأنه تبين فصارت قاتلة للجنين فتجب الغرة ،له ويقال للمستحق إن شئت سلم الجارية وإن شئت أفدها لأنه الحكم في جناية المملوك. وفي جامع الفتاوى وفي نوادر رستم : امرأة شربت دواء لتسقط ولدها عمداً فألقت جنيناً حياً ثم مات فعلى العاقلة ولا ترث منه شيئاً وعليها الكفارة، وإن ألقت جنيناً ميتاً فعلى عاقلتها غرة ولا ترث منه شيئاً وعليها الكفارة، وقال أبو بكر في هذه الصورة: إنها إذا اسقطت سقطاً ليس عليها إلا التوبة والاستغفار، وإن كان جنيناً فعليها غرة، وتأويله إذا شربت دواء يوجب سقوط الولد وتعمدت ذلك. وفي المنتقى رواية مجهولة : امرأة شربت دواء فأسقطت وكانت شربت لغير ذلك يعني لغير إسقاط الولد فعليها الغرة ولا كفارة عليها في قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد ولا ترثه وقال بعضهم: عليها الكفارة، وهذا الجواب من زيادات الحاوي وفي المنتقى سئل أبو بكر عن حامل أرادت أن تلقي العلقة لغلبة الدم قال : يسأل أهل الطب عن ذلك إن قالوا يضر بالحمل لا تفعل، إن قالوا لا يضر تفعل، وكذا الحجامة والفصد قال الفقيه وسمعت ممن يعرف ذلك الأمر قال : لا ينبغي لها أن تفعل ما لم يتحرك الولد فإذا تحرك فلا بأس بالحجامة ما لم تقرب الولادة، فإذا قربت فلا يفعل. وأما الفصد فالامتناع في حال الحبل أفضل لأنه يخاف على الولد إلا أن مختلعة يدخل الأم ضرر بين في تركه. وفي فتاوى النسفي سئل عن وهي حامل لإسقاط العدة بإسقاط الولد قال : إن سقط بفعلها وجب عليها الغرة ويكون ذلك للزوج . وفي الحاوي : وهي لا ترث منه لأنها قاتلة قال : الأب إذا ضرب ابنه الصغير تأديباً فعطب ذلك ينظر إن ضربه حيث لا يضرب للتأديب فعليه الدية والكفارة عند أبي حنيفة. وقال من أبو يوسف ومحمد لا شيء عليه. وفي نوارد بشر عن أبي يوسف أن عليه كفارة، وعلى هذا احتالت
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And if she drinks medicine to cause miscarriage or treats her private parts until she miscarries, her 'aqlah are liable for the ghurrah if she does so without permission, because she expelled it transgressingly, so she is liable for its guarantee, and the 'aqlah bear it for her as we mentioned, and she does not inherit anything from the ghurrah because she killed it without right and the killer does not inherit, unlike if she did that with the husband's permission where the ghurrah is not wajib due to lack of transgression. And if an umm walad does that herself until she miscarries, then nothing is upon her because it is impossible for a debt to be wajib upon a slave to her master; but if she deserves, the ghurrah is wajib to the master because he is not the owner of both and he is deceived, and the child of a deceived person is originally free, and she is transgressing by that act because it becomes clear that she became the killer of the fetus, so the ghurrah is wajib to him, and it is said to the claimant: if you wish, hand over the slave woman, or if you wish, ransom her, because it is the ruling for the crime of a slave. And in Jami' al-Fatawa and in Nawadir Rustam: A woman deliberately drank medicine to abort her child and expelled a live fetus that then died; then the 'aqlah are liable, she does not inherit from it, and upon her is kaffarah. And if she expelled a dead fetus, then upon her 'aqlah is a ghurrah, she does not inherit from it, and upon her is kaffarah. Abu Bakr said in this case: If she aborted a stillborn (sīqāt) then upon her is only repentance and seeking forgiveness; if it was a formed fetus (janīn) then upon her is ghurrah. Its interpretation is if she drank a medicine that causes abortion and she intended it. And in al-Muntaqa, an unknown narration: A woman drank medicine and aborted, and she drank for other than abortion, meaning not to abort, so upon her is ghurrah and no kaffarah according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and she does not inherit it, and some said: upon her is kaffarah, and this answer is from the additions of al-Hawi. And in al-Muntaqa, Abu Bakr was asked about a pregnant woman who wanted to abort the clot due to overwhelming blood; he said: Ask the medical experts about that; if they say it harms the pregnancy, she should not do it; if they say it does not harm, she may do it. Likewise cupping and phlebotomy. Al-Faqih said: I heard from someone who knows that matter: She should not do it as long as the child has not moved; when it moves, then there is no harm in cupping as long as birth is not near; when birth approaches, she should not do it. As for phlebotomy, abstaining during pregnancy is better because it is feared for the child, unless she is a concubine (?) and there is clear harm to the mother in leaving it. And in Fatawa al-Nasafi, he was asked about a pregnant woman for the purpose of ending the waiting period by aborting the child; he said: If it aborts by her action, ghurrah is wajib upon her, and it is for the husband. And in al-Hawi: She does not inherit from it because she is a killer. He said: If the father strikes his young son as discipline and he dies as a result, then look: if he struck him where one should not strike for discipline, then upon him is blood money (diyah) and kaffarah according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Nothing upon him. And in Nawadir Bashr from Abu Yusuf that upon him is kaffarah, and upon this they devised? ... (text cut off).
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on a woman who intentionally induces abortion by means of drugs or physical treatment. The core ruling: if she does so without her husband's permission, she is a transgressor (mut'addiyah), and her 'aqlah (agnatic group responsible for paying blood money) must pay a ghurrah (a fine of one-tenth of the mother's value, typically 5 camels or equivalent) for the fetus. She does not inherit from this ghurrah because she is the killer. If the husband permitted, no ghurrah is due because no transgression. The passage then discusses special cases: if the woman is an umm walad (a slave concubine who has borne her master a child), then no ghurrah is payable because a slave cannot owe a debt to her master; but if the child was conceived in a situation where the master was deceived (maghrur), then the child is free-born and the ghurrah is wajib to the master. There is also a discussion of the distinction between aborting a live fetus (requiring kaffarah as well) vs. a dead fetus (only ghurrah). The passage includes various fatwas: from Abu Bakr al-Razi saying that for a stillborn (sīqāt) only repentance is needed; from al-Muntaqa, a narration that if the woman drank medicine for a purpose other than abortion, no kaffarah but still ghurrah; from Fatawa al-Nasafi, that if a woman aborts to end her waiting period, the ghurrah is for the husband. Finally, the passage touches on a father disciplining his son and causing death: according to Abu Hanifa, if he strikes where not allowed, diyah and kaffarah are due; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, nothing. The passage ends abruptly.

Key Terms
غرة (ghurrah): A fine for causing miscarriage, equal to one-tenth of the mother's value (or 5 camels). It is the compensation for the fetus.
عاقلة (‘āqilah): The agnatic relatives (tribe or clan) of the perpetrator who are collectively responsible for paying blood money (diyah/ghurrah) in cases of accidental or quasi-intentional killing.
تعدي (ta‘addī): Transgression; acting without right or permission. Here, the woman's act is mut'addiyah if done without husband's permission.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master, thereby gaining special status: she cannot be sold and becomes free upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman drinks medicine to abort without her husband's permission and miscarries a dead fetus, what is the ruling on kaffarah according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?
A) Kaffarah is wajib
B) No kaffarah is wajib, only ghurrah
C) Kaffarah is not wajib but ghurrah is not either
D) Both kaffarah and ghurrah are wajib

Key Takeaway
A woman who induces abortion without permission is a transgressor; her 'aqlah must pay ghurrah, she does not inherit, and kaffarah is due only if the fetus was born alive (disputed).

Rulings on a Woman Aborting Her Fetus and the Ghurrah Liability
Ruling and intra-Hanafi differences on woman aborting fetus and blood money

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghurrah for abortion and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad versus Abu Yusuf regarding kaffarah.

Core Idea
A woman who aborts without permission owes ghurrah via her 'aqilah, but the killer does not inherit; kaffarah is disputed.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the liability of a woman who intentionally aborts her fetus. The author explains that the ghurrah (blood money for a fetus) is wajib upon her 'aqilah if she acted without her husband's permission. She does not inherit from the ghurrah because she caused the death. Additionally, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether kaffarah (expiation) is also required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a woman taking medicine or treating herself to abort. The ruling: ghurrah is wajib on her 'aqilah if she acted without permission.
If she had permission, no liability.
2
Determine the condition for liability
She must have acted without the husband's permission; with permission, no ghurrah because there is no transgression.
3
Note the inheritance rule
The woman does not inherit from the ghurrah because she is the killer, and a killer does not inherit from the victim.
This is a settled rule in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that no kaffarah is required if she took medicine for another purpose; Abu Yusuf requires kaffarah. Some narrations from Abu Yusuf also require kaffarah.
The text cites fatwa collections showing variation.
5
Understand the basis of the dispute
The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argues that the fetus is not a fully independent person with limbs, so analogy to killing does not apply for kaffarah.
Kaffarah is like a penalty on limbs, which does not apply to abortion.

Source Text

كتاب الديات وإن شربت دواء لتطرحه أو عالجت فرجها حتى أسقطته ضمن عاقلتها الغرة إن فعلت من وجه ولهذا لم يجب فيه كل البدل فكذا لا تجب فيه الكفارة لأن الأعضاء لا كفارة فيها إلا إذا تبرع بها هو لأنه ارتكب محظوراً فإذا تقرب بها إلى الله تعالى كان أفضل ويستغفر الله تعالى مما صنع من الجريمة العظيمة. والجنين الذي استبان بعض خلقه في جميع ما ذكرنا من الأحكام كالتام لإطلاق ما روينا ولأنه ولد في حق الأحكام كأمومية الولد وانقضاء العدة به والنفاس وغير ذلك فكذا في حق هذا العلقة فلا ولأنه الحكم، يتميز من والدم بد منه. قال رحمه الله: (وإن شربت دواء لتطرحه أو عالجت فرجها حتى أسقطته ضمن عاقلتها الغرة إن فعلت بلا إذن لأنها ألقته متعدية فيجب عليها ضمانه وتتحمل عنها العاقلة لما بينا، ولا ترث هي من الغرة شيئاً لأنها قاتلته بغير حق والقاتل لا يرث بخلاف ما إذا فعلت ذلك بإذن الزوج حيث لا تجب الغرة لعدم التعدي. تبين فصارت قاتلة للجنين فتجب الغرة، له ويقال للمستحق إن شئت سلم الجارية وإن شئت أفدها لأنه الحكم في جناية المملوك. وفي جامع الفتاوى وفي نوادر رستم : امرأة شربت دواء لتسقط ولدها عمداً فألقت جنيناً حياً والاستغفار، وإن كان جنيناً فعليها غرة، وتأويله إذا شربت دواء يوجب سقوط الولد وتعمدت ذلك. وفي المنتقى رواية مجهولة : امرأة شربت دواء فأسقطت وكانت شربت لغير ذلك يعني لغير إسقاط الولد فعليها الغرة ولا كفارة عليها في قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد ولا ترثه وقال بعضهم: عليها الكفارة، وهذا الجواب من زيادات الحاوي وفي المنتقى سئل أبو بكر عن حامل أرادت أن تلقي العلقة لغلبة الدم قال : يسأل أهل الطب عن ذلك إن قالوا يضر بالحمل لا تفعل، إن قالوا لا يضر تفعل، وكذا الحجامة والفصد قال الفقيه وسمعت ممن يعرف ذلك الأمر قال : لا ينبغي لها أن تفعل ما لم يتحرك الولد فإذا تحرك فلا بأس بالحجامة ما لم تقرب الولادة، فإذا قربت فلا يفعل. وأما الفصد فالامتناع في حال الحبل أفضل لأنه يخاف على الولد إلا أن مختلعة يدخل الأم ضرر بين في تركه. وفي فتاوى النسفي سئل عن وهي حامل لإسقاط العدة بإسقاط الولد قال : إن سقط بفعلها وجب عليها الغرة ويكون ذلك للزوج . وفي الحاوي : وهي لا ترث منه لأنها قاتلة قال : الأب إذا ضرب ابنه الصغير تأديباً فعطب ذلك ينظر إن ضربه حيث لا يضرب للتأديب فعليه الدية والكفارة عند أبي حنيفة. وقال من أبو يوسف ومحمد لا شيء عليه. وفي نوارد بشر عن أبي يوسف أن عليه كفارة، وعلى هذا احتالت
The Book of Diyat. If she drank medicine to abort or treated her vagina until she miscarried, her 'aqilah is liable for a ghurrah if she did it without permission because she caused it wrongfully, so she must guarantee it and her 'aqilah bear it as we mentioned, and she does not inherit anything from the ghurrah because she killed him without right and the killer does not inherit, contrary to if she did it with the husband's permission where the ghurrah is not obligatory due to lack of transgression. If a slave mother (umm walad) did that herself and miscarried, nothing is upon her due to impossibility of obligation of debt upon a slave for her master, and if she becomes entitled, the ghurrah is obligatory for the master...
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the ruling on a woman who intentionally aborts her fetus. The author begins by stating the general ruling: if a woman takes medicine or treats herself to cause abortion, she is liable for the ghurrah (blood money for a fetus) which is paid by her 'aqilah (tribal guarantors) if she acted without the husband's permission. She does not inherit from this ghurrah because she is the killer. The text then clarifies that if she acted with the husband's permission, no ghurrah is due because there is no transgression. For a slave woman (umm walad), no liability arises because a slave cannot owe a debt to her master; but if she becomes free, the master is entitled to the ghurrah. The passage then quotes various fatwa collections presenting different views: in some, kaffarah (expiation) is also required; in others, only ghurrah. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say no kaffarah if she drank for another purpose, while some scholars say kaffarah is needed. The text also discusses a case where a pregnant woman wants to abort due to blood pressure; she should consult doctors. The author concludes by quoting Al-Hawi about a father disciplining his son, which transitions to the next lesson.

Key Terms
الغرة (al-ghurrah): Blood money for a fetus, set at one-tenth of full diyah (500 dirhams or equivalent).
العاقلة (al-‘āqilah): The group of male relatives (tribal guarantors) who are liable to pay blood money on behalf of a killer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The woman herself
B) The husband
C) The 'aqilah (tribal guarantors)
D) No one, because it is permissible

Key Takeaway
The ghurrah is due from the 'aqilah, and the woman does not inherit; kaffarah is disputed but the stronger view is no kaffarah.

Liability of Teacher and Guardian for Disciplinary Beating: The Kaffarah Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kaffarah for teacher's disciplinary beating

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability of a teacher or guardian who beats a child in the usual place for discipline, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding kaffarah.

Core Idea
A teacher or guardian is not liable for diyah if beating in the usual place, but kaffarah is required according to the relied-upon view.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author expands on the ruling of liability when a teacher or guardian beats a child for discipline. The core issue is whether the death resulting from permissible discipline triggers any financial or expiatory obligation. The Hanafi school generally exempts from diyah, but differs on kaffarah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling on daman
The author first states the consensus that the teacher, father, and guardian are not liable (la yadman) if the beating is in the usual place. This is the position of all three imams.
Usual place means areas like hands or feet where disciplinary beating is customary.
2
Isolate the dispute on kaffarah
After stating the no-liability ruling, the author introduces a dispute: according to the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), kaffarah is required. But there is a weak narration saying no kaffarah. The fatwa is on the view requiring kaffarah.
Kaffarah here means expiation for killing, such as freeing a slave or fasting two months.
3
Trace the reason for the dispute
The underlying talil (reasoning) is that although the beating is permissible, it results in death, which is a prohibited outcome. Hence, expiation is needed. The opposing view considers the act fully permissible with permission and standard method, thus no sin.
This is a classic debate between considering the permissibility of the act versus the prohibited result.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The text explicitly states 'والفتوى على الأول' meaning the fatwa is on the view that kaffarah is required.
This is the operative ruling for practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ضمان عليه وعليه الكفارة في قولهما. وهذا إذا كان ضربه المعلم في موضع معتاد وفي رواية مجهولة لا كفارة عليهما والفتوى على الأول. والزوج إذا ضرب زوجته حيث تضرب للتأديب مثل ما تضرب حال نشوزها يضمن بالإجماع، والأب إذا سلما الصغير إلى معلم يعلمه القرآن أو علماً آخر فضربه المعلم للتعليم فلا ضمان على المعلم ولا على الأب والوصي. وفي المنتقى عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف أن عليه الكفارة وإن ضربه حيث لا يضرب أو فوق ضرب التعليم فالمعلم ضامن. قال هشام في نوادره قلت لمحمد : إن لم يكن الأب قال له في أمر الضرب شيئاً قال : يضمن المعلم. وفي رواية في بعض النسخ أن ضرب الصغير إنما يضمن على قول أبي حنيفة إذا كان للتأديب، أما إذا ضربه لتعليم القرآن لا يضمن كالمعلم فإذا لا فرق بين ضرب المعلم بإذن الأب وبين ضرب الأب إذا كان للتعليم . وذكر شمس الأئمة الحلواني في شرح كتاب الإجارات أن في ضرب الأب ابنه وفي ضرب الزوج زوجته روايتين عن محمد في رواية يضمن، وفي رواية لا يضمن. أما الوالدة إذا ضربت ولدها الصغير للتأديب فلا شك أنها تضمن على قول أبي حنيفة، وقد اختلف المشايخ فيه على قولهما قال بعضهم لا تضمن، وقال بعضهم هي لأن الضرب تصرف في النفس وليس لها ولاية التصرف في النفس أصلاً. وفي كتاب العلل للزوج أن يضرب امرأته على ترك الصلاة وللأب أن يضرب ابنه على ترك الصلاة، وذكر مسألة المعلم إذا ضرب الصغير بإذن الأب على الاتفاق قال نحو ما ذكرنا قال محمد ثمة وهذا عندنا . وفي الكبرى : وفي العيون : إذا قال لرجلين اضربا مملوكي هذا مائة سوط فليس لأحدهما أن يضربه المائة كلها، فإن ضربه أحدهما تسعة وتسعين وضربه الآخر سوطاً واحداً ففي القياس يضمن ضارب الأكثر، وفي رواية لا يضمن وهو نظير ما لو قال لامرأتيه إن أكلتما هذا الخبر فأنتما طالقتان فأكلتاه، وإن أكلت إحداهما عامته والأخرى بقيته لا تطلق استحساناً. المحترف إذا ضرب التلميذ فمات إن كان ضربه بأمر أبيه أو وصيه لا يضمن إذا كان في الموضع المعتاد لو ضرب امرأته على المضجع أو في أدب فماتت يضمن إجماعاً وعليه الكفارة؛ هما فرقا بينها وبين الأب فإن ضرب الأب لمنفعة الابن وضرب المرأة لمنفعة الزوج. وفي السراجية: رجل ضرب رجلاً سياطاً فجرحه فبرأ منه فعليه أرش الضرب إن بقي أثر الضرب، وإن لم يبق لا يجب عليه شيء سوى التغزير وقال أبو يوسف: تجب حكومة عدل. وقال محمد أجرة الطبيب وثمن الأدوية. وفي الجامع الصغير: الخامسة وهذا إذا جرح ابتداء، فأما إذا لم يجرح في الابتداء لا يجب بالاتفاق. وفي المنتقى : رجل قتل عمداً وله
The Book of Diyat. And the guardian (wasi) if he beats the minor child for discipline. In Al-Kubra: If the teacher beat him in the usual place and he died, neither the teacher, nor the father, nor the guardian are liable in all their opinions. Similarly, the tutor who teaches writing if he beats with the father's permission, no liability, but kaffarah is upon them according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). This if the teacher beat in the usual place, and in a unknown narration no kaffarah upon them, and the fatwa is on the first. The husband if he beats his wife where beating for discipline is like when she is nashizah (rebellious), he is liable by consensus. The father if he hands over the child to a teacher to teach Quran or other knowledge, and the teacher beats for education, there is no liability on the teacher, father, or guardian. In Al-Muntaqa from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that kaffarah is upon him, and if he beats where he should not beat or beyond beating for education, the teacher is liable. Hisham said in his Nawadir: I said to Muhammad: If the father did not say anything to him about beating, he said: the teacher is liable. In some copies: beating the child is only liable according to Abu Hanifa if it is for discipline, but if for teaching Quran, no liability like the teacher, so there is no difference between the teacher beating with the father's permission and the father beating for education...
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This second passage continues the Book of Diyat with a detailed discussion on liability for beating in disciplinary contexts. The author presents various scenarios and the differing opinions within the Hanafi school. The first scenario is the guardian (wasi) beating a child for discipline; the ruling is that if the teacher beats in the usual place and the child dies, there is no liability (daman) on the teacher, father, or guardian according to all (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). However, there is a dispute about kaffarah: in one narration, kaffarah is required; in another, it is not. The fatwa is on the view that kaffarah is required. For a husband beating his wife for discipline (nushuz), he is liable by consensus. For a teacher beating with the father's permission for education, no liability. The passage then records a transmission from Hisham that if the father gave no instructions, the teacher is liable. There is also a discussion about the mother beating her child: according to Abu Hanifa, she is definitely liable because she has no authority over the child's person. The scholars differ on the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): some say she is not liable, others say she is. Then the text moves to a case of a master ordering two people to beat his slave: if one beats most of the stripes and the other the remainder, the one who beat more is liable in qiyas, but in istihsan he is not liable. Finally, the passage discusses the case of a professional (teacher) beating a student and the slave beating, and ends with a ruling from Al-Sirajiyyah about a man whipping another: if the wound heals, he must pay the arsh (compensation for injury) if any trace remains, otherwise only ta'zir; Abu Yusuf says he must pay a just compensation, and Muhammad says the cost of doctor and medicine.

Key Terms
الوصي (al-waṣī): The guardian appointed by the father or judge to take care of a minor's affairs.
التأديب (al-ta’dīb): Disciplinary beating for the purpose of teaching or correcting behavior.
الكفارة (al-kaffārah): Expiation for killing, required when death results from a permissible act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in this passage, what is required of a teacher who beats a child in the usual place for discipline and the child dies?
A) Diyah only
B) Kaffarah only
C) Both diyah and kaffarah
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
A teacher or guardian is not liable for diyah when beating for discipline in the usual place, but the mufta bihi view requires kaffarah if death results.
